PART 1: GST SYSTEM OVERVIEW

---
[CHUNK_001]
[TOPIC: GST Overview — What It Is and How It Works]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: Section 9 CGST Act | Section 5 IGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | IGST_Act | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Goods and Services Tax (GST) is a comprehensive, multi-stage, destination-based indirect tax levied on every value addition in India. It replaced multiple central and state levies such as VAT, Service Tax, Excise Duty, CST, and others.

GST has four components:
- CGST (Central GST): Levied by the Central Government on intra-state supplies.
- SGST (State GST): Levied by the State Government on intra-state supplies.
- IGST (Integrated GST): Levied by the Centre on inter-state supplies and imports.
- UTGST (Union Territory GST): Levied on intra-UT supplies in Union Territories without legislature.

Tax rates: 0%, 5%, 12%, 18%, 28%. Special rates apply to composition taxpayers. Cess is levied on luxury and sin goods over and above the 28% rate.

Registration threshold (as of 2024-25):
- Goods suppliers: Rs. 40 lakh aggregate turnover (Rs. 20 lakh for special category states).
- Service providers: Rs. 20 lakh aggregate turnover (Rs. 10 lakh for special category states).
- Certain categories (e-commerce sellers, interstate suppliers) must register regardless of turnover.

---
[CHUNK_002]
[TOPIC: GST Return Ecosystem — Complete Picture of All Returns]
[GST_FORM: Multiple]
[SECTION: Section 37 | Section 39 | Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Every registered taxpayer must file returns periodically. The return ecosystem works as a chain:

GSTR-1 (Supplier files outward supplies) → auto-populates GSTR-2B of recipient → GSTR-3B (both supplier and recipient file summary return + pay tax) → GSTR-9 (annual reconciliation).

Full list of GST returns:
- GSTR-1: Monthly/Quarterly outward supplies (normal taxpayers)
- GSTR-1A: Amendment to GSTR-1 filed by supplier
- GSTR-2A: Dynamic auto-drafted inward supplies statement (read-only, not filed)
- GSTR-2B: Static auto-drafted ITC statement (read-only, not filed)
- GSTR-3B: Monthly/Quarterly summary return + tax payment
- GSTR-4: Annual return for Composition taxpayers
- GSTR-4A: Auto-drafted inward supply details for composition taxpayers
- CMP-08: Quarterly self-assessed tax challan for composition taxpayers
- GSTR-5: Monthly return for Non-Resident Foreign Taxpayers
- GSTR-5A: Monthly return for OIDAR service providers
- GSTR-6: Monthly return for Input Service Distributors (ISD)
- GSTR-7: Monthly TDS return for TDS deductors under GST
- GSTR-8: Monthly TCS statement for e-commerce operators
- GSTR-9: Annual return for regular taxpayers
- GSTR-9A: Annual return for Composition taxpayers
- GSTR-9C: Reconciliation statement for taxpayers with turnover > Rs. 5 crore
- GSTR-10: Final return on cancellation of registration
- GSTR-11: Inward supply statement for UIN holders (embassies, UN bodies etc.)

---
[CHUNK_003]
[TOPIC: GST Return Due Dates — Master Calendar]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B | GSTR-7 | GSTR-8 | GSTR-9 | CMP-08]
[SECTION: Section 37 | Section 39 | Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 59 | Rule 61 | Rule 80 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Quarterly | Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Monthly / Quarterly filing due dates:

GSTR-1 (Monthly filers): 11th of next month
GSTR-1 (Quarterly filers / QRMP): 13th of month following quarter end
IFF (Invoice Furnishing Facility, QRMP): 13th of M1 and M2 of quarter
GSTR-3B (Monthly filers): 20th of next month
GSTR-3B (Quarterly, QRMP — states Cat-1): 22nd of month following quarter
GSTR-3B (Quarterly, QRMP — states Cat-2): 24th of month following quarter
PMT-06 / QRMP monthly payment: 25th of next month
GSTR-7 (TDS return): 10th of next month
GSTR-8 (TCS, e-commerce operators): 10th of next month
GSTR-5 (Non-resident foreign taxpayers): 13th of next month (or 7 days after registration expiry)
GSTR-5A (OIDAR): 20th of next month
GSTR-6 (ISD): 13th of next month

Annual return due dates:
GSTR-9 (Regular taxpayers): 31st December following FY end
GSTR-9A (Composition taxpayers): 31st December following FY end
GSTR-9C (Reconciliation statement): 31st December following FY end
GSTR-4 (Composition, annual): 30th June following FY end
GSTR-10 (Final return after cancellation): within 3 months from date of cancellation order or effective date, whichever is later

PART 2: FORM GSTR-1 — DEEP DIVE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_004]
[TOPIC: GSTR-1 — Complete Structure of Tables]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1]
[SECTION: Section 37 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 59 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Schema]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Quarterly]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/GSTR_1.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GSTR-1 has the following key tables:

Table 4: B2B Supplies — Invoice-wise details of taxable supplies to registered persons. Includes invoice number, date, GSTIN of recipient, place of supply, taxable value, and tax amounts (IGST/CGST/SGST/Cess).

Table 5: B2C Large — Invoice-wise inter-state supplies to unregistered persons where invoice value exceeds Rs. 2.5 lakh (originally Rs. 2.5L; amended threshold — check current notifications).

Table 6A/6B: Exports / SEZ supplies — Details of zero-rated supplies (exports) and supplies to SEZ units/developers with or without payment of IGST.

Table 6C: Deemed exports — Supplies to EOU/STPI/EHTP/BTP units deemed as exports.

Table 7A/7B: B2C Small — Consolidated state-wise summary of taxable supplies to unregistered persons (intra-state and small inter-state < threshold).

Table 8: Nil-rated, exempt, and non-GST outward supplies — Summary by nature of supply.

Table 9A/9B/9C: Amendments — Corrections to invoices, credit notes, and debit notes of previous periods.

Table 10: Advance received and adjustments — Consolidated details of advances received for future supply of services, and their adjustments once invoices are issued.

Table 11: Amendment to advance entries.

Table 12: HSN-wise summary of outward supplies. From May 2025 onwards, separate for B2B and B2C.

Table 13: Documents issued during the tax period (invoices, credit notes, debit notes, advance receipts, delivery challans).

Table 14/14A: Supplies made through e-commerce operators where ECO pays tax under Section 9(5).

Table 15/15A: Supplies to SEZ units/developers through ECO where ECO pays tax under Section 9(5).

---
[CHUNK_005]
[TOPIC: GSTR-1 — Step-by-Step Filing Process]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1]
[SECTION: Section 37 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 59 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Quarterly]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/GSTR_1.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Steps to file GSTR-1 on GST Portal:

1. Login at www.gst.gov.in with valid GSTIN credentials.
2. Navigate to Services → Returns → Returns Dashboard.
3. Select financial year and tax period. The GSTR-1 tile will appear.
4. Click "Prepare Online" or use Offline Tool / ASP-GSP route.
5. Add invoice details in respective tables (B2B, B2C, Exports, CDNs, Advances, HSN summary).
6. Click GENERATE GSTR-1 SUMMARY to view consolidated summary. This can be generated every 10 minutes.
7. Review the summary — check for validation errors.
8. Submit using either:
   - DSC (Digital Signature Certificate — mandatory for Companies and LLPs)
   - EVC (Electronic Verification Code — OTP to registered mobile)
9. On successful filing:
   - ARN (Application Reference Number) is generated.
   - SMS and email confirmation sent to Primary Authorised Signatory.
   - GSTR-2B of all recipients is updated based on filed GSTR-1.

Important rules:
- Cannot file GSTR-1 before the end of the current tax period (exceptions: casual taxpayers after business closure, taxpayers who have applied for cancellation).
- Cannot have duplicate invoice numbers for the same GSTIN in the same financial year.
- All values must be reported up to 2 decimal places.
- Cannot amend invoices of previous financial year after 30th November of the following FY.

---
[CHUNK_006]
[TOPIC: GSTR-1A — Amendment Return]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1A | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 37 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 59 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Quarterly]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/GSTR_1.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2024-01-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Error_resolution]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GSTR-1A is an amended statement of outward supplies. It was introduced to allow suppliers to make corrections after recipients have taken action on invoices via the Invoice Management System (IMS).

Key features:
- Supplier can amend B2B invoices that were accepted, pending, or rejected by the recipient in IMS.
- GSTR-1A for a period can be filed after GSTR-1 for that period is filed.
- Due date: Same as GSTR-3B of that period (i.e., before GSTR-3B is filed).
- Once GSTR-3B is filed for a period, GSTR-1A for the same period cannot be filed.
- Values from GSTR-1A are used to update the auto-populated GSTR-3B of the supplier.

---
[CHUNK_007]
[TOPIC: GSTR-1 — IFF (Invoice Furnishing Facility) for QRMP Taxpayers]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1]
[SECTION: Section 37 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 59 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/GSTR_1.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2021-01-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

IFF (Invoice Furnishing Facility): An optional facility available to QRMP taxpayers to upload B2B invoice details for the first two months of each quarter (M1 and M2).

Purpose: Allows the recipient to see the invoice in their GSTR-2B without waiting for the quarterly GSTR-1. This helps recipients claim ITC on time.

Key rules:
- IFF filing is optional, not mandatory.
- Only B2B invoices, credit notes, and debit notes (for registered recipients) can be reported via IFF.
- Monthly IFF limit: Rs. 50 lakh per month (beyond this, invoices must wait for the quarterly GSTR-1).
- Due date: 13th of M1 and M2 of each quarter.
- IFF, once filed, cannot be revised.
- Details uploaded in IFF do not need to be re-uploaded in the quarterly GSTR-1 — they are auto-populated.

---

PART 3: FORM GSTR-3B — DEEP DIVE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_008]
[TOPIC: GSTR-3B — Detailed Table-by-Table Guide]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 61 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Schema]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Quarterly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Create_and_Submit_GSTR3B.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Table 3.1 — Tax on outward and reverse charge inward supplies:
- 3.1(a): Outward taxable supplies (other than zero-rated, nil-rated, and exempted) — auto-populated from GSTR-1/1A.
- 3.1(b): Outward taxable supplies (zero-rated) — exports and SEZ — auto-populated from GSTR-1/1A.
- 3.1(c): Other outward supplies (nil-rated, exempted) — auto-populated from GSTR-1/1A.
- 3.1(d): Inward supplies liable to reverse charge — auto-populated from GSTR-2B.
- 3.1(e): Non-GST outward supplies — auto-populated from GSTR-1/1A.

Table 3.1.1 — Supplies notified under Section 9(5) (ECO pays tax):
- 3.1.1(i): Taxable supplies where ECO (e-commerce operator) pays tax under Section 9(5) — filed by ECO.
- 3.1.1(ii): Taxable supplies made by registered supplier through ECO where ECO pays tax — filed by supplier (only taxable value, no tax).
- Negative values allowed from September 2024 tax period onwards.

Table 3.2 — Inter-state supplies breakdown:
Breakup of inter-state supplies made to unregistered persons, composition taxable persons, and UIN holders, state-wise.

Table 4 — Eligible ITC:
- 4A(1): ITC on imports of goods.
- 4A(2): ITC on inward supplies from ISD.
- 4A(3): ITC on RCM supplies.
- 4A(4): ITC from ISD distributions.
- 4A(5): ITC on all other inward supplies from registered persons.
- 4B: ITC reversed under Rule 42/43 and other reversals.
- 4C: Net ITC available (4A minus 4B).
- 4D(1): ITC reclaimed after reversal.
- 4D(2): Ineligible ITC under Section 16(4) and POS rules — auto-populated from GSTR-2B.

Table 5 — Exempt, nil-rated, and non-GST inward supplies (summary).

Table 5.1 — Interest and late fee for previous tax period.

Table 6 — Payment of tax: Shows IGST, CGST, SGST, Cess liability; ITC offset; and cash payment.

---
[CHUNK_009]
[TOPIC: GSTR-3B — Sequential Filing Rule and Locking Mechanism]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B | GSTR-1]
[SECTION: Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 61 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Quarterly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Create_and_Submit_GSTR3B.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2024-08-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Error_resolution]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Sequential filing rule for GSTR-3B (from CBIC):
- GSTR-1 must be filed before GSTR-3B can be filed for the same period.
- GSTR-3B must be filed in chronological order — a taxpayer cannot file GSTR-3B for October 2024 without first filing GSTR-3B for September 2024.
- This applies to all periods from August 2024 onwards.

RCM/ITC Reversal Locking:
- If entries in the RCM Liability/ITC Statement are not posted for a previous return period, the taxpayer will not be allowed to file GSTR-3B for the next period.
- The SAVE button will be disabled and an error message will be shown at the dashboard.

Warning messages in GSTR-3B:
- If ITC claimed in Table 4A(2) and 4A(3) is more than the liability paid in 3.1(d) plus RCM liability/ITC statement closing balance — warning appears.
- A RED highlight appears on cells where edited values deviate from system-computed values, with the direction of the deviation also checked (downward for 3.1a/b/c/d/e, 4B; upward for 4A).

---
[CHUNK_010]
[TOPIC: GSTR-3B — Payment of Tax and Offsetting Liability]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B | PMT-06]
[SECTION: Section 49 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 86 | Rule 87 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Payment | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Quarterly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/payments/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Tax payment steps in GSTR-3B:
1. After filling all tables, click PREVIEW DRAFT GSTR-3B to review consolidated liability.
2. Navigate to Table 6 — Payment of Tax.
3. Offset liability using ITC available in the Electronic Credit Ledger:
   - IGST ITC can offset IGST, then CGST, then SGST.
   - CGST ITC can offset CGST only (cannot offset SGST).
   - SGST ITC can offset SGST only (cannot offset CGST).
4. Any remaining liability after ITC offset must be paid in cash via Electronic Cash Ledger.
5. If cash is insufficient, generate a PMT-06 challan, make payment, then proceed.
6. After offsetting and payment, click PROCEED TO FILE.
7. File using DSC (mandatory for Companies/LLPs) or EVC.

Payment modes via PMT-06: Net banking, UPI, credit/debit card, NEFT/RTGS, over-the-counter (OTC) up to limits.

---

PART 4: FORM GSTR-2A AND GSTR-2B — COMPLETE GUIDE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_011]
[TOPIC: GSTR-2A vs GSTR-2B — Key Differences]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-2A | GSTR-2B]
[SECTION: Section 38 | Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 60 | Rule 36(4) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Manual_gstr2b.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2020-09-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reconciliation | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-2A:
- Dynamic, continuously updated as suppliers file/amend GSTR-1 or GSTR-5.
- Reflects TDS credits when GSTR-7 is filed and TCS credits when GSTR-8 is filed.
- Also reflects auto-populated import of goods from ICEGATE (Indian Customs).
- Read-only view only — no filing or action required.
- Useful for tracking all inward supplies across any date range.
- Parts: Part A (supplier GSTR-1 based), Part B (GSTR-5 of non-resident suppliers), Part C (ISD distributions from GSTR-6, TDS from GSTR-7, TCS from GSTR-8), Part D (Imports from ICEGATE).

GSTR-2B:
- Static, generated once per month on a specific cut-off date.
- Shows ITC available and ITC not available — fixed for that statement period.
- Used as the basis for ITC claims in GSTR-3B.
- Generated based on: GSTR-1/1A/IFF filed by suppliers, GSTR-5 by non-resident suppliers, GSTR-6 by ISD.
- Cut-off: Typically generated on 14th of the month for the previous month. Quarterly GSTR-2B also available for QRMP taxpayers.
- From October 2024 onwards: Includes ITC Rejected tab (invoices rejected via IMS).
- ITC Reversal section: Rule 37A reversals for supplier non-filing visible here.

Key rule: Under Rule 36(4), ITC can be claimed only up to 100% of eligible ITC appearing in GSTR-2B. Provisional ITC beyond GSTR-2B is not permitted from FY 2022-23 onwards.

---
[CHUNK_012]
[TOPIC: IMS — Invoice Management System (from October 2024)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-2B | GSTR-1A | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 38 | Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 60 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Manual_gstr2b.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2024-10-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

The Invoice Management System (IMS) was introduced from October 2024. It allows recipients to take action on inward supplies uploaded by their suppliers.

How IMS works:
- Supplier files GSTR-1 → invoices appear in recipient's IMS dashboard.
- Recipient can Accept, Reject, or mark as Pending each invoice.
- Accepted invoices → eligible ITC flows to GSTR-2B and GSTR-3B.
- Rejected invoices → marked as "ITC Rejected" in GSTR-2B; also pushed back to supplier's GSTR-1A for amendment.
- Pending invoices → treated as deemed accepted for ITC purposes by the system.

Impact on GSTR-2B:
- From October 2024, GSTR-2B has a new "ITC Rejected" tab showing invoices rejected via IMS.
- ITC Rejected invoices will NOT auto-populate in GSTR-3B Table 4.

Impact on supplier:
- If recipient rejects an invoice, the supplier receives it back and can amend via GSTR-1A before filing GSTR-3B.

---

================================================================================
PART 5: COMPOSITION SCHEME — CMP-08 AND GSTR-4
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_013]
[TOPIC: Composition Scheme — Eligibility and Key Restrictions]
[GST_FORM: CMP-02 | CMP-04]
[SECTION: Section 10 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 3 | Rule 5 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Composition]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/registration/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Eligibility for Composition Scheme:
- Manufacturers and traders: Aggregate turnover in preceding FY up to Rs. 1.5 crore (Rs. 75 lakh for North-Eastern states and hill states).
- Service providers (special composition): Aggregate turnover up to Rs. 50 lakh.
- Mixed suppliers (goods + services, where services ≤ 10% of turnover or Rs. 5 lakh, whichever is higher).

Key restrictions for composition taxpayers:
1. Cannot claim Input Tax Credit (ITC) on purchases.
2. Cannot collect GST from customers (tax is borne by the business).
3. Must write "Composition Taxable Person, not eligible to collect tax on supplies" on bills of supply.
4. Cannot make inter-state outward supplies.
5. Cannot supply non-taxable goods (e.g., alcohol for human consumption, petroleum products).
6. Cannot supply goods through an e-commerce operator (with some exceptions for restaurant services).

Tax rates for composition:
- Manufacturers: 1% (0.5% CGST + 0.5% SGST) of turnover.
- Traders: 1% (0.5% CGST + 0.5% SGST) of turnover of taxable supplies.
- Restaurants (not serving alcohol): 5% (2.5% CGST + 2.5% SGST) of turnover.
- Service providers (special scheme): 6% (3% CGST + 3% SGST) of turnover.

Opt-in: File CMP-02 before 31st March of preceding FY. New registrants can opt in at the time of registration.
Opt-out: Mandatory if turnover exceeds the limit. Must file CMP-04 to opt out.

---
[CHUNK_014]
[TOPIC: Form CMP-08 — Quarterly Tax Payment for Composition Taxpayers]
[GST_FORM: CMP-08]
[SECTION: Section 10 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 62 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Composition]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Payment | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Quarterly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2019-04-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form CMP-08 (Statement-cum-Challan for Self-Assessed Tax):
- Applicable from 1st April 2019.
- Replaces the earlier quarterly GSTR-4 that was filed as a return.
- Filed quarterly by all composition scheme taxpayers.

Due dates for CMP-08:
- Q1 (April–June): 18th July
- Q2 (July–September): 18th October
- Q3 (October–December): 18th January
- Q4 (January–March): 18th April

What CMP-08 contains:
- Self-declared tax liability on outward supplies (calculated on turnover at applicable composition rate).
- Inward supplies on which reverse charge applies.
- Interest payable for late payment.
- Tax is paid based on self-assessment (not on invoice-by-invoice basis).

GSTR-4A: Auto-drafted inward supply details for composition taxpayers from supplier GSTR-1/GSTR-5 filings. Read-only reference form. Helps in reconciling inward supplies. Not required to be filed.

Filing process: Login → Services → Returns → Returns Dashboard → Select Quarter → CMP-08 tile → Prepare Online → Enter turnover details and tax liability → Pay using Electronic Cash Ledger → File.

---
[CHUNK_015]
[TOPIC: Form GSTR-4 — Annual Return for Composition Taxpayers]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-4]
[SECTION: Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 62 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Composition]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2019-04-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GSTR-4 is the annual return for composition taxpayers. It covers the entire financial year in a single filing.

Applicability: All taxpayers who were under the composition scheme at any point during the financial year.

Due date: 30th June following the end of the financial year (changed from 30th April for FY 2024-25 onwards).

What GSTR-4 contains:
- Table 4: Summary of inward supplies (from registered suppliers, reverse charge supplies, from unregistered suppliers).
- Table 5: Summary of outward supplies and total turnover for the year.
- Table 6: Details of tax paid in each quarter's CMP-08.
- Reconciliation of CMP-08 payments with actual tax liability.

Important distinction:
- CMP-08: Quarterly payment challan — filed 4 times a year for tax payment.
- GSTR-4: Annual return — filed once a year summarising all CMP-08 payments.
- GSTR-4 cannot be revised once filed. Verify all figures before submission.

Aggregate turnover: GSTR-4 asks for aggregate turnover of the previous FY (for all businesses under same PAN, across India). This figure determines continued eligibility for the composition scheme.

---

================================================================================
PART 6: FORM GSTR-7 — TDS UNDER GST
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_016]
[TOPIC: GSTR-7 — TDS Deduction under GST (Section 51)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-7]
[SECTION: Section 51 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 66 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: TDS_Deductor]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/GSTR7_Manual.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 51 of CGST Act: Certain specified persons must deduct TDS at 2% (1% CGST + 1% SGST/UTGST, or 2% IGST) on payments made to suppliers for supply of taxable goods/services where the contract value exceeds Rs. 2.5 lakh.

Who must deduct TDS under GST:
- Department or establishment of Central or State Government.
- Local authority.
- Governmental agencies.
- Persons or category of persons notified by government (PSUs, societies registered under Societies Act).
- Authority or Board or any other body set up by Parliament or State Legislature, with 51% or more government equity/control.

Who is NOT subject to TDS deduction:
- Composition taxpayers.
- Supplies subject to reverse charge.
- Personal consumption supplies.
- Supplies between specified Government entities.

TDS amount: 2% of the payment made to supplier (on taxable value, not gross invoice value including GST). If IGST: 2% IGST; if CGST/SGST: 1% each.

Registration: TDS deductors must register separately on the GST portal as TDS deductors. They get a separate GSTIN.

---
[CHUNK_017]
[TOPIC: GSTR-7 — Filing Process and Rules]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-7 | GSTR-7A]
[SECTION: Section 51 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 66 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: TDS_Deductor]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/GSTR7_Manual.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GSTR-7: Monthly return filed by TDS deductors. Due date: 10th of next month.

What GSTR-7 contains:
- Table 3: Details of TDS deducted (supplier GSTIN, contract value, payment, TDS amount).
- Table 4: Amendments to TDS details from previous periods.
- Tables 5 & 6: Payment of TDS amount and interest.

TDS Certificate (GSTR-7A): Auto-generated certificate of TDS deducted, available to supplier on the portal.

Sequential filing of GSTR-7:
- From October 2024 onwards, GSTR-7 must be filed sequentially.
- Cannot file GSTR-7 for a period without filing all past due periods.
- Exception: If there are no saved records in GSTR-7 for periods prior to October 2024, the system will not force sequential filing for those old periods.

Nil GSTR-7:
- Can be filed only if no TDS was deducted (no records in Table 3) AND no rejected records from previous period are visible in Table 4.
- From October 2024: No late fee is computed for delayed filing of Nil GSTR-7.

Effect on supplier: TDS deducted by the deductor appears in the supplier's TDS/TCS Credit Received form, where the supplier can accept or reject it.

Action by supplier on TDS/TCS Credit:
- Supplier must accept/reject all records in the TDS/TCS Credit Received form.
- Accepted TDS gets credited to Electronic Cash Ledger of supplier.
- Rejected records go back to the deductor's GSTR-7 Table 4 (amendments) for correction.

---

================================================================================
PART 7: FORM GSTR-8 — TCS BY E-COMMERCE OPERATORS
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_018]
[TOPIC: GSTR-8 — TCS Collection by E-Commerce Operators (Section 52)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-8]
[SECTION: Section 52 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 67 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: TCS_Collector]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Manual_GSTR-8.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-10-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 52 of CGST Act: Every e-commerce operator (ECO) must collect Tax at Source (TCS) at the rate notified by the government on the net value of taxable supplies made through its platform by registered suppliers.

TCS rate:
- Prior to July 2024: 1% (0.5% CGST + 0.5% SGST/UTGST, or 1% IGST).
- From July 2024 onwards: Reduced to 0.5% (0.25% CGST + 0.25% SGST, or 0.5% IGST).

"Net value of taxable supplies" = Aggregate value of supplies of goods/services made through ECO less the aggregate value of supplies returned to suppliers.

E-commerce operators registered under GST must:
- Collect TCS from supplier at the time of payment.
- File GSTR-8 by 10th of the next month.
- Issue TCS certificates to suppliers.

When GSTR-8 filing is NOT mandatory:
- If no TCS was collected in that period AND no transactions are auto-populated in Table 4 due to rejection by supplier.

---
[CHUNK_019]
[TOPIC: GSTR-8 — Table Structure and Filing Rules]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-8]
[SECTION: Section 52 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 67 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: TCS_Collector]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Schema]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Manual_GSTR-8.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-10-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-8 Table structure:
- Table 3: Details of supplies attracting TCS — supplier GSTIN, gross value of supplies, returns made, net value, TCS amount. From April 2025, Place of Supply (POS) must be selected for each record.
- Table 4: Amendments to TCS details of previous periods.
  - Uploaded by ECO tab: Amendments to transactions uploaded by ECO in previous period.
  - Rejected by supplier tab: Records auto-populated here after supplier rejects in TDS/TCS Credit form.
- Table 5: Interest on late payment of TCS (auto-calculated).

Amendment rules:
- Table 4 amendments can be made multiple times (limit removed from a prior advisory).
- However, once TCS details have been accepted by the supplier, no amendment is allowed.
- If not yet accepted: Can be amended once; goes back to supplier.
- If originally rejected by supplier: Goes to rejected tab → ECO can amend → returns to supplier.

TCS liability calculation on amendment:
- First amendment: TCS liability = Last amended value minus original value.
- Second amendment: TCS liability = Last amended value minus previous amended value.

Validation rule (from July 2024): Total TCS (IGST + CGST + SGST) must be between 0.5% and 1% of the net taxable value (allows up to 0.01% decimal tolerance).

---

================================================================================
PART 8: FORM GSTR-6 — INPUT SERVICE DISTRIBUTOR
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_020]
[TOPIC: GSTR-6 — ISD Return (Input Service Distributor)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-6]
[SECTION: Section 20 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 39 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: ISD]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Input Service Distributor (ISD): A registered person who receives invoices for input services on behalf of distinct persons (branches/units with different GSTINs under same PAN) and distributes the ITC to those units.

GSTR-6: Monthly return filed by ISD by 13th of next month.

What GSTR-6 contains:
- Table 3: Inward supplies received — details of all invoices received by ISD.
- Table 4: Eligible ITC to be distributed.
- Tables 5, 8: Distribution of ITC to branches (ISD Invoices and ISD Credit Notes).
- Table 9: Redistribution of ITC if corrected in a subsequent period.

ITC distribution rules:
- IGST ITC received at ISD: Distributed as IGST to all eligible recipients.
- CGST ITC: Distributed as CGST to units in the same state; as IGST to units in other states.
- SGST ITC: Distributed as SGST to units in the same state; as IGST to units in other states.
- Distribution is pro-rata based on turnover of the recipient unit to total turnover of all recipient units.

ISD cannot distribute ITC on services exclusively for one unit to other units. Exclusive ITC must be given only to the relevant unit.

Effect on recipient: ISD distribution credit appears in GSTR-2B of recipient units under the "ISD Credits" section.

---

================================================================================
PART 9: INPUT TAX CREDIT — COMPLETE RULES
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_021]
[TOPIC: ITC — Section 16 Eligibility Conditions (All Four)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 16 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 36 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP | Exporter]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 16(2) of CGST Act — All four conditions MUST be satisfied to claim ITC:

Condition 1: Tax invoice or debit note must be in possession of the registered person. The document must contain all prescribed particulars.

Condition 2: Goods/services must have been received by the registered person. If goods are received in instalments, ITC is available only upon receipt of the last lot/instalment.

Condition 3: The tax charged on the supply must have actually been paid to the government by the supplier, either in cash or through utilisation of ITC.

Condition 4: The registered person must have filed their GST return (GSTR-3B).

Additional rule — 180-day payment rule:
If the recipient has not paid the supplier (consideration + GST) within 180 days from the invoice date, the ITC already claimed must be reversed with interest at 18% p.a. The ITC can be re-claimed in the period when payment is subsequently made.

Time limit for claiming ITC — Section 16(4) (as amended):
ITC for an invoice of FY 2024-25 must be claimed by 30th November 2025 (i.e., the November GSTR-3B) or before filing GSTR-9 for FY 2024-25, whichever is earlier.

---
[CHUNK_022]
[TOPIC: ITC — Section 17(5) Blocked Credits — Complete List]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 17(5) CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

ITC is NOT available (blocked) on the following under Section 17(5):

(a) Motor vehicles for transportation of persons having approved seating capacity ≤ 13 persons (including driver). Exceptions: When used for further supply of vehicles, transportation of passengers, imparting training on driving.

(b) Vessels and aircraft — same exceptions apply.

(c) Services of general insurance, servicing, repair and maintenance of the above motor vehicles, vessels, and aircraft (if ITC on the vehicle itself is blocked).

(d) Food and beverages, outdoor catering, beauty treatment, health services, cosmetic and plastic surgery, leasing/renting/hiring of motor vehicles (with approved seating ≤13). Exception: If the inward supply is used for making an outward taxable supply of the same category.

(e) Life insurance and health insurance — Exception: If obligatory by employer under any statute.

(f) Travel benefits for employees on vacation (leave travel concession).

(g) Works contract services for construction of an immovable property (other than plant and machinery). Exception: Where input service is used for further supply of works contract services.

(h) Goods/services received for construction of immovable property (other than plant and machinery) on own account.

(i) Goods/services on which tax has been paid under composition scheme.

(j) Goods/services received by non-resident taxable person (except on goods imported by them).

(k) Goods/services used for personal consumption.

(l) Goods lost, stolen, destroyed, written off, or gifted/free samples.

---
[CHUNK_023]
[TOPIC: ITC — Reversal Triggers and Rules]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 16 | Section 17 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 37 | Rule 37A | Rule 38 | Rule 42 | Rule 43 | Rule 44 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Penalty]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

ITC must be reversed in the following situations:

Rule 37 (Non-payment to supplier within 180 days):
Reverse ITC + pay interest at 18% p.a. from date of claim. Re-claim when payment is made.

Rule 37A (Supplier non-filing of GSTR-3B):
If a supplier fails to file GSTR-3B by 30th September of the following financial year, recipient must reverse ITC on that supplier's invoices. Auto-calculated in GSTR-2B ITC Reversal tab. Re-claim is possible when supplier subsequently files.

Rule 38 (Banking/financial companies):
50% of ITC is reversed every month by banking and financial institutions as they supply both exempt and taxable services.

Rule 42 (Common inputs used for exempt and taxable supplies):
ITC must be apportioned and partially reversed based on the ratio of exempt turnover to total turnover. Annual reconciliation required.

Rule 43 (Common capital goods used for exempt and taxable supplies):
Similar to Rule 42 but for capital goods. ITC on capital goods is spread over 5 years (60 months) and 1/60th is reversed monthly for the exempt use portion.

Rule 44 (Cancellation/opting out of composition scheme):
On cancellation of registration or opting out of composition scheme, all ITC on stocks, capital goods (reduced by 5% per quarter from date of invoice), and semi-finished goods must be reversed.

Section 17(5) blocked credits: Must be reversed in the period they were incorrectly claimed, with interest at 24% if detected by authorities.

---
[CHUNK_024]
[TOPIC: ITC — Section 16(5) and 16(6) Retrospective Relief]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B | DRC-03]
[SECTION: Section 16(5) | Section 16(6) | Section 128A CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 164 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC | Notice]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cbic-website/hindi/pdf/central-tax-circulars/Circular-238-32-2024-GST.pdf]
[VALID_FROM: 2024-08-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 16(5) — Retrospective relief for delayed ITC under Section 16(4):
Applicable to invoices pertaining to FY 2017-18 to FY 2021-22 where ITC was denied only because it was claimed after the cut-off date under Section 16(4).
Under Section 128A proceedings (for FY 2017-18 to 2019-20), if the demand notice was solely on account of denial under Section 16(4), and the taxpayer has now paid the principal tax, the ITC denial may be set aside retrospectively.

Section 16(6): Provides that ITC for a period during which registration was cancelled but later restored is also eligible — a taxpayer does not lose ITC merely because registration was cancelled and subsequently restored.

Key CBIC clarification (Circular 238/32/2024-GST): The tax officer scrutinising Section 128A applications must verify that the ITC denial was solely on account of Section 16(4), and not on any other ground, before allowing the deduction from the demanded amount.

---
[CHUNK_025]
[TOPIC: ITC — Documents Required to Claim ITC]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 16(2) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 36 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Documents eligible for ITC claim:

1. Tax invoice issued by a registered supplier.
2. Invoice issued by Input Service Distributor (ISD) for distributed credit.
3. Bill of entry (for imports of goods).
4. Debit note issued by supplier against a tax invoice.
5. Any document prescribed by the government (e.g., invoice issued by recipient under reverse charge).

ITC cannot be claimed on:
- Pro-forma invoices.
- Payment vouchers (used in RCM where supplier is unregistered).
- Delivery challans.
- Documents without mandatory GST details.

Mandatory details on a valid tax invoice:
- GSTIN of supplier and recipient.
- Invoice number and date.
- HSN/SAC code.
- Description, quantity, and value of goods/services.
- Taxable value and tax rate.
- Place of supply (for inter-state transactions).
- Signature/digital signature.

================================================================================
PART 10: GST PAYMENT MECHANISM — LEDGERS AND CHALLANS
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_026]
[TOPIC: Three Electronic Ledgers under GST]
[GST_FORM: PMT-01 | PMT-02 | PMT-05]
[SECTION: Section 49 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rules 85 | Rule 86 | Rule 87 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Payment]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/payments/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Every registered taxpayer has three electronic ledgers maintained on the GST Portal:

1. Electronic Cash Ledger (Form GST PMT-05):
- Records all cash deposits made by the taxpayer via challan.
- Debited when taxes, interest, penalties, fees are paid from this ledger.
- Balance maintained separately for IGST, CGST, SGST, and Cess.
- Cash deposited in one tax head (e.g., CGST) cannot be used to pay another head (e.g., SGST).

2. Electronic Credit Ledger (Form GST PMT-02):
- Records all ITC availed by the taxpayer.
- Debited when ITC is used to offset tax liability.
- IGST ITC can offset IGST first, then CGST, then SGST.
- CGST ITC can only offset CGST liability.
- SGST/UTGST ITC can only offset SGST/UTGST liability.
- Cannot be used for payment of interest, penalty, or fees.

3. Electronic Liability Ledger (Form GST PMT-01):
- Auto-updated by the system with tax liabilities as declared in GSTR-3B.
- Gets discharged when payments are made from Cash or Credit Ledger.
- Shows cumulative outstanding dues.

---
[CHUNK_027]
[TOPIC: Form GST PMT-06 — Payment Challan (Complete Guide)]
[GST_FORM: PMT-06]
[SECTION: Section 49 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 87 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Payment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based | Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/payments/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GST PMT-06 is the universal challan for GST payments. It is used to deposit:
- GST tax (IGST, CGST, SGST, Cess)
- Interest
- Penalty
- Late fees
- Any other amount payable under the Act

Challan generation:
1. Login to GST Portal → Services → Payments → Create Challan.
2. Select GSTIN (auto-fills name and address).
3. Enter amounts head-wise (IGST, CGST, SGST, Cess) for each minor head (Tax, Interest, Penalty, Fee, Other).
4. Select payment mode: Net banking / UPI / Credit-Debit Card / NEFT-RTGS / OTC.
5. Click Generate Challan — CPIN (Challan Portal Identification Number) is generated.
6. CPIN is valid for 15 days. Payment must be made within this period.

After successful payment:
- Bank generates a CIN (Challan Identification Number).
- Amount is credited to the taxpayer's Electronic Cash Ledger immediately for online payments.
- For NEFT/RTGS: Reflected after bank processes the payment.
- For online payments made after 8 PM: Credited on the same day.

QRMP taxpayers and PMT-06:
- For M1 and M2 of each quarter, QRMP taxpayers must pay via PMT-06.
- Due date: 25th of the following month.
- Two payment methods:
  - Fixed Sum Method (FSM): Pre-filled challan for 35% of last quarter's cash payment (or 100% of last month's cash payment if monthly filer in previous quarter).
  - Self-Assessment Method (SAM): Manually assess and pay actual liability.

GST practitioners can generate challans on behalf of clients but cannot opt in/out of QRMP scheme for clients.

---
[CHUNK_028]
[TOPIC: Form GST PMT-07 — Challan Discrepancy Resolution]
[GST_FORM: PMT-07 | PMT-04]
[SECTION: Section 49 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 87 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Payment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/payments/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Error_resolution]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

If the taxpayer's bank account is debited but no CIN (Challan Identification Number) is generated or communicated to the GST Portal, the taxpayer can file Form GST PMT-07 through the Common Portal to the bank or electronic gateway for assistance.

Alternatively, the Electronic Cash Ledger may be updated based on the RBI's e-Scroll if the details match the CPIN generated on the portal.

Form GST PMT-04: Used if a CIN is generated but the amount is not correctly reflected in the Electronic Cash Ledger or Electronic Credit Ledger or Electronic Liability Ledger. Used to report the discrepancy to the jurisdictional officer.

---

================================================================================
PART 11: RECONCILIATION — COMPLETE GUIDE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_029]
[TOPIC: GSTR-1 vs GSTR-3B Reconciliation — Why and How]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 37 | Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 88C CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Reconciliation]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-1 and GSTR-3B reconciliation is mandatory before filing GSTR-9 and should ideally be done monthly.

Why mismatches occur:
1. Wrong table reporting: Supply reported in wrong table in GSTR-3B (e.g., zero-rated in 3.1a instead of 3.1b).
2. Timing difference: Invoice uploaded in GSTR-1 in one month, tax paid in GSTR-3B in a different month.
3. Credit note/debit note mismatch: CDN reported in GSTR-1 not reflected proportionately in GSTR-3B.
4. Advance receipt: Advance tax declared in GSTR-3B but invoice not yet in GSTR-1.
5. Amendment mismatch: GSTR-1A amendments not mirrored in GSTR-3B correction.
6. IGST vs CGST/SGST misclassification: Inter-state supply reported as intra-state or vice versa.

Reconciliation steps:
1. Download GSTR-1 summary from the portal for all months of the FY.
2. Download GSTR-3B summary for all months.
3. Compare Table 3.1(a) of GSTR-3B with taxable B2B + B2C supplies in GSTR-1.
4. Compare Table 3.1(b) with zero-rated supplies in GSTR-1 Tables 6A/6B.
5. Identify and document all differences.
6. Correct in subsequent return periods (no amendment of filed GSTR-3B is allowed).

---
[CHUNK_030]
[TOPIC: GSTR-2B vs Purchase Register Reconciliation]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-2B | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 38 | Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 36(4) | Rule 60 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Reconciliation | ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Manual_gstr2b.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2020-09-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-2B reconciliation with purchase register is essential to ensure ITC claimed in GSTR-3B is correct and defensible.

Step-by-step process:
1. Download GSTR-2B from GST Portal (Services → Returns → Returns Dashboard → GSTR-2B tile → Download).
2. Export your purchase register / accounts payable data.
3. Match each invoice in purchase register with GSTR-2B using:
   - Supplier GSTIN
   - Invoice number
   - Invoice date
   - Invoice value
4. Categorise results:
   - Matched: ITC available → claim in GSTR-3B.
   - In purchase register but NOT in GSTR-2B: Supplier has not filed GSTR-1. Follow up with supplier. Do NOT claim this ITC yet.
   - In GSTR-2B but NOT in purchase register: Check if invoice was received; update books.
   - Amount mismatch: Verify original invoice. If portal is wrong, supplier must amend via GSTR-1A.
5. Identify ineligible ITC (Section 17(5) blocked credits) and exclude.
6. Claim only matched and eligible ITC in GSTR-3B Table 4.

Rule 36(4): From FY 2022-23 onwards, no provisional ITC. Only 100% of ITC in GSTR-2B can be claimed. No additional 5% provisional credit allowed.

Record retention: Under GST law, all records (invoices, books, return filings) must be maintained for at least 72 months (6 years) from the date of filing the relevant annual return.

---
[CHUNK_031]
[TOPIC: GSTR-9 Annual Reconciliation — Key Checks]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-9]
[SECTION: Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 80 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Reconciliation | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Manual_gstr9.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reconciliation | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Before filing GSTR-9, verify:

1. Outward supplies (Sales) reconciliation:
   - Total taxable supplies across all months of GSTR-1 should match GSTR-9 Table 4.
   - Total taxes paid across all GSTR-3B filings (Table 3.1) should match GSTR-9 Table 9.
   - Any missed invoices in any month's GSTR-1 must be adjusted in GSTR-9 Tables 10/11.

2. ITC reconciliation:
   - Total ITC claimed across all months of GSTR-3B Table 4A should match GSTR-9 Table 6.
   - Table 8A in GSTR-9 (auto-populated from GSTR-2B, non-editable) shows ITC available from suppliers.
   - Table 8D = Table 8A minus Table 8C = difference between available and claimed ITC. This is the ITC lapsed/not availed.
   - Investigate Table 8D carefully — large amounts attract scrutiny.

3. Outward vs inward reconciliation:
   - GSTR-9 asks for total supplies separately (B2B, B2C, exports, etc.) — must match financial accounts.

4. HSN-wise summary (Table 17): From FY 2024-25, this table is mandatory. HSN-wise details of outward supplies are required. Portal provides a downloadable template.

5. Document-wise details of Table 8A (from FY 2023-24): Available for download in Excel format (B2B, B2BA, CDNR, CDRA, ECO, ECOA tables).

---

PART 12: GST NOTICES — DETAILED GUIDE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_032]
[TOPIC: Types of GST Notices — Complete Classification]
[GST_FORM: ASMT-10 | DRC-01 | DRC-01A | DRC-01B | ADT-01 | REG-03 | REG-17]
[SECTION: Section 61 | Section 65 | Section 73 | Section 74 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 99 | Rule 142 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Circular | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GST notices can be categorised as follows:

A. Assessment Notices:
- ASMT-10: Scrutiny notice under Section 61 / Rule 99 — issued for discrepancies found in return.
- ASMT-11: Taxpayer reply to ASMT-10.
- ASMT-12: Order accepting explanation after scrutiny.
- ASMT-13: Best judgement assessment order if no reply to ASMT-10.

B. Show Cause Notices (Demand):
- FORM GST DRC-01: Show cause notice for unpaid tax/short-paid tax/wrong refund/wrong ITC under Sections 73/74.
- FORM GST DRC-01A: Summary of proposed demand before SCN — gives taxpayer an opportunity to respond informally before formal SCN.
- FORM GST DRC-01B: Intimation of difference between liability in GSTR-1 and GSTR-3B.

C. Refund Notices:
- FORM GST RFD-03: Deficiency memo for incomplete refund application.
- FORM GST RFD-08: Notice to reject refund application.

D. Registration Notices:
- FORM GST REG-03: Notice seeking clarification during registration.
- FORM GST REG-17: Notice for cancellation of registration.

E. Audit/Investigation:
- FORM GST ADT-01: Notice for departmental audit under Section 65.
- FORM GST ADT-03: Notice after audit findings.

F. Return Defaulter:
- FORM GSTR-3A: System-generated notice for non-filing of GSTR-3B.
- FORM 3A: Notice for non-filing of GSTR-1.

---
[CHUNK_033]
[TOPIC: DRC-01B — GSTR-1 vs GSTR-3B Liability Mismatch Notice]
[GST_FORM: DRC-01B | DRC-03]
[SECTION: Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 88C CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2022-08-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GST DRC-01B: Intimation of difference in liability between GSTR-1 and GSTR-3B.

Trigger: The system automatically generates this intimation when the liability declared in GSTR-1 exceeds the liability declared and paid in GSTR-3B for the same period, beyond a specified threshold.

Taxpayer options on receiving DRC-01B:
1. File DRC-01B reply on the portal, either:
   a. Accepting the discrepancy → Pay differential tax with interest using Form GST DRC-03.
   b. Providing explanation for the difference (e.g., credit note, amendment, pre-payment, etc.).

Timeline: Must respond within 30 days of receiving DRC-01B. If no response, the officer may initiate Section 73/74 proceedings.

GSTR-3B filing impact: From 2024 onwards, in certain cases, GSTR-3B of the next period may be blocked if an outstanding DRC-01B is not addressed.

---
[CHUNK_034]
[TOPIC: GST Audit — Sections 65 and 66]
[GST_FORM: ADT-01 | ADT-02 | ADT-04]
[SECTION: Section 65 | Section 66 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 101 | Rule 102 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice | Assessment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 65 — Departmental Audit:
- Conducted by the Commissioner or an officer authorised by them.
- Notice in FORM GST ADT-01 given at least 15 working days in advance.
- Audit to be completed within 3 months (extendable by Commissioner up to 6 months).
- Taxpayer must provide all records and facilities.
- Audit findings communicated in FORM GST ADT-02.
- If discrepancy found: Officer must inform taxpayer within 30 days of completion of audit for payment of tax/interest/penalty.

Section 66 — Special Audit by CA/CMA:
- Commissioner can order special audit by a CA or CMA if the case is complex.
- Conducted at the direction of the Commissioner.
- Report submitted in FORM GST ADT-04 within 90 days (extendable).
- Cost of the audit borne by the government.

---
[CHUNK_035]
[TOPIC: Responding to GST Show Cause Notice — Practical Guide]
[GST_FORM: DRC-01 | DRC-06 | APL-01]
[SECTION: Section 73 | Section 74 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 142 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice | Appeal]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Steps to respond to a GST Show Cause Notice (SCN) under Section 73/74:

1. Read the SCN carefully — identify:
   - Sections invoked (73 or 74).
   - Specific allegations (non-payment, wrong ITC, wrong exemption).
   - Demand amount (tax, interest, penalty separately).
   - Response deadline (typically 30 days from date of receipt, extendable on application).

2. Gather supporting evidence:
   - All relevant invoices.
   - GSTR-1, GSTR-3B, GSTR-2B downloaded from portal.
   - Books of account (purchase/sales ledgers).
   - Payment proof.

3. Prepare written reply:
   - Reference the SCN number and date.
   - Address each allegation point by point with legal arguments and documentary evidence.
   - Cite relevant case law where applicable.
   - Request personal hearing if needed.

4. File reply on GST Portal:
   - Services → User Services → My Applications → Show Cause Notice.
   - Upload reply and supporting documents.

5. If demand is valid:
   - Pay under Section 73: Pay tax + interest to avoid penalty (within 30 days of SCN for full penalty waiver; within 60 days as per Budget 2024 amendment once notified).
   - Pay under Section 74: Pay tax + interest + 15% penalty (within 30 days) or 25% penalty (within 30 days of hearing order) to avoid higher penalty.

6. Appeal:
   - If order is unfavourable: File appeal before GST Appellate Authority within 3 months using FORM GST APL-01.
   - Deposit 10% of disputed tax to file appeal (waived in some cases).

---

================================================================================
PART 13: GST REFUNDS — COMPLETE GUIDE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_036]
[TOPIC: GST Refund — Types and Legal Basis]
[GST_FORM: RFD-01]
[SECTION: Section 54 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 89 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Exporter | Regular | All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Refund]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/refund/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Legal basis: Section 54 of CGST Act.

Situations where refund can be claimed (via Form GST RFD-01):
1. Tax paid on zero-rated supplies (exports of services with IGST payment; supplies to SEZ units/developers).
2. ITC accumulated on zero-rated supplies (exports of goods/services under LUT/Bond without IGST payment).
3. ITC accumulated due to inverted duty structure (input tax rate > output tax rate).
4. Excess balance in Electronic Cash Ledger.
5. Tax paid on supply later determined to be inter-state when paid as intra-state (or vice versa).
6. Refund due to assessment, provisional assessment, appeal, or any other order.
7. Tax paid on deemed exports (by recipient or supplier).
8. Excess tax paid due to cancellation or termination of contract for services.

Situations where RFD-01 is NOT to be filed:
- Exports of goods subject to export duty.
- IGST paid on export of goods where shipping bill acts as automatic refund application.

Time limit: 2 years from the "relevant date" (date of export, date of payment, date of acknowledgement of order, etc.).

---
[CHUNK_037]
[TOPIC: GST Refund — Process from RFD-01 to RFD-06]
[GST_FORM: RFD-01 | RFD-02 | RFD-03 | RFD-04 | RFD-05 | RFD-06 | RFD-08]
[SECTION: Section 54 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 89 | Rule 90 | Rule 91 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Exporter | Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Refund]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Circular | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/refund/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Step-by-step refund process:

RFD-01: Online refund application filed by taxpayer on GST Portal (Services → Refunds → Application for Refund). Select refund type, upload documents, file using DSC/EVC. ARN (Acknowledgement Reference Number) is generated.

RFD-02: Acknowledgement issued by tax officer within 15 days if application is complete.

RFD-03: Deficiency memo if application is incomplete. Taxpayer must refile after correcting deficiencies.

RFD-04: Provisional refund order — 90% of claim granted within 7 days for zero-rated supplies (exports), before detailed scrutiny. Not applicable for all refund types.

RFD-05: Sanctioned refund order — final order after scrutiny. Issued within 60 days from RFD-02 date.

RFD-06: Payment order issued after RFD-05. Amount credited to taxpayer's bank account within 60 days from filing date.

RFD-08: Notice to show cause why refund should not be rejected. Taxpayer replies in RFD-09.

Track status: Services → Refunds → Track Application Status using ARN.

Common reasons for rejection/delay:
- Incomplete documents.
- Mismatch between RFD-01 data and GST returns (GSTR-1, GSTR-3B).
- Incorrect bank details.
- Unfiled GSTR-1 or GSTR-3B for the relevant periods.
- LUT not filed (for exports without IGST payment).

---
[CHUNK_038]
[TOPIC: GST Refund — Zero-Rated Supplies (Exports and SEZ)]
[GST_FORM: RFD-01 | RFD-11]
[SECTION: Section 16(3) IGST Act | Section 54 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 89 | Rule 96 | Rule 96A CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Exporter]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Refund]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: IGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/refund/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Zero-rated supplies: Exports of goods/services and supplies to SEZ units/developers are zero-rated. ITC on inputs used for zero-rated supplies is fully refundable.

Two options for exporters:
Option A (LUT/Bond route): Export without payment of IGST. File a Letter of Undertaking (LUT) annually in Form GST RFD-11 by 31st March. Claim refund of accumulated ITC via RFD-01.

Formula for refund (LUT route):
Refund = Net ITC × (Turnover of zero-rated supplies ÷ Adjusted Total Turnover) for the relevant period.

Option B (Tax payment route): Pay IGST on exports. Claim refund of IGST paid through the shipping bill (for goods) or through RFD-01 (for services).

For export of goods: Shipping bill is automatically treated as refund application. No separate RFD-01 needed. Customs and GST systems share data.

For export of services: File RFD-01 with invoice details, bank realization certificates (BRC/FIRC), or Foreign Inward Remittance Advice.

---
[CHUNK_039]
[TOPIC: GST Refund — Inverted Duty Structure]
[GST_FORM: RFD-01]
[SECTION: Section 54(3)(ii) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 89(5) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Refund]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Instruction]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Inverted Duty Structure (IDS): When the tax rate on inputs is higher than the tax rate on output supplies, accumulation of ITC results. This accumulated ITC is eligible for refund.

Formula under Rule 89(5):
Maximum Refund = [Turnover of inverted-rated supply × Net ITC ÷ Adjusted Total Turnover] − Tax payable on inverted-rated supply

"Net ITC" = ITC availed on inputs (excluding input services, capital goods) used in the relevant period.
"Adjusted Total Turnover" = Total turnover in the state minus exempt supplies for the relevant period.

Important restrictions:
- Refund only on ITC from inputs — NOT on input services or capital goods.
- Not available for nil-rated or fully exempt supplies.
- Cannot club IDS refund with exports refund for the same supplies.

Provisional refund: CBIC Instruction 6/2025 (dated 3rd October 2025): 90% provisional refund of accumulated ITC in IDS cases, effective 1st October 2025 for applications filed after that date.

Documents required: GSTR-1, GSTR-3B for the refund period; Statement 1A (auto-generated); Declaration under Rule 89(2)(l) and 89(2)(m); Undertaking for no unjust enrichment; CA certificate if refund > Rs. 2 lakh; invoices of inward and outward supplies.

---

PART 14: GSTR-9 AND GSTR-9C — ANNUAL RETURN FILING GUIDE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_040]
[TOPIC: GSTR-9 Table-by-Table Guide]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-9]
[SECTION: Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 80 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Schema]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Manual_gstr9.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-9 has the following key tables:

PART I (Tables 1-3): Basic information — GSTIN, legal name, financial year.

PART II (Tables 4-5): Details of outward and inward supplies for the year:
- Table 4A-4L: Outward supplies (taxable, zero-rated, nil-rated, exempted, non-GST), net of CDNs.
- Table 5A-5N: Details of outward supplies on which tax was not payable (exempt, nil, non-GST).

PART III (Tables 6-8): Details of ITC:
- Table 6A: Total ITC availed through GSTR-3B (sum of Table 4A of GSTR-3B) — NON-EDITABLE.
- Table 6B-6L: ITC reversals declared in GSTR-3B and ineligible ITC.
- Table 7A-7H: ITC reversals and additions in GSTR-9 (if different from GSTR-3B).
- Table 8A: ITC available from GSTR-2B — NON-EDITABLE (from FY 2023-24 onwards).
- Table 8C: ITC reclaimed (previously reversed under Rule 42/43 etc.).
- Table 8D: Difference between 8A and 8C + 6B — ITC lapsed or not claimed.

PART IV (Table 9): Details of taxes paid during the year (from GSTR-3B) — auto-filled, tax payable column editable.

PART V (Tables 10-14): Transactions/adjustments of FY reported in next year's returns.

PART VI (Tables 15-17): Other information:
- Table 15: Refund details.
- Table 16: Demand and payment details.
- Table 17: HSN-wise summary of outward supplies (MANDATORY from FY 2024-25).
- Table 18: Late fee payable and paid (new from FY 2024-25).

---
[CHUNK_041]
[TOPIC: GSTR-9C — Reconciliation Statement Guide]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-9C]
[SECTION: Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 80(3) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Reconciliation]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Circular | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Manual_gstr9.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-9C is a self-certified reconciliation statement reconciling data in GSTR-9 with audited financial statements.

Applicability: Registered taxpayers with aggregate turnover exceeding Rs. 5 crore in the financial year.

Note: From FY 2020-21 onwards, GSTR-9C is self-certified by the taxpayer (not required to be certified by CA/CMA for most cases). The taxpayer (or their authorised representative) certifies the reconciliation.

What GSTR-9C covers:
- Part A: Reconciliation statement — compares turnover, taxable turnover, tax paid as per books versus GSTR-9.
- Part A Table 5: Reconciliation of gross turnover (books vs GST returns).
- Part A Table 7: Reconciliation of taxable turnover.
- Part A Table 9: Reconciliation of tax paid.
- Part A Table 11-16: Reconciliation of ITC (availed, reversed, net ITC).
- Part B: Certification (self-certification by taxpayer).

Late fee for GSTR-9C: As per Circular No. 246/03/2025-GST, late fee under Section 47(2) applies to GSTR-9C for delayed filing where it is required along with GSTR-9. Both GSTR-9 and GSTR-9C late fees are calculated together.

---

================================================================================
PART 15: GSTR-10 — FINAL RETURN ON CANCELLATION
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_042]
[TOPIC: GSTR-10 — Final Return After Registration Cancellation]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-10]
[SECTION: Section 45 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 81 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GSTR-10 is the final return filed after GST registration is cancelled or surrendered.

Applicability: All registered persons whose registration is cancelled (either voluntarily or by the department), except:
- Input Service Distributors.
- Non-resident taxable persons.
- Persons paying TDS under Section 51.
- Persons paying TCS under Section 52.

Due date: Within 3 months from the date of cancellation order or the effective date of cancellation, whichever is later.

What GSTR-10 requires:
- Details of stocks held on the effective date of cancellation (including goods in transit, semi-finished, and finished goods, as well as capital goods).
- ITC on these stocks must be reversed (by paying equivalent ITC as tax).
- Details of ITC reversed on closing stock.

Penalty for non-filing: If GSTR-10 is not filed within the due date, a notice in FORM GST REG-23 is issued by the proper officer. Taxpayer must then file GSTR-10 within 15 days.

After filing GSTR-10: The registration is formally closed. The taxpayer cannot make any further transactions under the cancelled GSTIN.
