================================================================================
PART 16: GST REGISTRATION — COMPLETE GUIDE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_043]
[TOPIC: GST Registration — Who Must Register and How]
[GST_FORM: REG-01 | REG-06]
[SECTION: Section 22 | Section 23 | Section 24 | Section 25 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 8 | Rule 9 | Rule 10 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Registration]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Instruction | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/registration/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Mandatory registration — persons who must register regardless of turnover:
- Persons making inter-state taxable supplies.
- Casual taxable persons making taxable supplies.
- Persons liable to pay tax under reverse charge.
- Non-resident taxable persons.
- E-commerce operators.
- Persons required to deduct TDS under Section 51.
- Persons making supplies on behalf of others as agent.
- Input Service Distributors.
- Persons supplying through e-commerce operators (if the ECO collects TCS).

Registration process:
1. File application in Form GST REG-01 online on the GST Portal.
2. If Aadhaar-authenticated: Processed within 7 working days.
3. If not Aadhaar-authenticated or high-risk: Physical verification may be required; must be completed within 30 calendar days.
4. If clarification needed: Officer sends Form GST REG-03; taxpayer responds in Form GST REG-04 within the time specified (usually 7 working days).
5. On approval: GSTIN (GST Identification Number) is issued in Form GST REG-06.
6. On rejection: Rejection order in Form GST REG-05.

GSTIN structure: 15-digit alphanumeric number: 2 digits (state code) + 10 digits (PAN) + 1 digit (entity number) + 1 digit (Z by default) + 1 digit (checksum).

---
[CHUNK_044]
[TOPIC: GST Registration — Cancellation and Revocation]
[GST_FORM: REG-16 | REG-17 | REG-18 | REG-19 | REG-21]
[SECTION: Section 29 | Section 30 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 20 | Rule 21 | Rule 23 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Registration]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/registration/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Voluntary cancellation: A taxpayer can apply for cancellation if they are no longer liable to be registered (turnover below threshold, business closed, change of business structure).

Suo moto cancellation by department: The department can cancel registration if the taxpayer:
- Has not filed returns for 6 consecutive months (monthly filers) or 3 consecutive quarters (quarterly filers).
- Has not commenced business within 6 months of registration.
- Has obtained registration by fraud.
- Violates anti-profiteering rules.

Cancellation procedure:
- Department issues notice in Form GST REG-17.
- Taxpayer responds in Form GST REG-18 (within 7 working days).
- On cancellation: Form GST REG-19 (cancellation order) is issued.

Revocation of cancellation:
- If the department cancelled registration suo moto, the taxpayer can apply for revocation in Form GST REG-21 within 90 days.
- Extended revocation window: Section 30 amended to allow revocation application up to 30th June 2023 (one-time window for historical cancellations).

---

================================================================================
PART 17: REVERSE CHARGE MECHANISM (RCM)
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_045]
[TOPIC: Reverse Charge Mechanism — Section 9(3) and 9(4)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 9(3) | Section 9(4) CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | Composition]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/central-tax-notifications-2017.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Under the reverse charge mechanism (RCM), the liability to pay GST shifts from the supplier to the recipient.

Section 9(3) — Statutory Reverse Charge: Applies to specific categories of goods and services notified by the government. Examples:
- Services from goods transport agencies (GTA) to registered persons.
- Services by an advocate to a business entity.
- Services provided by Government/Local Authority (except notified services).
- Import of services.
- Rent-a-cab services.
- Security services provided by a non-body corporate to a registered person.
- Sponsorship services from non-corporate bodies.

Section 9(4) — Reverse Charge from Unregistered Suppliers: Applies when a registered person receives supplies from unregistered suppliers in notified categories. Currently applies in limited categories (as the broad 9(4) was suspended and reintroduced for specific cases).

Key compliance requirements for RCM:
- Recipient must pay tax under RCM even if they cannot claim ITC (e.g., composition taxpayer).
- ITC on RCM paid is available to the recipient in the same period (if eligible).
- Tax invoice must be raised by the recipient (self-invoice) when receiving services from unregistered suppliers.
- RCM liability is paid in cash only — cannot be offset using ITC.
- Reported in GSTR-3B Table 3.1(d) (inward supplies under reverse charge).

---

================================================================================
PART 18: PLACE OF SUPPLY RULES
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_046]
[TOPIC: Place of Supply — Why It Matters and Basic Rules]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 10 | Section 11 | Section 12 | Section 13 IGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: IGST_Act | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/igst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Place of Supply (POS) determines whether a transaction is intra-state (CGST + SGST) or inter-state (IGST). Correctly determining POS is critical for:
- Correct tax type (CGST/SGST vs IGST).
- Correct revenue allocation to states.
- Avoiding notices for wrong tax head payment.

For goods:
- General rule: Where goods are delivered (destination-based).
- For movement of goods: Location where goods are delivered to recipient.
- For assembled/installed goods: Place of installation/assembly.
- For goods on board a conveyance (train, aircraft, vessel): Destination of the conveyance.

For services (key rules):
- General rule: Location of the registered recipient (if registered). If not registered, location of the recipient.
- Services related to immovable property: Location of the immovable property.
- Restaurant and food services: Where the service is actually performed.
- Transportation of goods: Destination of the goods.
- Passenger transport: Where the journey begins.
- Banking/financial services to registered person: Location of recipient.
- Telecom services: Location where SIM card is issued (fixed telecom), or location of recipient.

---

================================================================================
PART 19: E-INVOICING — COMPLETE RULES
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_047]
[TOPIC: E-Invoicing — Applicability, Process, and IRN]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: NA]
[RULE: Rule 48(4) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | Exporter]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: E_Invoice]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification | IRP_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://einvoice1.gst.gov.in/]
[VALID_FROM: 2020-10-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

E-invoicing applicability (as of 2024-25): Mandatory for registered taxpayers with aggregate turnover exceeding Rs. 5 crore in any preceding financial year.

Exempted from e-invoicing: SEZ units for outward supplies; Insurance companies; Banking companies; Financial Institutions; NBFCs; GTA (Goods Transport Agencies) for specific services; Multiplexes; Passenger transportation companies.

E-invoicing process:
1. Supplier generates invoice on their own ERP/accounting software.
2. Invoice is uploaded to the Invoice Registration Portal (IRP) in JSON format.
3. IRP validates the data, generates a unique IRN (Invoice Reference Number) — hash of supplier GSTIN + financial year + document type + document number.
4. IRP digitally signs the invoice and generates a QR code.
5. IRP returns the signed JSON with IRN and QR code.
6. Supplier prints IRN and QR code on the invoice.
7. IRP automatically shares the invoice data with GST portal (auto-populates GSTR-1) and e-Way Bill portal.

IRN: A unique 64-character alphanumeric hash. Once generated, the invoice cannot be altered. Cancellation must be done within 24 hours of IRN generation.

QR code on e-invoice: Contains key fields — supplier GSTIN, recipient GSTIN, invoice number, date, invoice value, number of line items, HSN of major items, IRN, and signed hash.

---
[CHUNK_048]
[TOPIC: E-Way Bill — Rules, Generation, and Validity]
[GST_FORM: EWB-01]
[SECTION: Section 68 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 138 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: EWB]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | EWB_Portal | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://ewaybillgst.gov.in/]
[VALID_FROM: 2018-04-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

E-Way Bill: An electronic document generated on the e-Way Bill portal (ewaybillgst.gov.in) for movement of goods where consignment value exceeds Rs. 50,000.

Who generates: Supplier, recipient, or transporter (whoever initiates the movement).

When NOT required:
- Transport by non-motorised vehicles.
- Goods transported by Customs under Customs supervision.
- Goods transported by defence vehicles.
- Consignment value ≤ Rs. 50,000.
- Exempted goods (e.g., fresh milk, eggs, curd, vegetables — as per Annexure to Rule 138).
- Intra-state movement (if the state government has set a higher threshold or exempted specific goods).

E-Way Bill components:
- Part A: Invoice details (supply type, goods description, GSTIN of supplier/recipient, value, HSN, POS).
- Part B: Transporter details (vehicle number or transport document number).

Validity: Calculated from the date and time of generation:
- Other than Over-Dimensional Cargo (ODC): 1 day per 200 km (or part thereof). Example: 450 km = 3 days validity.
- ODC: 1 day per 20 km.
- Validity can be extended 8 hours before or after expiry.

Intra-state threshold: Most states follow Rs. 50,000. Some states have different thresholds for intra-state movement.

Link with GSTR-1: Inconsistency between GSTR-1 supply details and e-Way Bill data is a primary trigger for GST scrutiny notices.

---

================================================================================
PART 20: LATE FEES AND INTEREST — DETAILED RATES
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_049]
[TOPIC: Late Fee Rates — All GST Returns]
[GST_FORM: Multiple]
[SECTION: Section 47 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Penalty | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Late fee is charged per day of delay from due date to date of actual filing.

GSTR-1:
- Normal return (where there is tax liability): Rs. 50/day (Rs. 25 CGST + Rs. 25 SGST).
- Nil return: Rs. 20/day (Rs. 10 CGST + Rs. 10 SGST).
- Maximum capped at Rs. 10,000 (Rs. 5,000 CGST + Rs. 5,000 SGST).

GSTR-3B:
- Normal return:
  - Turnover > Rs. 5 crore: Rs. 50/day. Maximum Rs. 10,000.
  - Turnover Rs. 1.5 crore to Rs. 5 crore: Rs. 25/day. Maximum Rs. 5,000.
  - Turnover ≤ Rs. 1.5 crore: Rs. 25/day. Maximum Rs. 2,000.
- Nil return: Rs. 20/day. Capped at Rs. 500 (Rs. 250 CGST + Rs. 250 SGST).

CMP-08: No late fee on CMP-08 per se; composition taxpayers pay interest for delayed payment.

GSTR-9:
- Rs. 200/day (Rs. 100 CGST + Rs. 100 SGST). Maximum capped at 0.25% of turnover in the state/UT.

GSTR-9C: Late fee same as GSTR-9 (Circular 246/03/2025-GST). Combined late fee on the consolidated GSTR-9 + GSTR-9C filing.

GSTR-7 (TDS return): Rs. 200/day (Rs. 100 CGST + Rs. 100 SGST). No maximum specified; continues to accrue.
Exception: From October 2024, no late fee for delayed Nil GSTR-7.

---
[CHUNK_050]
[TOPIC: Interest on Delayed GST Payment]
[GST_FORM: Multiple]
[SECTION: Section 50 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Payment]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Penalty]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Interest rates:
- 18% per annum: On tax not paid or short-paid by due date. Calculated on net tax payable (i.e., after ITC offset).
- 24% per annum: On ITC wrongly availed or utilised. Also on tax collected but not paid.

Interest calculation basis:
- As per Section 50(1): Interest on net tax payable from the day after the due date to the date of actual payment.
- As per amendment to Section 50 (Finance Act 2021): Interest is calculated on net cash tax liability (i.e., after offsetting ITC), not on gross liability. Retrospective effect from 1st July 2017.

Interest on ITC reversal (Rule 37):
- When ITC is reversed for non-payment to supplier within 180 days, interest at 18% from the date of availing ITC to the date of reversal.

No interest if:
- GSTR-3B is filed on time but challan payment is delayed for technical reasons (bank issues) — officer discretion may apply.
- Under Section 128A: Waiver of interest for demands under Section 73 for FY 2017-18 to 2019-20, subject to full tax payment by 31st March 2025.

================================================================================
PART 22: COMMON COMPLIANCE ERRORS AND HOW TO AVOID THEM
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_053]
[TOPIC: Top GST Compliance Errors That Trigger Notices]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B | GSTR-2B]
[SECTION: Section 39 | Section 17 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 36(4) | Rule 88C CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice | Return_Filing | ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Instruction | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reconciliation | Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

1. GSTR-1 vs GSTR-3B mismatch: Tax liability declared in GSTR-1 exceeds what was paid in GSTR-3B. Triggers DRC-01B automatically. Fix: Reconcile before filing GSTR-3B every month.

2. Excess ITC claim vs GSTR-2B: Claiming more ITC in GSTR-3B Table 4A than what appears in GSTR-2B. Triggers ASMT-10. Fix: Only claim ITC reflected in GSTR-2B per Rule 36(4).

3. Non-filing of GSTR-1 before GSTR-3B: Sequential filing rule violation. Fix: Always file GSTR-1 first.

4. Wrong Place of Supply: Charging CGST+SGST instead of IGST or vice versa. Triggers demand for differential tax. Fix: Always verify POS before raising invoice.

5. Ignoring RCM liability: Not paying GST under reverse charge on eligible services (advocate fees, GTA, security services etc.). Triggers Section 73 demand. Fix: Identify all RCM categories and report in GSTR-3B 3.1(d) every month.

6. Late filing of returns: Accumulates late fees (up to Rs. 10,000 per return) and interest (18% p.a.). Fix: File before due dates.

7. ITC on blocked credits: Claiming ITC on vehicles, food, personal expenses etc. under Section 17(5). Triggers notice with 24% interest on reversal. Fix: Maintain a blocked-credit exclusion list in your books.

8. Mismatch between e-Way Bill and GSTR-1: Inconsistent description, value, or GSTIN between portal records. Triggers scrutiny. Fix: Verify e-Way Bill data matches invoice data before movement.

9. HSN code errors: Wrong or missing HSN codes. Triggers validation errors and scrutiny. Fix: Use 8-digit HSN for all supplies (mandatory for turnover > Rs. 5 crore, 4-digit for others).

10. Non-filing after cancellation (GSTR-10): Forgetting to file the final return after registration cancellation. Fix: File GSTR-10 within 3 months of cancellation order.

================================================================================
PART 23: FORM GSTR-5 — NON-RESIDENT FOREIGN TAXPAYER
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_055]
[TOPIC: GSTR-5 — Who Files It and Registration Rules]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-5 | REG-09]
[SECTION: Section 27 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 63 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: NRTP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GSTR-5 is the monthly GST return filed exclusively by Non-Resident Taxable Persons (NRTPs) — foreign individuals or foreign entities that temporarily conduct taxable business activities in India without a fixed place of business or residence.

Who is an NRTP:
- Does not maintain a fixed business establishment in India.
- Comes to India for a short period (e.g., for trade fairs, exhibitions, short-term project work) to make taxable supplies.
- Distinct from: OIDAR service providers (who file GSTR-5A, not GSTR-5).

Registration for NRTPs (Section 27):
- Must apply for temporary GST registration in Form GST REG-09 before starting any business activity in India.
- Registration is valid for the period specified in the application or 90 days, whichever is earlier. Can be extended.
- Must deposit advance tax equal to the estimated tax liability for the entire registration period at the time of registration.
- An Indian resident with a valid PAN must act as the authorised signatory for the NRTP.

Due date: 13th of the month following the tax period. For the final period, within 7 days of registration expiry — whichever is earlier.

---
[CHUNK_056]
[TOPIC: GSTR-5 — Table Structure and Key Rules]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-5]
[SECTION: Section 27 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 63 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: NRTP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Schema]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-5 table structure:
- Basic Info: GSTIN (auto-filled), legal name, validity period, return period.
- Goods Imported: Bill of Entry details — port code, IGST paid, assessable value.
- Outward Supplies (Table 3): Invoice-wise B2B supplies to registered persons.
- B2C Large (Table 4): Inter-state supplies to unregistered persons where invoice value exceeds Rs. 1 lakh.
- Credit Notes / Debit Notes (Table 5/6): Notes issued against previous invoices.
- Tax Liability (Table 7): Summary of IGST, CGST, SGST, Cess.
- Tax Paid (Table 8): Payment from Electronic Cash Ledger.

Key rules:
- NRTPs can claim ITC only on imports of goods (bill of entry basis). Cannot claim ITC on inward supplies within India.
- All tax must be paid from the advance deposit made at time of registration (Electronic Cash Ledger).
- Data filed in GSTR-5 auto-populates the GSTR-2A and GSTR-2B of Indian buyer-recipients who purchased from the NRTP.
- Late fee: Rs. 50 per day (Rs. 25 CGST + Rs. 25 SGST). Interest at 18% p.a. on delayed payment.
- Penalties for non-filing: Portal blocks subsequent period returns; GSTIN may be cancelled.

---

================================================================================
PART 24: FORM GSTR-5A — OIDAR SERVICE PROVIDERS
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_057]
[TOPIC: GSTR-5A — Online Information and Database Access/Retrieval (OIDAR) Services]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-5A | REG-10]
[SECTION: Section 14 IGST Act | Section 24(xi) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 64 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: OIDAR]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: IGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

OIDAR services: Services delivered over the internet or electronic network, requiring minimal human intervention. Examples include: cloud services, software downloads, online gaming, e-books, music/video streaming, online advertising, distance learning.

Who files GSTR-5A:
- Non-resident OIDAR service providers supplying services to non-taxable persons (end consumers) in India.
- Must register on the GST portal in Form GST REG-10.

Key features:
- Due date: 20th of the month following the tax period.
- Tax must be paid in foreign currency converted at RBI reference rate.
- Only IGST applies (as supply is treated as inter-state/import of services).
- Payment must be made in cash only — no ITC available.
- Distinct from GSTR-5 (which is for NRTPs supplying goods/services within India with a physical presence).

---

================================================================================
PART 25: INVOICING RULES — COMPLETE GUIDE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_058]
[TOPIC: Tax Invoice — Mandatory Fields under Rule 46 of CGST Rules]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: Section 31 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 46 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP | Exporter]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

A tax invoice must contain all 21 mandatory fields prescribed under Rule 46 of the CGST Rules:

1. Name, address, and GSTIN of the supplier.
2. A consecutive serial number (max 16 characters, alphanumeric with dash/slash allowed) unique for a financial year.
3. Date of issue of the invoice.
4. Name, address, and GSTIN or UIN of the recipient (if registered). If unregistered and supply value > Rs. 50,000: name, address, and state name of recipient; delivery address if different.
5. HSN code of goods or SAC code of services.
6. Description of goods or services.
7. Quantity (number) and unit (UQC — Unique Quantity Code) of goods.
8. Total value of supply of goods or services.
9. Taxable value of supply — after accounting for any discount/abatement.
10. Rate of tax (CGST, SGST/UTGST, IGST, Cess separately).
11. Amount of tax charged (CGST, SGST/UTGST, IGST, Cess separately).
12. Place of supply — state name and code (for inter-state supply).
13. Address of delivery if different from place of supply.
14. Whether supply is on reverse charge basis.
15. Signature or digital signature of the supplier or their authorised representative.
16. IRN (Invoice Reference Number) and QR code — if e-invoice applicable.
17. For exports: declaration "Supply meant for export on payment of IGST" or "Supply meant for export under LUT without payment of IGST".

---
[CHUNK_059]
[TOPIC: Invoice Timing Rules — When Must Invoice Be Issued]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: Section 31 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 47 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Timing of invoice issuance:

For supply of GOODS:
- Where movement of goods is involved: Before or at the time of removal.
- Where no movement is involved: Before or at the time of delivery or making goods available.
- Goods sent on approval basis: Before or at time of supply, or 6 months from date of removal — whichever is earlier.

For supply of SERVICES:
- General rule: Within 30 days from the date of supply of service.
- By banking and insurance companies or financial institutions: Within 45 days.
- Continuous supply of services (where successive statements of account/payments are involved): On or before each due date of payment, or date of receipt of payment — whichever is earlier.
- Where service is completed before periodic payment: Within 30 days from the date of completion of each event specified in the contract.

Invoice for advance received:
- For services: If advance is received before supply, issue a receipt voucher. The invoice is issued as per normal rules when service is actually provided.
- For goods: No advance invoice; GST is payable on receipt of advance only for services, not goods (after 2018 amendment).

---
[CHUNK_060]
[TOPIC: Bill of Supply, Credit Note, Debit Note — Rules and Format]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: Section 31(3) | Section 34 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 49 | Rule 53 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Schema_reference]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Bill of Supply (Section 31(3)(c), Rule 49):
Issued instead of a tax invoice in these cases:
- Registered person supplying exempted goods or services.
- Composition scheme taxpayers.
- Exporters (in certain cases).
Must mention: "Composition taxable person, not eligible to collect tax on supplies" (for composition dealers). Must contain supplier details, description, value, but NO tax rate/amount columns.

Credit Note (Section 34(1)):
Issued when taxable value or GST charged in an invoice is more than the correct amount. Cases:
- Goods returned by recipient.
- Deficiency in services.
- Post-supply discount agreed upon in contract.
Must contain: Reference to original invoice number and date, GSTIN of supplier and recipient, reason for credit note, taxable value, tax amount adjusted.
Time limit: Cannot be issued after 30th November of the following FY or date of filing annual return — whichever is earlier.

Debit Note (Section 34(3)):
Issued when taxable value or GST charged in an invoice is less than the actual amount due. Cases:
- Value was understated.
- Tax was undercharged.
Amendment to Section 34: As of Finance Act 2021, debit note ITC is delinked from the date of the original invoice. Recipient can claim ITC up to 30th November of the FY to which the debit note pertains, regardless of the original invoice year.

Penalty for wrong/missing invoice: Rs. 10,000 or the tax evaded, whichever is higher (Section 122, CGST Act).

---
[CHUNK_061]
[TOPIC: E-Invoice IRP Reporting Timeline — Advisory November 2024]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: NA]
[RULE: Rule 48(4) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | Exporter]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: E_Invoice]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification | IRP_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://einvoice1.gst.gov.in/]
[VALID_FROM: 2025-04-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

CBIC Advisory (November 5, 2024) — IRN reporting time limit:
From April 1, 2025 onwards:
- Taxpayers with Aggregate Annual Turnover (AATO) of Rs. 10 crore or more must report all e-invoices (including credit notes and debit notes) to the Invoice Registration Portal (IRP) within 30 days of the document date.
- IRNs reported beyond 30 days from invoice date will be rejected by the IRP.
- This applies to B2B invoices, B2G invoices, export invoices, reverse charge invoices, credit notes, and debit notes.

Implication for CA/CS compliance platform:
- Any document for these taxpayers submitted to IRP after the 30-day window is invalid.
- All invoices older than 30 days at time of IRP upload will fail.
- This is a significant change for businesses with high invoice volumes or delayed processing.

================================================================================
PART 26: HSN AND SAC CODE RULES — COMPLETE GUIDE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_062]
[TOPIC: HSN Codes — What They Are and Digit Requirements by Turnover]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1]
[SECTION: NA]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/central-tax-notifications-2017.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2021-04-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | Schema_reference]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

HSN (Harmonized System of Nomenclature): An internationally standardised system used to classify goods. India has added 2 additional digits (8-digit codes) for deeper classification beyond the international 6-digit standard.

HSN digit requirements by turnover (PAN-level, preceding FY):

| Turnover Slab         | HSN Digits Required      | Applicability                  |
|-----------------------|--------------------------|--------------------------------|
| Up to Rs. 1.5 crore   | Exempt from HSN          | Not mandatory on invoice/GSTR  |
| Rs. 1.5 crore – Rs. 5 crore | 4-digit HSN        | Mandatory for B2B; optional B2C|
| Above Rs. 5 crore     | 6-digit HSN              | Mandatory for all supplies     |
| Exports               | 8-digit HSN              | Mandatory always               |

Important rule: Turnover is PAN-level (aggregated across all GSTINs under one PAN), not GSTIN-level. If a company with multiple branches has combined PAN-level turnover above Rs. 5 crore, 6-digit HSN is mandatory across ALL branches, even if individual GSTINs are below Rs. 5 crore.

From May 2025 onwards: GSTR-1 requires separate HSN-wise summary for B2B and B2C supplies, with rate and quantitative details.

Penalty for wrong/missing HSN code: Rs. 50,000 (Rs. 25,000 CGST + Rs. 25,000 SGST) under Section 125 of the CGST Act.

---
[CHUNK_063]
[TOPIC: SAC Codes — Service Accounting Codes under GST]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1]
[SECTION: NA]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/gst-goods-services-rates.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Rate_lookup | Schema_reference]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

SAC (Service Accounting Code): A 6-digit classification system for services under GST. All services fall under Chapter 99 of the HSN module. SAC codes are used to classify services for accurate tax rate determination and return reporting.

SAC code structure:
- First 2 digits: Always 99 (indicating services).
- Next 2 digits: Major service category (e.g., 82 = Legal services).
- Last 2 digits: Specific nature of service within the category.

Example:
- 998211: Legal advisory and representation services.
- 998213: Legal documentation for patents, copyrights, IP rights.
- 9954: Construction services.

SAC digit requirements by turnover:
- Turnover below Rs. 1.5 crore: Not mandatory.
- Turnover Rs. 1.5 crore to Rs. 5 crore: 4-digit SAC mandatory.
- Turnover above Rs. 5 crore: All 6 digits mandatory.
- SAC is always mandatory for all service suppliers in GSTR-1 and on invoices (unlike goods where small turnover businesses are exempt).

UQC (Unique Quantity Code): Mandatory on all tax invoices and GST documents. Represents the unit of measurement of goods (e.g., KGS, LTR, NOS, PCS, MTR, SQM). Required in GSTR-1 HSN summary as well.

---

================================================================================
PART 27: GSTR-9 — FY 2024-25 UPDATES AND APPLICABILITY
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_064]
[TOPIC: GSTR-9 Applicability — Turnover Thresholds and Exemptions (FY 2024-25)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-9]
[SECTION: Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 80 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/central-tax-notifications-2017.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2025-09-17]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Mandatory filing threshold for GSTR-9 (FY 2024-25 onwards):
- Mandatory for taxpayers with Aggregate Annual Turnover (AATO) above Rs. 2 crore.
- Taxpayers with AATO up to Rs. 2 crore are EXEMPT from filing GSTR-9 (voluntary filing is allowed).
- This exemption is now PERMANENT from FY 2024-25 onwards via Notification No. 15/2025-Central Tax dated 17 September 2025. Previously it was renewed year-by-year.

AATO computation: Computed at PAN level (all-India, all GSTINs under same PAN). Includes taxable, exempt, export, and inter-state supplies. Excludes GST itself and inward supplies under RCM.

GSTR-9C threshold: Mandatory for AATO above Rs. 5 crore. Below Rs. 5 crore, only GSTR-9 is required.

Who is ALWAYS exempt from GSTR-9 (regardless of turnover):
- Casual Taxable Persons (CTPs).
- Non-Resident Taxable Persons (NRTPs).
- Input Service Distributors (ISDs).
- TDS deductors under Section 51.
- TCS collectors under Section 52.
- Composition taxpayers (they file GSTR-4 instead).

GSTR-9 filing prerequisite: All monthly/quarterly GSTR-1 and GSTR-3B returns for the financial year must be filed before GSTR-9 can be filed.

GSTR-9 cannot be revised once filed. Additional tax dues identified after GSTR-9 can now be paid using ITC (via DRC-03) per Notification 13/2025-CT changes.

---
[CHUNK_065]
[TOPIC: GSTR-9 FY 2024-25 — Key New Changes (Notification 13/2025-CT)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-9]
[SECTION: Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 80 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Schema]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/central-tax-notifications-2017.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2025-09-17]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Schema_reference]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Significant changes to GSTR-9 form for FY 2024-25 via Notification 13/2025-Central Tax:

1. New Table 6A1: Separate reporting of ITC claimed in current FY that pertains to previous financial years (i.e., delayed ITC claims).

2. Table 8A updated: Now uses GSTR-2B data with invoice-wise reconciliation precision. Non-editable.

3. New reversal sub-tables: Separate disclosure of ITC reversals under Rule 37 (non-payment to supplier) and Rule 37A (supplier non-filing) within the annual return.

4. Table 9 (Tax Paid): Mandatory explanation required if there is a variance between tax liability declared and actual tax payment. No silent passage of unexplained differences.

5. Additional tax via ITC: From FY 2024-25, any additional tax liability identified in GSTR-9 can be paid using available ITC credits via DRC-03 (earlier only cash payment was allowed).

6. HSN Summary (Table 17): Mandatory for all taxpayers filing GSTR-9 (regardless of turnover), from FY 2024-25.

7. Late fee table (Table 18): New table explicitly showing late fee payable and paid.

8. GSTR-1A amendments: Auto-reflected in GSTR-9 Tables 4/5 for the year.

================================================================================
PART 28: GST AND E-COMMERCE — SECTION 9(5) SUPPLIES
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_066]
[TOPIC: Section 9(5) — E-Commerce Operator Tax Liability]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B | GSTR-8]
[SECTION: Section 9(5) CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: TCS_Collector | Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2019-10-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 9(5) of CGST Act: Notified categories of services supplied through e-commerce operators (ECOs) — the ECO is liable to pay GST, NOT the actual supplier (who may be an individual or unregistered person).

Services currently covered under Section 9(5) (as notified):
1. Passenger transportation services (e.g., Ola, Uber — cab aggregators).
2. Accommodation services by hotels/inns/guest houses etc. supplied through ECO (e.g., Airbnb, MakeMyTrip).
3. Housekeeping services (plumbers, electricians, carpenters) through ECO.
4. Restaurant services supplied through ECO (e.g., Swiggy, Zomato).

Impact on ECO:
- ECO must pay GST on the full supply value.
- ECO must register in every state where it operates (no aggregate turnover exemption).
- ECO reports these supplies in GSTR-3B Table 3.1.1(i).
- ECO reports in GSTR-1 Table 15 (supplies through ECO, Section 9(5)).

Impact on actual supplier (restaurant/driver/hotel):
- Not liable to pay GST on these specific supplies.
- Must report turnover in GSTR-1 Table 14 (taxable supplies through ECO liable under Section 9(5)).
- Must report in GSTR-3B Table 3.1.1(ii) — only taxable value, no tax amount.
- These supplies count towards aggregate turnover for registration threshold purposes.

Composition taxpayers: Restaurant services under composition CAN be supplied through ECO (exception introduced via CGST Notification — only for restaurant services).

================================================================================
PART 29: GST DEMAND AND RECOVERY — SECTIONS 73, 74, 74A
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_067]
[TOPIC: Section 73 — Demand Without Fraud (Complete Process)]
[GST_FORM: DRC-01A | DRC-01 | DRC-07]
[SECTION: Section 73 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 142 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice | Assessment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Penalty | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 73 applies to cases of non-payment/short-payment/wrong refund/wrong ITC where there is NO fraud, no wilful misstatement, and no suppression of facts.

Time limit for issuing demand notice under Section 73:
- 3 years from the due date of filing the relevant annual return (e.g., for FY 2022-23, the due date is 31 Dec 2023, so demand can be issued up to 31 Dec 2026).

Process:
Step 1: DRC-01A (Pre-notice intimation): Officer may issue DRC-01A first, giving the taxpayer an opportunity to pay and avoid formal SCN.
Step 2: DRC-01 (Show Cause Notice): Formal SCN issued specifying the demand.
Step 3: Taxpayer response within 30 days (or further time granted by officer).
Step 4: Personal hearing — mandatory if requested by taxpayer.
Step 5: Adjudication order.

Benefit of reduced penalty on timely payment under Section 73:
- If taxpayer pays full tax + interest BEFORE receipt of SCN: No penalty.
- If taxpayer pays full tax + interest WITHIN 30 DAYS of SCN: No penalty (penalty is deemed to have not been levied).
- Budget 2024 amendment: This window is being extended to 60 days (once notified).
- If not paid within time: Penalty up to 10% of tax or Rs. 10,000 — whichever is higher.

---
[CHUNK_068]
[TOPIC: Section 74 — Demand With Fraud and Section 74A — New Common Provision]
[GST_FORM: DRC-01 | DRC-07]
[SECTION: Section 74 | Section 74A CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 142 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice | Assessment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Penalty]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 74 applies to cases involving fraud, wilful misstatement, or suppression of facts with intent to evade tax.

Time limit: 5 years from the due date of filing annual return.

Penalty under Section 74:
- Minimum penalty: 100% of tax demanded (i.e., equal to the full tax amount).
- If taxpayer pays within 30 days of SCN: 25% penalty.
- If taxpayer pays within 30 days of adjudication order: 50% penalty.
- Budget 2024: Window extended to 60 days once Section 74A is notified.

Section 74A — New Common Time Limit (Budget 2024, effective FY 2024-25 onwards):
- Provides a SINGLE common time limit for issuing demand notices for both fraud and non-fraud cases for FY 2024-25 onwards.
- Time limit: 42 months from the due date of filing annual return (for non-fraud cases), 60 months (for fraud cases) — to be confirmed via CBIC notification.
- Until Section 74A is officially notified, Sections 73 and 74 continue to apply separately.

Key practical difference (73 vs 74):
- Section 73: 3-year window, lower penalty, no allegation of intent.
- Section 74: 5-year window, 100% penalty, allegation of fraud/wilful suppression.
- For your AI CA platform: Classification of notice as Section 73 vs 74 is critical for determining response strategy and penalty exposure.

---

================================================================================
PART 30: GST REGISTRATION — SUSPENSION AND SYSTEM BLOCKING
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_069]
[TOPIC: GST Registration Suspension — Automatic and Manual]
[GST_FORM: REG-31]
[SECTION: Section 29 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 21A CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Registration]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/registration/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2019-11-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Automatic system-based suspension:
- Triggered when a normal (non-composition) taxpayer fails to file GSTR-3B for 2 consecutive months (monthly filers) or 1 quarter (quarterly filers).
- On suspension: A notice is issued in Form GST REG-31. The taxpayer cannot make taxable supplies until revived.
- IFF: QRMP taxpayers suspended if they fail to file GSTR-1/IFF for 2 consecutive quarters.

Manual suspension by proper officer:
- Officer can suspend GST registration if there are reasons to cancel registration (e.g., fraudulent registration, non-commencement of business).
- Taxpayer can file reply to suspend-cum-show cause notice.
- During suspension, the taxpayer cannot collect GST on outward supplies.
- Cannot claim ITC during suspension period.

Revocation of suspension:
- Suspension is automatically revoked if the taxpayer files all pending returns and any dues.
- If officer initiated: Revocation requires officer's order.

GSTIN block (separate from suspension):
- Electronic Credit Ledger can be blocked under Rule 86A if the officer has reason to believe ITC was fraudulently availed.
- This blocks outflow from credit ledger, not the registration itself.

---

================================================================================
PART 31: LETTER OF UNDERTAKING (LUT) — FOR EXPORTERS
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_070]
[TOPIC: LUT (Letter of Undertaking) — Form GST RFD-11]
[GST_FORM: RFD-11]
[SECTION: Section 16 IGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 96A CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Exporter]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Refund | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: IGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/refund/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Letter of Undertaking (LUT): A declaration filed by exporters that allows them to export goods or services without paying IGST upfront, with an undertaking to realise export proceeds within the prescribed time.

Applicability:
- Any registered person who is exporting goods or services (zero-rated supplies) can file an LUT.
- Exception: Exporters with a prosecution case under CGST Act or any other fiscal law (pending sentence exceeding 2 years) are NOT eligible and must provide a bond with surety instead.

Filing Form GST RFD-11 (LUT):
- Filed online on the GST Portal: Services → User Services → Furnish Letter of Undertaking (LUT).
- Must be filed before the start of each financial year (before 1st April).
- Once accepted, valid for the entire financial year.
- No bank guarantee or surety required for LUT (only for bond in case of ineligible exporters).

Key undertakings in LUT:
- Export proceeds will be realised within 1 year from the date of export (for goods) or 1 year from the date of invoice (for services) — or within the extended period allowed by RBI.
- IGST will be paid on supplies if export conditions are not fulfilled.

Impact on GSTR-1: Exports under LUT must be reported in GSTR-1 Table 6A with the "Without Payment of IGST" flag. Shipping bill or Bill of Export number must be furnished.

ITC refund with LUT: File Form GST RFD-01 on the portal within 2 years of the export invoice date to claim refund of accumulated ITC.

---

================================================================================
PART 32: RETURN FILING SEQUENCE — STEP BY STEP (PRACTICAL WORKFLOW)
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_071]
[TOPIC: Monthly Compliance Workflow for a Normal Taxpayer — Complete Sequence]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-2B | GSTR-3B | PMT-06]
[SECTION: Section 37 | Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 59 | Rule 61 | Rule 36(4) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

The correct monthly compliance sequence for a normal (regular) taxpayer:

STEP 1 — Before 11th of the month:
- Compile all sales invoices for the previous month.
- Generate IRN for all eligible invoices (if e-invoicing applicable).
- File GSTR-1 (declare all outward supplies: B2B, B2C, exports, CDNs, advances, HSN summary).
- Filing GSTR-1 is a PREREQUISITE for filing GSTR-3B.

STEP 2 — After 14th of the month (GSTR-2B generation):
- Download GSTR-2B for the previous month (generated on 14th based on suppliers' GSTR-1 filings).
- Reconcile GSTR-2B with your purchase register.
- Identify matched ITC, unmatched ITC, and ineligible ITC (Section 17(5)).
- Follow up with suppliers whose invoices are missing from GSTR-2B.

STEP 3 — Before 20th of the month (GSTR-3B filing):
- Verify auto-populated GSTR-3B Tables 3.1 and 4A against your records.
- Edit if necessary (RED warnings will appear for downward edits in 3.1; upward edits in 4A).
- Fill in Table 3.2 (inter-state breakup), Table 5 (exempt/nil inward supplies), and Table 5.1 (interest/late fee if applicable).
- Offset liability using ITC (Credit Ledger). Any shortfall: generate PMT-06 challan and pay.
- File GSTR-3B using DSC (for Companies/LLPs) or EVC (for others).

STEP 4 — Monitor DRC-01B notices:
- Check for any DRC-01B intimations (GSTR-1 vs GSTR-3B mismatch alerts) and respond within 30 days.

STEP 5 — Before 31st December (Annual):
- Reconcile all 12 months of GSTR-1 and GSTR-3B.
- File GSTR-9 (if turnover > Rs. 2 crore).
- File GSTR-9C (if turnover > Rs. 5 crore).

---
[CHUNK_072]
[TOPIC: Quarterly Compliance Workflow for QRMP Taxpayers — Sequence]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B | CMP-08 | PMT-06]
[SECTION: Section 37 | Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 59 | Rule 61 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Quarterly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2020-10-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Monthly and quarterly compliance sequence for QRMP taxpayers (turnover ≤ Rs. 5 crore):

Month 1 and Month 2 of quarter (e.g., April, May for Q1):
- By 13th: File IFF (Invoice Furnishing Facility) — optional, for B2B invoices only. Allows recipient to get ITC without waiting for quarterly GSTR-1.
- By 25th: Pay monthly tax via PMT-06 challan using either:
  - Fixed Sum Method (FSM): 35% of prior quarter's cash tax payment.
  - Self-Assessment Method (SAM): Compute and pay actual liability.

Month 3 of quarter (e.g., June for Q1):
- By 13th: File GSTR-1 for the full quarter (all B2B, B2C, exports, CDNs, HSN).
- By 22nd (Cat-1 states) or 24th (Cat-2 states): File GSTR-3B for the quarter.

Annual:
- By 31st December: File GSTR-9 (if turnover > Rs. 2 crore).
- By 31st December: File GSTR-9C (if turnover > Rs. 5 crore).

QRMP state categories for GSTR-3B due dates:
- Category 1 (22nd): Chhattisgarh, Madhya Pradesh, Gujarat, Maharashtra, Karnataka, Goa, Kerala, Tamil Nadu, Telangana, Andhra Pradesh, Daman & Diu, Puducherry, Dadra & Nagar Haveli, Lakshadweep, Andaman & Nicobar.
- Category 2 (24th): Himachal Pradesh, Punjab, Uttarakhand, Haryana, Rajasthan, Uttar Pradesh, Bihar, Sikkim, Arunachal Pradesh, Nagaland, Manipur, Mizoram, Tripura, Meghalaya, Assam, West Bengal, Jharkhand, Odisha, Jammu & Kashmir, Ladakh, Chandigarh, Delhi.

================================================================================
PART 33: SYSTEM-GENERATED NOTICES — AUTO-TRIGGER RULES
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_073]
[TOPIC: System-Triggered GST Notices — What Triggers What]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3A | DRC-01B | REG-31]
[SECTION: Section 39 | Section 29 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 88C | Rule 21A CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Error_resolution]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

The GST system auto-generates the following notices without manual officer intervention:

1. FORM GSTR-3A (Return Defaulter Notice):
   Trigger: GSTR-1 not filed by due date.
   Content: Reminder to file GSTR-1 within 15 days.

2. FORM GSTR-3B Defaulter Notice:
   Trigger: GSTR-3B not filed for 2 consecutive months (monthly filers) or 1 quarter (QRMP).
   Action: Auto-suspension of GSTIN after notice in REG-31.

3. FORM GST DRC-01B (Liability Difference Intimation):
   Trigger: Tax liability in GSTR-1 > tax declared + paid in GSTR-3B for the same period, beyond a threshold.
   Governed by: Rule 88C of CGST Rules.
   Taxpayer must reply within 30 days — Accept (pay via DRC-03) or Explain.

4. ITC Auto-Reversal via GSTR-2B (Rule 37A):
   Trigger: Supplier has not filed GSTR-3B for the period by 30th September of following FY.
   Action: ITC of recipient auto-reversed in GSTR-2B ITC Reversal tab. Reflected in GSTR-3B pre-fill.

5. HSN Mismatch Warning in GSTR-1:
   Trigger: HSN declared in GSTR-1 for an invoice does not match the registered HSN in GSTIN master data.
   Action: Validation error/warning during GSTR-1 filing.

6. GSTIN Validation Failure in GSTR-1:
   Trigger: Recipient GSTIN in B2B invoice was not active on the date of invoice.
   Action: System throws error; invoice cannot be saved until corrected.

7. E-Invoice Rejection at IRP:
   Trigger: Duplicate IRN, invalid GSTIN, or (from April 2025) invoice date older than 30 days at time of upload (for AATO ≥ Rs. 10 crore).
   Action: IRP rejects the e-invoice upload; no IRN generated.

---

================================================================================
PART 34: GST LEDGER MANAGEMENT AND UTILISATION RULES
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_074]
[TOPIC: ITC Utilisation Sequence — Order of Offset under Section 49]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 49 | Section 49A | Section 49B CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 88 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Payment | ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2019-02-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

ITC utilisation sequence (as per Section 49A and 49B):

The order of ITC utilisation as per amended Section 49A (mandatory sequence):

1. IGST ITC → First exhaust IGST liability.
   Remaining IGST ITC → Can be used to pay CGST (no limit).
   Remaining IGST ITC → Can be used to pay SGST/UTGST (no limit).

2. CGST ITC → First exhaust CGST liability.
   Remaining CGST ITC → CANNOT offset SGST.

3. SGST/UTGST ITC → First exhaust SGST/UTGST liability.
   Remaining SGST/UTGST ITC → CANNOT offset CGST.

Key rules:
- CGST and SGST cannot be cross-utilised. IGST is the "universal donor" that can offset any head.
- Cess ITC can only offset Cess liability.
- ITC cannot be used to pay interest, penalty, or late fees. These must be paid in cash via Electronic Cash Ledger.
- If Electronic Credit Ledger has CGST balance and SGST liability exists (or vice versa), the taxpayer MUST generate a PMT-06 challan and pay in cash. Cannot use CGST to pay SGST.

Rule 88: ITC cannot be used until it is "available" in the Electronic Credit Ledger. ITC is "available" when the supplier has filed GSTR-1 and the invoice appears in GSTR-2B.

---
[CHUNK_075]
[TOPIC: Electronic Liability Ledger and Offset Process in GSTR-3B]
[GST_FORM: PMT-01 | PMT-06 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 49 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 85 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Payment | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/payments/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

The Electronic Liability Ledger (Form GST PMT-01) accumulates all outstanding GST dues of the taxpayer. It is updated when:
- GSTR-3B is filed (tax declared becomes a liability).
- Demand orders are passed.
- Interest and late fee become due.

Offset process inside GSTR-3B (Table 6):
1. System auto-fills tax payable based on Tables 3.1 and 4.
2. Taxpayer clicks "OFFSET LIABILITY."
3. System automatically applies available ITC (following Section 49A/49B sequence):
   - IGST ITC first against IGST → then CGST → then SGST.
   - CGST ITC against CGST only.
   - SGST ITC against SGST only.
4. Remaining liability (after ITC offset) shows as cash payable.
5. If no cash in Electronic Cash Ledger: Taxpayer must generate PMT-06, pay, wait for reflection, then return to GSTR-3B to complete offset.
6. After full offset: Proceed to file.

================================================================================
PART 35: PENALTIES AND OFFENCES — QUICK REFERENCE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_076]
[TOPIC: GST Penalties — Section 122 and Other Key Provisions]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: Section 122 | Section 123 | Section 125 | Section 126 | Section 132 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Penalty]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 122 — Penalty for specific offences:
Rs. 10,000 or the tax evaded — whichever is HIGHER — for:
- Supply without invoice or with false invoice.
- Issue of invoice without supply (fake invoice).
- Collecting tax but not depositing it.
- Taking ITC without actual supply.
- Taking ITC using fake invoices.
- Obstructing tax officer.
- Destruction of evidence.

Section 123 — Penalty for failure to furnish information return:
Rs. 100 per day, maximum Rs. 10,000.

Section 125 — General penalty:
Up to Rs. 25,000 for any GST Act contravention not specifically covered elsewhere. Covers wrong HSN, missing mandatory invoice fields, etc.

Section 126 — Penalty not to be imposed in certain cases (exceptions):
Penalty not imposable if:
- The error is minor and easily rectifiable.
- The taxpayer has reasonable cause for the breach.
- The breach was not willful.

Section 132 — Prosecution (Criminal):
Criminal prosecution applicable for:
- Tax evasion above Rs. 5 crore involving fraud (up to 5 years imprisonment).
- Issuance of fake invoices (up to 5 years imprisonment).
- Repeat offences (more than 2 years imprisonment in some cases).

[CHUNK_077]
[TOPIC: Monthly GST Compliance Checklist for CA/CS Professionals]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-2B | GSTR-3B | PMT-06]
[SECTION: Section 37 | Section 39 | Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 59 | Rule 61 | Rule 36(4) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly | Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

MONTHLY CHECKLIST (for each client GSTIN):

PRE-FILING (1st–10th):
□ Collect all sales invoices, credit notes, debit notes from client.
□ Verify IRN generation for all eligible invoices (e-invoice threshold check).
□ Confirm all inter-state supplies have correct IGST (not CGST+SGST).
□ Verify GSTIN of all B2B recipients was active on invoice date.
□ Check LUT is active for exporters (file RFD-11 if new FY started).
□ Reconcile GST rate on each invoice with HSN/SAC code.

GSTR-1 FILING (by 11th/13th):
□ Upload all B2B invoices (Table 4) with correct GSTIN, HSN, POS.
□ Report B2C large invoices (Table 5) for inter-state > Rs. 2.5 lakh.
□ Report exports in Table 6A/6B with shipping bill numbers where available.
□ Report all credit notes and debit notes (Table 9A/9B/9C).
□ Submit HSN-wise summary (Table 12) — B2B and B2C separately from May 2025.
□ File using DSC (company) or EVC (others). Save ARN.

POST GSTR-1 / PRE GSTR-3B (14th–19th):
□ Wait for GSTR-2B to generate (after 14th).
□ Download GSTR-2B and reconcile with purchase register.
□ Identify ITC to claim: matched invoices from GSTR-2B only.
□ Exclude Section 17(5) blocked credits.
□ Check GSTR-2B ITC Reversal tab for Rule 37A reversals.
□ Check IMS dashboard for any rejected/pending invoices.
□ Compute RCM liability on all RCM services (Section 9(3) and 9(4)).

GSTR-3B FILING (by 20th/22nd/24th):
□ Verify auto-populated values in Tables 3.1 and 4A against manual calculation.
□ Enter RCM liability in Table 3.1(d).
□ Enter ITC reversals (Table 4B) for: 180-day non-payment, Rule 37A, Section 17(5) corrections.
□ Fill Table 5 (exempt/nil inward supplies summary).
□ Enter any interest/late fee in Table 5.1.
□ Offset liability using ITC then cash. Generate PMT-06 if needed.
□ File and save ARN.
□ Check for DRC-01B notices after filing and respond within 30 days.

QUARTERLY (for GSTR-9 preparation):
□ Maintain running reconciliation register (GSTR-1 vs GSTR-3B vs books).
□ Track all ITC reversals and reclaims (Rule 42/43 annual adjustments).
□ Maintain vendor non-compliance register (suppliers repeatedly missing from GSTR-2B).
□ Track debit notes issued/received across financial years.

ANNUAL:
□ File GSTR-9 (mandatory if turnover > Rs. 2 crore) by 31st December.
□ File GSTR-9C (mandatory if turnover > Rs. 5 crore) by 31st December.
□ File GSTR-4 by 30th June (composition taxpayers).
□ Renew LUT (Form GST RFD-11) at start of new financial year.
□ Check opt-in/opt-out of QRMP scheme for next year (by 31st January).

[CHUNK_079]
[TOPIC: Important GST Thresholds — Master Reference Table]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: Multiple]
[RULE: Multiple]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | IGST_Act | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | Rate_lookup]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

REGISTRATION THRESHOLDS:
- Goods (general states): Rs. 40 lakh aggregate turnover
- Goods (special category states): Rs. 20 lakh
- Services (general): Rs. 20 lakh
- Services (special category): Rs. 10 lakh
- Mandatory registration regardless of turnover: Inter-state supply, e-commerce sellers, RCM payers, TDS/TCS registrants

COMPOSITION SCHEME:
- Goods (manufacturer/trader): Rs. 1.5 crore (Rs. 75 lakh for NE/hill states)
- Services (special composition): Rs. 50 lakh
- Composition opt-out if turnover exceeds the above in current FY

QRMP SCHEME:
- Eligible if AATO ≤ Rs. 5 crore (preceding FY)

GSTR-9 FILING:
- Mandatory: AATO > Rs. 2 crore (permanent exemption below Rs. 2 crore via N/N 15/2025-CT)

GSTR-9C FILING:
- Mandatory: AATO > Rs. 5 crore

E-INVOICING:
- Mandatory: AATO > Rs. 5 crore (since 1 Aug 2023)
- 30-day IRP upload deadline: AATO ≥ Rs. 10 crore (from 1 Apr 2025)

HSN CODE DIGITS:
- Up to Rs. 1.5 crore: Exempt from HSN
- Rs. 1.5 crore–Rs. 5 crore: 4-digit HSN (B2B mandatory, B2C optional)
- Above Rs. 5 crore: 6-digit HSN (all supplies)
- Exports: 8-digit HSN always

ITC TIME LIMIT:
- Claim ITC by 30th November of following FY or date of GSTR-9 filing — whichever earlier

REFUND TIME LIMIT:
- File RFD-01 within 2 years from the relevant date

DEMAND TIME LIMITS:
- Section 73 (non-fraud): 3 years from due date of annual return
- Section 74 (fraud): 5 years from due date of annual return

CREDIT NOTE TIME LIMIT:
- Issue by 30th November of following FY or before annual return — whichever earlier

[CHUNK_080]
[TOPIC: Glossary — Key GST Terms for RAG Context Window]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: NA]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

ARN: Application Reference Number — generated on successful filing of any GST return or application.
AATO: Aggregate Annual Turnover — PAN-level total of all supplies including taxable, exempt, exports; excludes GST and RCM inward supplies.
B2B: Business-to-Business supply — supply to a registered person.
B2C: Business-to-Consumer supply — supply to an unregistered person.
CPIN: Challan Portal Identification Number — 14-digit number generated when PMT-06 challan is created. Valid 15 days.
CIN: Challan Identification Number — issued by bank on successful payment against a CPIN.
CDN: Credit/Debit Note.
DSC: Digital Signature Certificate — PAN-based, mandatory for Companies and LLPs to sign GST returns.
ECL: Electronic Cash Ledger (Form PMT-05) — records cash deposits for tax payment.
ECrL: Electronic Credit Ledger (Form PMT-02) — records available ITC.
ELL: Electronic Liability Ledger (Form PMT-01) — records outstanding tax dues.
EVC: Electronic Verification Code — OTP-based signing for non-company taxpayers.
GSTIN: 15-digit GST Identification Number assigned to each registered taxpayer.
IFF: Invoice Furnishing Facility — optional B2B invoice upload by QRMP taxpayers in M1 and M2 of quarter.
IMS: Invoice Management System — portal feature allowing recipients to accept/reject supplier invoices.
IRP: Invoice Registration Portal — portal for generating IRN for e-invoices.
IRN: Invoice Reference Number — 64-character unique hash generated by IRP for each e-invoice.
ISD: Input Service Distributor — entity that receives services and distributes ITC to branches.
ITC: Input Tax Credit — credit for GST paid on purchases, offsettable against output tax liability.
LUT: Letter of Undertaking — declaration by exporter to export without IGST payment.
NRTP: Non-Resident Taxable Person — foreign entity temporarily supplying goods/services in India.
OIDAR: Online Information Database Access or Retrieval — services delivered over the internet.
PAN: Permanent Account Number — basis for GSTIN and PAN-level turnover computation.
POS: Place of Supply — determines whether a transaction is intra-state (CGST+SGST) or inter-state (IGST).
QRMP: Quarterly Return Monthly Payment scheme — for taxpayers with AATO ≤ Rs. 5 crore.
RCM: Reverse Charge Mechanism — liability shifts from supplier to recipient.
SCN: Show Cause Notice — formal demand notice under Section 73 or 74.
SEZ: Special Economic Zone — zero-rated supply destination; supplies to SEZ are treated as exports.
TCS: Tax Collected at Source (under GST) — collected by e-commerce operators at 0.5% from July 2024.
TDS: Tax Deducted at Source (under GST) — deducted by specified government entities at 2%.
UIN: Unique Identification Number — issued to foreign diplomatic missions and UN bodies.
UQC: Unique Quantity Code — unit of measurement mandatory on GST invoices and HSN summaries.
