================================================================================
PART 37: TIME OF SUPPLY — SECTIONS 12, 13, 14
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_081]
[TOPIC: Time of Supply of GOODS — Section 12 CGST Act]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 12 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 082, 058, 059]

Time of Supply is the point at which GST liability crystallises — i.e., when the taxpayer becomes liable to pay tax. Section 12 governs this for GOODS.

General rule — Forward Charge (Section 12(2)):
Time of supply = EARLIEST of:
(a) Date of issue of invoice by the supplier, OR the last date by which invoice was required to be issued under Section 31(1), whichever is earlier.
(b) Date on which the supplier receives payment.

"Date of receipt of payment" = Earlier of:
- Date on which payment is entered in supplier's books of account.
- Date on which payment is credited to supplier's bank account.

Example: If goods are dispatched on 5th June, invoice issued on 7th June, and payment received on 20th June → Time of Supply = 7th June (date of invoice, which is earlier than payment).

Reverse Charge (Section 12(3)):
Time of supply = EARLIEST of:
(a) Date of receipt of goods by recipient.
(b) Date of payment by recipient.
(c) Date immediately following 30 days from date of invoice by supplier.

Vouchers (Section 12(4)):
- If supply is identifiable at the time of issue of voucher: Date of issue of voucher.
- If not identifiable: Date of redemption of voucher.

Residual clause (Section 12(5)):
If none of the above determines the time: Date on which periodical return is to be filed, or date of payment of tax — whichever is earlier.

Additional value — Interest/late fee/penalty (Section 12(6)):
Time of supply for any addition to value by way of interest, late fee, or penalty for delayed payment = Date on which the supplier receives such additional amount.

---
[CHUNK_082]
[TOPIC: Time of Supply of SERVICES — Section 13 CGST Act]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 13 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 081, 058, 059]

Section 13 governs time of supply for SERVICES.

General rule — Forward Charge (Section 13(2)):
Time of supply = EARLIEST of:
(a) Date of invoice (if issued within prescribed period under Section 31).
(b) Date of receipt of payment.
(c) Date of provision of service (if invoice NOT issued within prescribed period).

Exception: For advance up to Rs. 1,000 in excess of invoice amount — the supplier has the OPTION to treat the time of supply as the date of the invoice (not date of advance receipt).

Reverse Charge (Section 13(3)):
Time of supply = EARLIEST of:
(a) Date of payment by recipient (entered in books or credited to bank — whichever earlier).
(b) 61st day from date of invoice by supplier.

Exception for associated enterprises: If supplier is outside India, time of supply = date of entry of service in books of account of recipient OR date of payment — whichever earlier.

Vouchers for services (Section 13(4)):
- Supply identifiable at issue of voucher: Date of issue.
- Not identifiable: Date of redemption.

Residual clause (Section 13(5)):
Date of periodical return or date of payment of tax — whichever earlier.

Additional value — Interest/late fee/penalty (Section 13(6)):
Same as goods — date on which the supplier receives the additional amount.

---
[CHUNK_083]
[TOPIC: Time of Supply — Change in Tax Rate (Section 14)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 14 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Rates]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Rate_lookup]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 081, 082]

Section 14 governs the time of supply when there is a change in the rate of GST.

For GOODS or SERVICES supplied BEFORE the change in rate:
- If invoice issued AND payment received AFTER change: Time of supply = Date of invoice OR payment — whichever is EARLIER.
- If invoice issued BEFORE change but payment AFTER: Time of supply = Date of invoice (old rate applies).
- If payment received BEFORE change but invoice AFTER: Time of supply = Date of payment (old rate applies).

For GOODS or SERVICES supplied AFTER the change in rate:
- If invoice issued AND payment received BEFORE change: Time of supply = Date of invoice OR payment — whichever is EARLIER.
- If invoice issued AFTER change but payment BEFORE: Time of supply = Date of invoice (new rate applies).
- If payment received AFTER change but invoice BEFORE: Time of supply = Date of payment (new rate applies).

Practical rule of thumb: The rate applicable is the rate on the date of supply as determined by Section 12/13. Section 14 specifically handles the transition period where invoice and payment straddle the change date.

---

================================================================================
PART 38: VALUATION OF SUPPLY — SECTION 15 AND RULES 27–35
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_084]
[TOPIC: GST Valuation — Section 15 Transaction Value and Inclusions]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 15 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 085, 086]

Section 15 of the CGST Act determines the VALUE on which GST is calculated.

Primary rule — Transaction Value (Section 15(1)):
The value of a supply = transaction value = the price actually paid or payable for the supply.
Applicable ONLY when:
- Supplier and recipient are NOT related parties.
- Price is the SOLE consideration for the supply.

Mandatory INCLUSIONS in transaction value (Section 15(2)):
The following MUST be added to arrive at taxable value:
(a) Any taxes, duties, cesses, fees charged under any other statute (not GST itself), if charged separately by supplier.
(b) Any amount the supplier is liable to pay but has been paid by the recipient (e.g., freight paid by buyer on behalf of seller).
(c) Incidental expenses: Commission, packing, loading, any amount charged before or at delivery.
(d) Interest, late fee, or penalty for delayed payment of consideration — included in taxable value when received.
(e) Subsidies directly linked to price — if subsidy received from non-government entity linked to the transaction price.

EXCLUSIONS from transaction value (Section 15(3)):
Discounts are EXCLUDED from taxable value if:
(a) Pre-supply discount: Established before or at the time of supply, recorded on the invoice.
(b) Post-supply discount: Established by agreement before supply, specifically linked to the invoice, and ITC has been reversed by recipient on the discounted amount.

Year-end trade discounts WITHOUT pre-agreement are NOT deductible — this has been upheld in adjudications. The agreement must pre-exist the supply.

---
[CHUNK_085]
[TOPIC: GST Valuation — Related Party Transactions and Valuation Rules 27–35]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 15(4) | Section 15(5) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 27 | Rule 28 | Rule 29 | Rule 30 | Rule 31 | Rule 32 | Rule 35 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 084, 086]

When transaction value CANNOT be used (Section 15(4)):
If supplier and recipient are related parties, or price is not the sole consideration, the value must be determined using CGST Rules Chapter IV (Rules 27–35).

Definition of "related persons" (Explanation to Section 15):
Persons are related if:
- One directly/indirectly owns, controls, or holds 25% or more of outstanding voting stock/shares of both.
- One directly/indirectly controls the other.
- A third person controls both.
- Together they control a third person.
- They are employer and employee.
- Any person directly/indirectly owns, controls, holds 25%+ of both.
- One of them is the sole agent, sole distributor, or sole concessionaire of the other.

Valuation Rules cascade (apply in order):
Rule 27: Open Market Value — the full value in money a buyer would pay for the same supply at the same time, excluding GST, between unrelated parties.
Rule 28: Value of supply between distinct or related persons — Open market value; if not available, 90% of price charged to unrelated customers; if not available, cost-based (Rule 30) or residual (Rule 31).
Rule 29: Pure agent exclusion — expenses incurred by supplier as pure agent of recipient are excluded from taxable value, subject to conditions.
Rule 30: Cost-based method — 110% of the cost of production/acquisition/provision.
Rule 31: Residual method — using reasonable means consistent with the principles and general provisions of Section 15 and the above Rules.
Rule 32: Special valuation for money changers, tour operators, second-hand goods dealers, token/voucher suppliers.
Rule 35: Tax exclusive value — where tax is included in the price, taxable value = price × 100 ÷ (100 + tax rate).

---
[CHUNK_086]
[TOPIC: GST Valuation — Practical Scenarios and Common Issues]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 15 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 29 | Rule 35 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 084, 085]

Common valuation issues in practice:

Free Supplies / Samples:
- If made to unrelated persons without consideration: Outside the ambit of supply (Section 7); no GST.
- If made to related persons / distinct persons: Treated as supply even without consideration (Schedule I, Section 7(1)(c)). Must be valued at open market value or under Rule 28.

Bundled Supplies (Composite and Mixed):
- Composite supply: Two or more supplies naturally bundled where one is principal supply. GST rate of principal supply applies to entire composite supply.
- Mixed supply: Two or more supplies not naturally bundled, made for single price. GST rate of the highest-rated supply applies to the entire mixed supply.

Inclusion of freight in invoice value:
When supplier charges freight separately on the invoice, it is included in the taxable value of the supply (incidental expense under Section 15(2)(c)). GST applies on the freight amount at the same rate as the goods.

Reimbursements:
If the supplier incurs expenses on behalf of the recipient and recovers them, they form part of the taxable value — UNLESS the pure agent conditions under Rule 29 are satisfied (strict conditions: supplier acts on behalf of recipient, does not add value, records expense separately, and is authorised by recipient).

Interest on delayed payment:
Interest charged on buyers for delayed payment is included in the taxable value at the time it is received (Section 15(2)(d) read with Section 12(6)/13(6)).

---

================================================================================
PART 39: SUPPLY CLASSIFICATION — ZERO-RATED, NIL-RATED, EXEMPT, NON-GST
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_087]
[TOPIC: Four Supply Categories — Zero-Rated, Nil-Rated, Exempt, Non-GST — Definitions and Differences]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 2(47) | Section 11 CGST Act | Section 16 IGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | IGST_Act | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Rate_lookup | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 088, 022, 038]

These four categories are critically distinct in law. Misclassification is one of the top triggers for GST notices and ITC reversal demands.

ZERO-RATED SUPPLY (IGST Act Section 16):
Definition: Exports of goods/services AND supplies to SEZ units/developers.
GST rate: 0% output tax.
ITC: FULLY ELIGIBLE and REFUNDABLE.
Key rule: Supplier can either (a) pay IGST and claim refund, or (b) export under LUT without IGST and claim ITC refund via RFD-01.
Reporting: GSTR-1 Table 6A/6B; GSTR-3B Table 3.1(b).

NIL-RATED SUPPLY:
Definition: Supplies where the GST rate in the rate schedule is 0%. Listed in Schedule I of CGST/IGST Rate Notification.
GST rate: 0% (by rate schedule, not by exemption notification).
ITC: NOT AVAILABLE on inputs used for nil-rated supplies.
Examples: Unbranded rice, wheat, fresh vegetables, fresh milk, eggs, curd, natural honey, human blood, contraceptives.
Reporting: GSTR-1 Table 8; GSTR-3B Table 3.1(c).

EXEMPT SUPPLY (CGST Act Section 2(47)):
Definition: Supplies specifically exempted from GST by government notification under Section 11 of CGST Act or Section 6 of IGST Act. Includes nil-rated and non-taxable supplies within its broader definition for ITC reversal purposes.
GST rate: No GST charged.
ITC: NOT AVAILABLE on inputs/input services used for exempt supplies. Rule 42/43 reversal applies for common inputs.
Examples: Healthcare services, educational services (up to secondary level), hotel accommodation below threshold, public transport.
Reporting: GSTR-1 Table 8; GSTR-3B Table 3.1(c).

NON-GST SUPPLY:
Definition: Supplies that fall entirely outside the scope of GST legislation. Not taxable under GST but may be taxed under other laws.
Examples: Alcohol for human consumption (taxed by states), petroleum crude, high-speed diesel, motor spirit, natural gas, aviation turbine fuel (taxed under old regime pending GST Council inclusion), electricity.
ITC: NOT AVAILABLE.
Reporting: GSTR-1 Table 8 (non-GST outward supplies); GSTR-3B Table 3.1(e).

---
[CHUNK_088]
[TOPIC: ITC Reversal Obligation — Exempt, Nil-Rated, and Non-GST Supplies]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 17(2) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 42 | Rule 43 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 087, 022, 023]

Section 17(2): ITC is NOT available on inputs/input services used exclusively for making exempt supplies (including nil-rated and non-taxable supplies).

For businesses making BOTH taxable and exempt supplies (mixed suppliers):
ITC on inputs/services exclusively for taxable supplies: Fully available.
ITC on inputs/services exclusively for exempt supplies: Not available — reverse in full.
ITC on COMMON inputs/services (used for both): Must be apportioned under Rule 42.

Rule 42 — Common credit apportionment (inputs and input services):
Ineligible common credit = Total common ITC × (Exempt turnover ÷ Total turnover)
This amount must be reversed every month on a provisional basis, with an annual adjustment in the September GSTR-3B of the following FY.

Aggregate turnover for ITC purposes:
- Exempt turnover INCLUDES: nil-rated supplies, exempt supplies, non-taxable supplies.
- Total turnover INCLUDES: all taxable supplies + exempt supplies + exports + nil-rated.
- Total turnover EXCLUDES: supplies on which RCM is paid by recipient.

For the purpose of REGISTRATION threshold calculation:
- Aggregate turnover INCLUDES exempt and nil-rated supplies.
- Non-GST supplies (petroleum, alcohol) are EXCLUDED from aggregate turnover for registration threshold.

Common mistake: Many businesses include non-GST supplies in their ITC reversal calculation under Rule 42, leading to over-reversal. Non-GST supplies are separately reported in GSTR-3B Table 3.1(e) but not factored into Rule 42 calculation unless the CBIC notification specifically includes them.

---

PART 40: APPEALS AND DISPUTE RESOLUTION
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_089]
[TOPIC: GST Appeals — Four-Tier Structure and Forms]
[GST_FORM: APL-01 | APL-03 | APL-04 | APL-05]
[SECTION: Section 107 | Section 109 | Section 112 | Section 117 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 108 | Rule 110 | Rule 111 | Rule 113 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Appeal]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date | Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 090, 091, 035]

GST has a four-tier appellate structure:

Tier 1 — First Appellate Authority (FAA):
Who: Commissioner (Appeals) of Central Tax or State Tax.
Governed by: Section 107 of CGST Act.
Appeal form: FORM GST APL-01 (by taxpayer) or FORM GST APL-03 (by department).
Time limit: 3 months from date of communication of the order (extendable by a further 1 month at FAA's discretion).
Pre-deposit required: Full admitted liability + 10% of disputed tax (maximum Rs. 20 crore CGST + Rs. 20 crore SGST per 53rd GST Council recommendation, June 2024).
Order by FAA: Issued in FORM GST APL-04 with summary of final demand confirmed.
Withdrawal of appeal: Allowed via FORM GST APL-01/03W before SCN under Section 107(11) is issued. If final acknowledgement (APL-02) is issued, FAA approval needed.

Tier 2 — GST Appellate Tribunal (GSTAT):
Who: Goods and Services Tax Appellate Tribunal.
Status: Became operational in 2025 (GSTAT Procedure Rules 2025 notified 24 April 2025 via G.S.R. 256(E)).
Appeal form: FORM GST APL-05.
Time limit: 3 months from date of FAA order (from a date notified by government). Staggered filing lifted by Order No. 315/2025 dated 16 December 2025 — all appeals can now be filed without restriction. Universal deadline for backlog cases: 30 June 2026.
Pre-deposit: 10% of disputed tax (reduced from 20%) capped at Rs. 20 crore each CGST/SGST (per 53rd GST Council, June 2024).
Department monetary limit for GSTAT: Rs. 20 lakh (department will not appeal below this amount).

Tier 3 — High Court:
Section 117. Substantial question of law only.
Department monetary limit: Rs. 1 crore.

Tier 4 — Supreme Court:
Section 118. Exceptional cases of national significance.
Department monetary limit: Rs. 2 crore.

---
[CHUNK_090]
[TOPIC: GST APL-01 — Detailed Filing Procedure (First Appellate Authority)]
[GST_FORM: APL-01 | APL-02]
[SECTION: Section 107 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 108 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Appeal]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 089, 091]

Steps to file FORM GST APL-01 (appeal against adjudication order):

1. Login to GST Portal → Services → User Services → My Applications → Appeal to Appellate Authority.
2. Select the order being challenged. Enter Order Number, Order Date, and Order type.
3. Complete all tabs:
   - Order details.
   - Grounds of appeal (state clearly each ground — factual and legal).
   - Relief sought (specific reduction/set aside of demand).
   - Documents: Upload certified copy of order being appealed, supporting evidence (PDF, max 5 MB each).
4. Statement of Facts and Grounds: Must be specific. Vague grounds lead to rejection.
5. Pre-deposit payment: Pay admitted tax and 10% of disputed demand via PMT-06 challan. Quote CRN of payment in APL-01.
6. Submit using DSC or EVC. Provisional acknowledgement generated immediately.
7. Final acknowledgement in FORM GST APL-02 issued by FAA on admission of appeal.

Common reasons for rejection:
- Filed beyond time limit without sufficient cause.
- Pre-deposit not paid or short-paid.
- Order being appealed is not an "appealable order" (purely procedural orders cannot be appealed under Section 107).
- Grounds too vague.

After filing APL-01: If FAA does not decide within 1 year of filing, the appeal is deemed to be allowed (Section 107(14) — benefit of deemed allowance). However, the department can contest this deemed allowance in a higher forum.

---
[CHUNK_091]
[TOPIC: GST DRC-03 — Voluntary Payment and Post-Assessment Use]
[GST_FORM: DRC-03]
[SECTION: Section 73 | Section 74 | Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 142 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice | Payment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/payments/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 035, 067, 068, 089]

Form GST DRC-03 is used for voluntary payment of tax, interest, or penalty — outside the regular GSTR-3B payment process.

When to use DRC-03:
1. Voluntary payment BEFORE receiving SCN: To pre-emptively pay shortfall and avoid penalty under Section 73.
2. Payment in response to SCN within 30/60 days: To avail reduced penalty benefit.
3. Payment of any additional liability discovered during reconciliation (GSTR-9 shortfall).
4. Payment in response to ASMT-10 (scrutiny notice) where discrepancy is accepted.
5. DRC-01B response: When accepting GSTR-1 vs GSTR-3B mismatch and choosing to pay.
6. Post-audit payment: After departmental audit under Section 65.
7. Section 128A payments: Tax-only payment for FY 2017-18 to 2019-20 demands to avail interest/penalty waiver.

From FY 2024-25 (Notification 13/2025-CT): Additional tax identified in GSTR-9 can now be paid using AVAILABLE ITC via DRC-03 (previously only cash was allowed).

DRC-03 filing process:
1. GST Portal → Services → User Services → Intimation of Voluntary Payment — DRC-03.
2. Select cause of payment (SCN reference, ASMT-10 reference, self-ascertained, etc.).
3. Enter IGST/CGST/SGST/Cess amounts and applicable interest.
4. Offset using Electronic Credit Ledger (ITC) where allowed, then Electronic Cash Ledger.
5. File. ARN generated.

Important: DRC-03 payments are final — they cannot be reversed. If excess is paid, refund must be claimed via RFD-01. Always verify the demand amounts before filing DRC-03.

================================================================================
PART 41: GST ANNUAL RETURN — COMMON MISTAKES AND COMPLIANCE PITFALLS
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_092]
[TOPIC: GSTR-9 — Top 10 Mistakes That Attract Scrutiny]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-9 | GSTR-9C]
[SECTION: Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 80 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Reconciliation]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Instruction | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/Manual_gstr9.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reconciliation | Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 040, 041, 064, 065]

1. Table 8D showing large unexplained ITC gap:
Table 8D = ITC available in GSTR-2B (Table 8A) minus ITC claimed (Table 6B+8C). Large positive Table 8D means ITC was available but not claimed. Tax officers treat this as a sign of either understated outward supplies or over-reported ITC by suppliers. Investigate every item in Table 8D before filing.

2. Outward supply turnover mismatch with financial statements:
GSTR-9 Table 4/5 must reconcile with the audited P&L. Differences arise from: GST on advances not yet invoiced, supplies under RCM not counted, inter-branch stock transfers counted as turnover in books but not in GST. Document every difference before filing.

3. Not reporting prior-year invoices in Tables 10/11:
If you reported FY 2024-25 invoices in April–November 2025 GSTR-1 filings (next year's returns), those must be reported in GSTR-9 Tables 10/11 so the annual reconciliation is complete. Omitting these creates a mismatch between Table 4 (annual outward) and what was actually reported.

4. ITC reversal under Rule 42/43 not annualised:
Monthly Rule 42 reversals in GSTR-3B are provisional. A final annual computation is required in the September return of the following FY. If the annual computation reveals a shortfall in reversals, the additional reversal must be reported in GSTR-9.

5. GSTR-9 turnover lower than GSTR-1 aggregate:
GSTR-9 Table 4 must be ≥ aggregate of GSTR-1 Tables 4+5+6+7+9 (net of CDNs) for the year. If GSTR-9 is lower, it signals that declared outward supply liability in monthly returns has been reduced in the annual return — a major red flag for tax officers.

6. Missing HSN summary (Table 17):
Mandatory from FY 2024-25 for all GSTR-9 filers. Omitting it or populating with incorrect HSN codes triggers notices.

7. Ignoring GSTR-9C reconciliation differences:
Table 5 of GSTR-9C reconciles book turnover with GSTR-9 turnover. Differences must be explained with specific reasons. "Rounding off" or blank explanations are not acceptable to auditors.

8. Reporting ITC on blocked credits:
If ITC under Section 17(5) was claimed in monthly GSTR-3B, it must be reversed in GSTR-9 Tables 7A-7I. Failure to reverse in GSTR-9 means the annual return confirms the wrong ITC claim — creating demand exposure.

9. Not filing before GSTR-9 due date:
GSTR-9 cannot be filed before all GSTR-1 and GSTR-3B for the year are filed. If even one monthly return is missing, GSTR-9 gets blocked. Late filing of GSTR-9 = Rs. 200/day penalty.

10. Treating GSTR-9 as just a summary:
GSTR-9 is a LEGAL DECLARATION. Any additional liability identified post-GSTR-9 filing requires DRC-03. The return cannot be revised. Errors in GSTR-9 cannot be corrected — they become the basis for audit and demand proceedings.

================================================================================
PART 42: SPECIFIC NOTICE SCENARIOS — ASMT-10 RESPONSE GUIDE
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_093]
[TOPIC: ASMT-10 Notice — Common Scenarios and Reply Drafting Guide]
[GST_FORM: ASMT-10 | ASMT-11 | DRC-03]
[SECTION: Section 61 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 99 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice | Assessment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Instruction]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cbic-website/hindi/pdf/instructions/Instruction-No-02-2022-GST.pdf]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 032, 033, 035, 091]

ASMT-10 is a scrutiny notice issued when the tax officer finds a discrepancy between the taxpayer's GSTR-1, GSTR-3B, GSTR-2B, and other data. The notice must specify the discrepancy and the computed tax, interest, and other dues.

Common ASMT-10 scenarios and reply approach:

Scenario 1 — ITC claimed > GSTR-2B:
Cause: Supplier filed GSTR-1 late, invoices appeared in GSTR-2B only in the next month.
Reply: Provide evidence that: (a) ITC was claimed in the subsequent month when GSTR-2B reflected it; (b) or explain timing difference. Attach GSTR-2B of the relevant month showing the credit.

Scenario 2 — GSTR-1 turnover > GSTR-3B turnover:
Cause: Invoice was uploaded in GSTR-1 but tax was paid in the wrong GSTR-3B period (e.g., rectification in next month).
Reply: Show that GSTR-3B of subsequent months included the tax payment. Provide month-by-month reconciliation.

Scenario 3 — ITC on exempt/nil supplies:
Cause: Taxpayer claimed ITC but also declared exempt outward supplies. Rule 42 reversal not found.
Reply: Show that Rule 42 reversal was done (reference GSTR-3B Table 4B). If not done, accept discrepancy and pay via DRC-03.

Scenario 4 — E-Way Bill vs GSTR-1 mismatch:
Cause: E-Way Bill generated for higher value than invoice value reported in GSTR-1.
Reply: Explain that e-Way Bill value can include freight/insurance which are not part of taxable supply (if separately invoiced). Attach both the invoice and e-Way Bill.

Scenario 5 — Excess ITC on capital goods vs Rule 43:
Reply: Provide detailed capital goods register showing 1/60th monthly credit claim, total ITC on each asset, and the proportionate exempt-use reversal.

Reply format for ASMT-11:
- Reference: ASMT-10 notice number and date.
- Para-by-para response to each discrepancy raised.
- Supporting documents: Relevant GSTR filings (downloaded from portal), invoices, books of account extracts.
- Conclusion: Either accept (with DRC-03 attached) or contest (with legal and factual grounds).
- Filing: Services → Returns → View Notices and Orders → ASMT-10 → File Reply (ASMT-11).

================================================================================
PART 43: GST REGISTRATION — SPECIAL CATEGORIES
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_094]
[TOPIC: Casual Taxable Person (CTP) — Registration and Returns]
[GST_FORM: REG-01 | GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 2(20) | Section 24 | Section 27 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 8 | Rule 13 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: CTP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Registration | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/registration/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 043, 044]

Casual Taxable Person (CTP): A person who occasionally undertakes supply of goods/services in a state/UT where they have no fixed place of business.

Examples: A trader from Maharashtra supplying goods at a trade fair in Delhi; a service provider from Karnataka providing services at a one-time event in Rajasthan.

Registration rules:
- Must apply for TEMPORARY registration in the state/UT where the supply is being made.
- Registration is valid for the period specified in the application or 90 days — whichever is earlier. Extendable for a further 90 days.
- Must estimate tax liability for the registration period and deposit it in advance at the time of registration.
- Cannot opt for Composition Scheme.

Returns filed by CTP:
- GSTR-1 (outward supplies) — monthly.
- GSTR-3B (summary return + payment) — monthly.
- NOT required to file GSTR-9.

Refund of advance deposit: If the advance deposited exceeds actual tax liability, the excess can be claimed as refund after the registration period ends.

---
[CHUNK_095]
[TOPIC: UIN Holders — Unique Identification Number (GSTR-11)]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-11 | REG-13]
[SECTION: Section 25(9) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 82 | Rule 17 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: UIN_Holder]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Registration | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Quarterly | Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 043]

Unique Identification Number (UIN): A special GST identification number issued to certain foreign diplomatic missions, embassies, consulates, and international organizations (e.g., United Nations and its specialized agencies) that are not liable to pay GST but are entitled to claim refund of GST paid on inward supplies.

Who gets a UIN:
- Foreign diplomatic missions and their attachés.
- Persons notified by the Commissioner as entitled to a UIN.
- Multilateral financial institutions and organizations under the United Nations (Privileges and Immunities) Act, 1947.

Return filed: FORM GSTR-11 — Statement of Inward Supplies received by UIN holders. Filed monthly by 28th of the following month. This is the basis for claiming GST refund.

How UIN works in GSTR-1: Suppliers who supply to UIN holders must report these in GSTR-1 Table 4 (B2B section) using the recipient's UIN. The data flows into GSTR-11 of the UIN holder and forms the basis of their refund claim.

---

================================================================================
PART 44: SPECIAL TRANSACTIONS IN GST
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_096]
[TOPIC: Job Work — GST Rules and Compliance]
[GST_FORM: ITC-04]
[SECTION: Section 2(68) | Section 19 | Section 143 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 45 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Quarterly | Annual | Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 045, 048]

Job Work: Processing or working upon goods belonging to another registered person (the "principal"). The job worker performs value addition on the principal's goods.

Key GST rules for job work:
- Principal can send inputs/capital goods to job worker WITHOUT paying GST — using a DELIVERY CHALLAN (not a tax invoice).
- E-Way Bill must be generated if value of goods sent exceeds Rs. 50,000.
- ITC: Principal can avail ITC on inputs/capital goods sent to job worker even without physical receipt at own premises (provided goods are returned within prescribed time).

Return time limits:
- Inputs sent to job worker must be returned within 1 YEAR.
- Capital goods sent must be returned within 3 YEARS.
- If not returned within time: Supply is deemed to have been made by principal on the date of original sending. GST and interest become payable.

Registration of job worker: Job worker need NOT be registered under GST if their turnover is below threshold. Exception: For certain notified goods (e.g., jewellery, precious metals, tobacco), job worker must be registered regardless of turnover.

ITC for job worker: Job worker cannot claim ITC on goods received from principal (as they are not the owner). Job worker charges only their service value (conversion charges) to principal.

GSTR-1 for job work transactions: Principal reports job work in Table 4 (B2B) when final processed goods are supplied from job worker's premises. If goods are directly supplied from job worker's premises to the end customer, the principal must report this as their supply in GSTR-1.

---
[CHUNK_097]
[TOPIC: Stock Transfers Between Branches — Distinct Persons and IGST]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 25(4)(5) CGST Act | Schedule I Entry 2 | Section 7 IGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 28 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | IGST_Act]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 085, 046]

Distinct Persons: When a single legal entity (same PAN) has multiple registrations in different states, each GSTIN is treated as a "distinct person" under GST.

Supply between distinct persons (Schedule I, Entry 2):
Supply of goods or services between distinct persons is TREATED AS A SUPPLY even if made WITHOUT CONSIDERATION. This is one of the deemed supplies under Schedule I.

Tax implications:
- Branch transfer from Maharashtra GSTIN to Delhi GSTIN: Treated as an inter-state supply. IGST applies.
- Branch transfer within the same state (two GSTINs in same state): Intra-state supply. CGST + SGST applies.
- Valuation: At open market value or cost (Rule 28).
- ITC: Receiving branch can claim ITC on the stock received (provided it is used for taxable outward supplies).

Common mistake: Many businesses treat intra-company stock transfers as non-taxable movements. Under GST, these are TAXABLE supplies when the branches have separate GSTINs. Non-compliance leads to ASMT-10 notices for undeclared outward supplies.

GSTR-1 reporting: Stock transfers must be reported as B2B supplies in GSTR-1 Table 4 of the transferring GSTIN, with the recipient GSTIN of the receiving branch.

---
[CHUNK_098]
[TOPIC: Import of Services — GST Treatment and Compliance]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 7(4) IGST Act | Section 9(3) CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Monthly]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: IGST_Act | CGST_Act | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/igst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 045, 082]

Import of services: When a registered person in India receives services from a supplier located outside India, GST is payable under Reverse Charge Mechanism (RCM).

Legal basis: Section 7(4) of IGST Act — import of services for use in business by a taxable person = inter-state supply. IGST applies.

Who pays: The Indian recipient pays IGST at 18% (or applicable rate) under RCM.

Applies even if:
- Indian recipient is an individual, not a business.
- Service is received for personal use (no ITC allowed in that case).
- The overseas supplier has no establishment in India.
- The overseas supplier is not registered under GST.

Compliance steps:
1. Raise a self-invoice in your own name (as recipient acting as deemed supplier).
2. Pay IGST via Electronic Cash Ledger (RCM — no ITC offset for payment of RCM tax).
3. Claim ITC of IGST paid, in the SAME period (if used for taxable outward supply).
4. Report in GSTR-3B: Table 3.1(d) (inward supplies under reverse charge) — taxable value and IGST.
5. Report in GSTR-3B Table 4A(3): ITC claimed on RCM supplies.

Common imported services subject to RCM:
- Cloud computing services (AWS, Azure, Google Cloud).
- Software licenses from overseas vendors.
- Consulting/professional services from foreign firms.
- Royalty payments to non-residents.
- Online advertising (Google Ads, Meta Ads billed from outside India — though large platforms now register under OIDAR).

---

[CHUNK_099]
[TOPIC: GST Notice Risk Indicators — For AI Risk Scoring Engine]
[GST_FORM: Multiple]
[SECTION: Section 61 | Section 73 | Section 74 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 88C | Rule 36(4) | Rule 99 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice | Evaluation]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Instruction | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cbic-website/hindi/pdf/instructions/Instruction-No-02-2022-GST.pdf]
[VALID_FROM: 2022-03-22]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 032, 033, 053, 073, 093]

This chunk is specifically structured for the AI CA platform's risk analysis module. Each indicator below maps to a specific notice risk level.

HIGH RISK indicators (likely to result in ASMT-10 or DRC-01):
- GSTR-1 outward tax > GSTR-3B tax declared for same period by more than 5% or Rs. 50,000 (triggers DRC-01B automatically).
- ITC claimed in GSTR-3B > 100% of GSTR-2B for the period (violates Rule 36(4)).
- GSTR-3B filed but GSTR-1 not filed for the same period (sequential filing violation).
- Inward supplies from suppliers with >3 months of non-filing history in GSTR-2B.
- Large Table 8D gap in GSTR-9 (available ITC >> claimed ITC) without explanation.
- Export refund claimed without LUT on file for the relevant FY.
- No Rule 42 reversal despite declaring both taxable and exempt outward supplies.

MEDIUM RISK indicators (may trigger scrutiny or advisory):
- GSTR-3B filed after due date for 3+ consecutive months.
- HSN codes on invoices inconsistent with previous period filings.
- E-Way Bill values consistently higher than GSTR-1 invoice values (by >10%).
- ITC reversal under Rule 37 (180-day rule) not done despite vendor payments being overdue.
- Section 9(5) supplies reported by ECO not matching ECO's GSTR-8 data for same period.

LOW RISK indicators (advisory level):
- First-time late filing of GSTR-1 or GSTR-3B.
- Minor GSTR-1 vs GSTR-3B mismatch < Rs. 10,000.
- HSN digits used below required level (e.g., 4-digit when 6 required for turnover > Rs. 5 crore).
- GSTR-9C not filed within 7 days of GSTR-9 for turnover > Rs. 5 crore.

COMPLIANCE SCORE INPUTS:
- Return filing punctuality (12-month history).
- GSTR-1 vs GSTR-3B variance trend.
- ITC reconciliation accuracy (GSTR-2B vs GSTR-3B Table 4).
- Outstanding DRC-01B notices.
- Pending ASMT-10 replies.
- GSTR-9 filing completeness.
- Active LUT status (exporters).
- Rule 42/43 reversal compliance.

---
[CHUNK_100]
[TOPIC: Notice Reply Templates — Key Phrases and Legal Arguments for AI Draft Engine]
[GST_FORM: ASMT-11 | DRC-06 | APL-01]
[SECTION: Section 61 | Section 73 | Section 74 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 142 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]
[RELATED_CHUNKS: 035, 093, 099]

This chunk provides structured reply language patterns for the AI draft reply module of the CA platform.

For TIMING DIFFERENCE defences:
"The apparent discrepancy of Rs. [X] in [GSTR-1/GSTR-3B] for the period [month/quarter] arises due to a timing difference in reporting. The invoice dated [date] was issued in [period A] and the corresponding tax liability was discharged in GSTR-3B for [period B] filed on [date]. The aggregate tax for FY [year] is correct and consistent. Reference: GSTR-3B for [period B] — ARN [number]."

For CREDIT NOTE defences:
"The difference of Rs. [X] between GSTR-1 and GSTR-3B for period [month] is attributable to a Credit Note No. [CDN number] dated [date] issued against Invoice No. [invoice] for [reason — goods return/price revision]. The credit note has been reported in GSTR-1 Table 9B for [month]. Net taxable supply after CDN is Rs. [Y], which matches the GSTR-3B Table 3.1(a) declaration."

For ITC TIMING defences (Rule 36(4)):
"The ITC of Rs. [X] claimed in GSTR-3B for [month] corresponds to invoices that appeared in GSTR-2B only in [subsequent month], consistent with Rule 36(4). The claim was not made in excess of GSTR-2B — it was made in the period when GSTR-2B reflected the credit. Reference: GSTR-2B for [month] — download attached."

For EXPORT WITHOUT IGST (LUT):
"The supply worth Rs. [X] has been made as a zero-rated export of [goods/services] under Letter of Undertaking (LUT) for FY [year], filed vide Form GST RFD-11 ARN [number] dated [date]. IGST has not been charged as is permitted under Section 16(3)(a) of the IGST Act. The shipping bill/FIRC (as applicable) is enclosed."

For RULE 42 COMPLIANCE:
"The ITC proportionate reversal under Rule 42 of CGST Rules has been carried out monthly in GSTR-3B Table 4B for all periods. The computation is based on [exempt turnover] ÷ [total turnover] = [%]. Annual reconciliation was done in September [year] GSTR-3B. Details attached."

into your vector DB as filterable attributes. Field semantics:

                  | TCS_Collector | NRTP | OIDAR | ISD | CTP | UIN_Holder | All

                  Payment | Appeal | Assessment | Recovery | Enforcement |
                  EWB | E_Invoice | Rates | Schema | Errors | Evaluation
[FREQUENCY]       Monthly | Quarterly | Annual | Event_Based | Reference
[RISK_LEVEL]      Low | Medium | High | Critical (notice/penalty exposure if
                  the rule in this chunk is violated or misapplied)
[SOURCE_TYPE]     CGST_Act | IGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification |
                  CBIC_Circular | CBIC_Instruction | GST_Portal | EWB_Portal |
                  IRP_Portal | GST_Council
[SOURCE_URL]      Exact official URL (government domain only).

[VALID_TO]        "Current" or ISO date superseded.
[USER_INTENT]     How_to_file | Due_date | Penalty | Eligibility |
                  Reply_drafting | Reconciliation | Error_resolution |
                  Document_checklist | Rate_lookup | Schema_reference
[JURISDICTION]    India_All | specific state(s) | QRMP_Cat1 | QRMP_Cat2

FORM-TABLE DISAMBIGUATION RULE (critical for retrieval):
When a chunk references a table inside a form, the canonical key is
"FORM::Table_N" (e.g. GSTR-1::Table_4 vs GSTR-3B::Table_4). Never store a bare
"Table 4" reference. Embedding text inside chunks below always prefixes the
form name before the table number for the same reason.

RETRIEVAL FILTER RECOMMENDATIONS:
- Always filter VALID_TO = "Current" unless the user asks about a historical
  period; then filter VALID_FROM <= period <= VALID_TO.
- Filter TAXPAYER_TYPE against the client profile (composition clients must
  never retrieve Regular-only ITC chunks, etc.).
- JURISDICTION filter applies mainly to EWB thresholds and QRMP due dates.

PART 46: PAYMENT FORMS — PMT-09 AND WRONG TAX HEAD CORRECTION
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_101]
[TOPIC: Form GST PMT-09 — Transfer of Cash Ledger Balance Between Heads]
[GST_FORM: PMT-09]
[SECTION: Section 49(10), Section 49(11) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 87(13) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Payment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/payments/index.htm#t=Manual_pmt09.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2020-04-21]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Error_resolution]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GST PMT-09 allows a registered person to transfer any amount of tax,
interest, penalty, fee or other amount available in the Electronic Cash Ledger
from one head to another — both across MAJOR heads (IGST, CGST, SGST/UTGST,
Cess) and across MINOR heads (Tax, Interest, Penalty, Fee, Other).

Legal basis: Section 49(10) CGST Act empowers transfer of cash ledger amounts
between heads; Section 49(11) deems the transferred amount as deposited under
the destination head. Rule 87(13) prescribes Form GST PMT-09. Operationalised
on the GST Portal from 21 April 2020.

When to use PMT-09:
1. Cash deposited under the wrong major head (e.g., paid into CGST when SGST
   was due) — transfer instead of claiming refund and re-depositing.
2. Cash deposited under the wrong minor head (e.g., parked under Penalty when
   it was meant for Tax).
3. Reallocating idle cash balance before a GSTR-3B offset where one head is
   short and another has surplus cash.

What PMT-09 CANNOT do:
- It moves only ELECTRONIC CASH LEDGER balance. It cannot move Electronic
  Credit Ledger (ITC) balances between heads — ITC head utilisation is fixed
  by Section 49(5)/49A/49B.
- It cannot transfer an amount already debited (utilised) — only unutilised
  cash balance is transferable.
- Cross-GSTIN transfer: From Notification No. 14/2022-Central Tax (05-07-2022,
  amending Rule 87), PMT-09 also permits transfer of cash ledger balance to a
  DISTINCT PERSON (another GSTIN under the same PAN), except for transfers
  into the SGST/UTGST head of a different state where restrictions apply per
  Section 49(10) proviso (no transfer if any unpaid liability exists in the
  transferor's Electronic Liability Register).

Filing steps (GST Portal):
1. Login → Services → Ledgers → Electronic Cash Ledger → File GST PMT-09 for
   transfer of amount.
2. Cash ledger balance is displayed head-wise (major × minor grid).
3. In "Add Record": select Transfer FROM (major head + minor head + amount)
   and Transfer TO (major head + minor head).
4. Multiple transfer records can be added in one PMT-09.
5. Preview, then file with DSC (Companies/LLPs) or EVC.
6. ARN is generated; ledger is updated immediately; debit and credit entries
   appear in the Electronic Cash Ledger with the PMT-09 reference.

Practical note for the filing engine: PMT-09 is the FIRST remedy to evaluate
when GSTR-3B offset fails due to head-wise cash shortfall while another head
shows surplus. Only if no transferable cash exists should the system suggest a
fresh PMT-06 challan. This avoids unnecessary working-capital lock-in.

---
[CHUNK_102]
[TOPIC: Wrong Tax Head Payment — Section 77 CGST / Section 19 IGST Refund Route]
[GST_FORM: RFD-01 | PMT-09 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 77 CGST Act, Section 19 IGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 89(1A) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Refund | Payment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | IGST_Act | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cbic-website/hindi/pdf/central-tax-circulars/Circular-No-162-18-2021-GST.pdf]
[VALID_FROM: 2021-09-25]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Error_resolution | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Two distinct "wrong head" situations must not be confused by the platform:

SITUATION A — Cash DEPOSITED in wrong head but NOT yet offset against
liability: Remedy is Form GST PMT-09 (see CHUNK_101). No refund application
required. Instant, portal-based.

SITUATION B — Tax actually PAID/DISCHARGED under the wrong head because the
transaction was wrongly classified (intra-state treated as inter-state or
vice versa): Remedy is Section 77 CGST Act read with Section 19 IGST Act.

Section 77(1) CGST / Section 19(1) IGST: A registered person who paid
CGST+SGST on a transaction later held to be INTER-state shall be refunded
those amounts upon payment of the correct IGST (and vice versa).
Section 77(2) CGST / Section 19(2) IGST: NO INTEREST is payable on the
correct tax when it is paid following such re-classification. This is a
statutory interest shield — the reply-drafting module must always cite it
when an officer demands interest in a wrong-head scenario.

Rule 89(1A) (inserted by Notification No. 35/2021-Central Tax, 24-09-2021,
clarified by Circular No. 162/18/2021-GST, 25-09-2021):
- Refund of the wrongly paid tax is claimed in FORM GST RFD-01 under the
  category "Refund of tax paid under wrong head (Section 77)".
- TIME LIMIT: 2 years from the DATE OF PAYMENT OF THE CORRECT TAX (not from
  the original wrong payment). For payments of correct tax made before
  24-09-2021, the 2-year clock runs from 24-09-2021.
- The refund is available whether the re-classification was self-discovered
  or pointed out by a tax officer.
- The refund route applies even where the correct tax is paid through
  GSTR-3B of a later period or via DRC-03.

Drafting pattern for the AI reply engine (wrong-head demand): (1) admit the
classification error if factually correct; (2) evidence payment of correct
tax (ARN of GSTR-3B/DRC-03); (3) cite Section 77(2)/19(2) against interest;
(4) state RFD-01 under Rule 89(1A) has been/will be filed for the wrong-head
amount; (5) request dropping of penalty citing Section 126 (minor,
rectifiable, non-wilful breach).

---
================================================================================
PART 47: ITC COMPLIANCE FORMS — ITC-01, ITC-02, ITC-02A, ITC-03, ITC-04
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_103]
[TOPIC: Form GST ITC-01 — Claim of ITC in Special Circumstances (Section 18(1))]
[GST_FORM: ITC-01]
[SECTION: Section 18(1)(a)(b)(c)(d) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 40 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | Composition]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/itcforms/index.htm#t=manual_itc01.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GST ITC-01 is the declaration to claim ITC on stock in four special
circumstances under Section 18(1):

(a) New registration (mandatory registrant): Person who applied for
registration within 30 days of becoming liable → ITC on inputs in stock,
inputs in semi-finished/finished goods, held on the day IMMEDIATELY PRECEDING
the date of liability to register.
(b) Voluntary registration: ITC on stock held on the day immediately
preceding the DATE OF GRANT of registration. (No capital goods ITC in (a)/(b).)
(c) Composition to Regular switch: ITC on inputs in stock AND on CAPITAL
GOODS (reduced by 5% per quarter or part thereof from invoice date), held on
the day immediately preceding the date of switch.
(d) Exempt supply becoming taxable: ITC on inputs in stock and capital goods
(same 5%-per-quarter reduction) relatable to the supply, held on the day
immediately preceding the date the supply becomes taxable.

Conditions (Rule 40):
- ITC-01 must be filed WITHIN 30 DAYS of becoming eligible (extendable by
  Commissioner).
- Invoices must not be older than ONE YEAR from the eligibility date — ITC on
  older invoices lapses.
- If aggregate ITC claimed exceeds Rs. 2 lakh, the declaration must be
  certified by a practising Chartered Accountant or Cost Accountant.
  Certificate details are entered in the form.
- Invoice-wise details required: supplier GSTIN, invoice no./date, description,
  UQC, quantity, value, ITC amount per head.

Portal path: Services → Returns → ITC Forms → GST ITC-01 → Prepare Online /
Offline. File with DSC/EVC; ARN generated; credit posts to Electronic Credit
Ledger after filing.

Platform validation rules: (1) reject invoices dated > 1 year before
eligibility date; (2) capital goods rows only allowed for clauses (c)/(d);
(3) auto-compute the 5%-per-quarter reduction from invoice date to switch
date; (4) flag CA-certificate requirement at > Rs. 2 lakh.

---
[CHUNK_104]
[TOPIC: Form GST ITC-02 and ITC-02A — Transfer of ITC on Business Reorganisation]
[GST_FORM: ITC-02 | ITC-02A]
[SECTION: Section 18(3) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 41, Rule 41A CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Circular | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/itcforms/index.htm#t=manual_itc02.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

ITC-02 — Transfer of unutilised ITC on sale, merger, demerger, amalgamation,
lease or transfer of business (Section 18(3), Rule 41):
- Transferor files ITC-02 specifying the unutilised ITC (head-wise) to be
  transferred to the transferee GSTIN.
- Condition: transfer of business must be with SPECIFIC PROVISION FOR
  TRANSFER OF LIABILITIES.
- DEMERGER apportionment: ITC is transferred in the RATIO OF VALUE OF ASSETS
  of the new units as per the demerger scheme. Circular No. 133/03/2020-GST
  (23-03-2020) clarifies: (i) "value of assets" means value of ENTIRE assets
  of the business, whether or not ITC was availed on them; (ii) the ratio is
  applied STATE-WISE (per GSTIN), not entity-wide; (iii) the ratio applies to
  the TOTAL ITC balance, not head-wise — the transferor may choose head-wise
  split so long as the total matches.
- A certificate from a practising CA/CMA confirming the liability-transfer
  provision must be uploaded.
- Workflow: Transferor files ITC-02 → appears in transferee's portal →
  transferee ACCEPTS (or rejects) → on acceptance, ITC credits to
  transferee's Electronic Credit Ledger and debits transferor's ledger.
- No express statutory time limit, but file before transferor's registration
  cancellation takes effect, else the form becomes inaccessible.

ITC-02A — Transfer of ITC on obtaining separate registration for multiple
places of business WITHIN a State (Rule 41A, inserted by Notification No.
03/2019-Central Tax, 29-01-2019; effective 01-02-2019):
- When a taxpayer obtains a separate GSTIN for an additional place of
  business in the SAME state, unutilised ITC may be transferred in the RATIO
  OF VALUE OF ASSETS held by each registration.
- Must be filed within 30 DAYS of grant of the new registration.
- Newly registered GSTIN accepts on the portal; ledger entries mirror ITC-02.

Risk note: ITC transfers without the liabilities clause or without the asset
ratio working papers are a standard departmental audit target — store the
scheme document, asset valuation, and CA certificate in the client document
vault and link them to the ITC-02 ARN.

---
[CHUNK_105]
[TOPIC: Form GST ITC-03 — Reversal of ITC on Switching to Composition / Goods Becoming Exempt]
[GST_FORM: ITC-03]
[SECTION: Section 18(4) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 44 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | Composition]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/itcforms/index.htm#t=manual_itc03.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date | Penalty]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GST ITC-03 is the mirror image of ITC-01: it REVERSES (pays back) ITC
when a taxpayer (a) opts INTO the composition scheme, or (b) when goods or
services supplied become WHOLLY EXEMPT (Section 18(4)).

Amount to be reversed (Rule 44):
- Inputs in stock / semi-finished / finished goods: ITC proportionate to
  invoices, computed on the day immediately preceding the switch/exemption
  date.
- Capital goods: ITC reduced on a pro-rata basis taking USEFUL LIFE AS 5
  YEARS (60 months) — reverse the ITC attributable to the REMAINING useful
  life. (Note the asymmetry: ITC-01 re-credit uses 5% per quarter; ITC-03
  reversal uses remaining-life/60 months for capital goods.)
- Where invoices are not available, the prevailing market price on the
  effective date is used, with a certifying CA/CMA certificate (Rule 44(3)).
- Payment mode: reversal is made by DEBITING the Electronic Credit Ledger;
  any shortfall must be paid through the Electronic Cash Ledger. Balance ITC,
  if any, after reversal LAPSES on opting into composition.

Due dates:
- Composition opt-in from start of FY (CMP-02 route): ITC-03 must be filed
  within 60 DAYS of commencement of the relevant financial year.
- Goods/services becoming exempt: file within 30 days (period as specified
  in the relevant notification/order).

Portal path: Services → Returns → ITC Forms → GST ITC-03. One-time filing per
event; cannot be revised — the engine must hard-stop and force preview
confirmation before submission.

---
[CHUNK_106]
[TOPIC: Form GST ITC-04 — Job Work Quarterly/Half-Yearly Statement]
[GST_FORM: ITC-04]
[SECTION: Section 143 CGST Act, Section 19 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 45(3) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: ITC]
[FREQUENCY: Quarterly | Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/itcforms/index.htm#t=manual_itc04.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2021-10-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Form GST ITC-04 is the principal's statement of goods sent to and received
back from JOB WORKERS (Rule 45(3)). It is the compliance backbone of the
Section 143 job-work facility (goods move on delivery challan without tax).

Filing frequency (re-set by Notification No. 35/2021-Central Tax, 24-09-2021,
effective 01-10-2021):
- AATO > Rs. 5 crore (preceding FY): HALF-YEARLY —
  Apr–Sep: due 25th October; Oct–Mar: due 25th April.
- AATO ≤ Rs. 5 crore: ANNUALLY — due 25th April following the FY.
(Earlier regime, 01-07-2017 to 30-09-2021: quarterly, due 25th of the month
after the quarter — tag VALID_TO 2021-09-30 if historical queries arise.)

What is reported (table structure):
- Table 4: Details of inputs/capital goods SENT for job work — challan no./
  date, job worker GSTIN/state, description, UQC, quantity, taxable value,
  tax rate heads.
- Table 5A: Goods RECEIVED BACK from the job worker (original challan
  reference + job worker's challan where applicable).
- Table 5B: Goods sent to ANOTHER job worker from the first job worker's
  premises (job-worker-to-job-worker movement).
- Table 5C: Goods SUPPLIED DIRECTLY from the job worker's premises (with
  invoice details) — permissible only if the job worker is registered or the
  principal has declared the job worker's premises as an additional place of
  business (Section 143(1)(b)).

Link to deemed supply (Section 143 read with Section 19): inputs not received
back within 1 YEAR and capital goods within 3 YEARS (extendable 1 year / 2
years respectively by the Commissioner) are DEEMED SUPPLIED by the principal
on the date the goods were originally sent out — tax plus interest from that
original date becomes payable, declared through GSTR-1/GSTR-3B.

Engine rules: (1) maintain a challan ageing register; alert at 9 months
(inputs) and 30 months (capital goods); (2) reconcile Table 4 vs 5A/5B/5C to
surface unreturned challans before each ITC-04 filing; (3) cross-check e-way
bills generated for job-work movement (value > Rs. 50,000) against challans.

---

PART 48: GSTR-11 DETAILED WORKFLOW AND GSTR-9A STATUS/HISTORY
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_107]
[TOPIC: GSTR-11 — Table-Wise Filing Workflow for UIN Holders]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-11 | RFD-10]
[SECTION: Section 25(9), Section 55 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 82 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: UIN_Holder]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing | Refund]
[FREQUENCY: Quarterly | Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm#t=manual_gstr11.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-11 is the statement of inward supplies filed by UIN holders (embassies,
consulates, UN/multilateral bodies under Section 55) to support their refund
of GST paid on purchases.

Table-wise structure:
- Table 1: UIN (auto-populated).
- Table 2: Name of the person having UIN (auto-populated).
- Table 3: Details of inward supplies received — for each supply: supplier
  GSTIN, invoice/debit note/credit note number and date, taxable value, and
  tax amounts split as IGST / CGST / SGST-UTGST / Cess. Records auto-populate
  from suppliers' GSTR-1 (Table 4 B2B entries quoting the UIN) and are also
  manually addable if a supplier failed to report.
- Table 4: Refund amount claimed (auto-derived total of taxes in Table 3;
  read-only summary feeding the refund claim).

Filing mechanics:
- Filed for the QUARTER in which inward supplies are received; required only
  for quarters in which the UIN holder seeks a refund (no nil-filing
  obligation, no late fee regime).
- GSTR-11 is a PRE-CONDITION for the refund application in FORM GST RFD-10,
  which must be filed within the statutory window (Section 55: refund claim
  within the time prescribed — RFD-10 is enabled on the portal only after
  GSTR-11 for the quarter is filed).
- Portal path: Login with UIN credentials → Services → Returns → Returns
  Dashboard → select FY/quarter → GSTR-11 tile → Prepare Online → verify
  auto-populated invoices, add missing ones → Preview → File with DSC/EVC →
  ARN → proceed to RFD-10.

Supplier-side dependency the platform must check: a supplier invoicing a UIN
holder must record the UIN in the GSTIN field of GSTR-1 Table 4 and must NOT
charge tax incorrectly as exempt — the refund mechanism works only when tax
is charged and reported. Missing supplier reporting is the most common cause
of UIN refund shortfalls; generate a supplier-follow-up list from unmatched
purchase records.

---
[CHUNK_108]
[TOPIC: GSTR-9A — Composition Annual Return: Status, History, and Current Treatment]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-9A | GSTR-4]
[SECTION: Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 80 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Composition]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm#t=Manual_gstr9a.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | How_to_file]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-9A's status has changed over time — the platform must answer
period-specific questions correctly:

PHASE 1 (FY 2017-18 and FY 2018-19): GSTR-9A was the ANNUAL RETURN for
composition taxpayers under the then Rule 80. Filing was WAIVED/made optional
for these two years for composition taxpayers via GST Council decisions
implemented through CBIC notifications (optional filing; deemed filed if not
furnished, provided all CMP-08/returns were filed).

PHASE 2 (FY 2019-20 onwards): The annual compliance for composition taxpayers
moved to FORM GSTR-4 (ANNUAL) — Notification No. 31/2019-Central Tax
(28-06-2019) restructured Rule 62: quarterly tax payment via CMP-08 and a
single ANNUAL GSTR-4. GSTR-9A was effectively DISCONTINUED for FY 2019-20
onwards; the GSTR-9A tile is not applicable for these years.

CURRENT POSITION (answer template): "Composition taxpayers do NOT file
GSTR-9A for any period from FY 2019-20 onwards. Their annual return is
GSTR-4, due 30th June following the FY (due date shifted from 30th April by
Notification No. 12/2024-Central Tax). Quarterly tax is paid via CMP-08 (due
18th of the month after each quarter). GSTR-9A remains relevant ONLY for
historical queries relating to FY 2017-18/2018-19, where filing was optional."

Retrieval guard: if user query contains "GSTR-9A" + a year ≥ 2019-20, the
assistant must redirect to GSTR-4 annual; do not generate GSTR-9A filing
steps for those years.

PART 49: GST RATE CLASSIFICATION DATABASE — SCHEDULES, EXEMPTIONS, RATE LOOKUP

[CHUNK_109]
[TOPIC: GST Rate Schedule Architecture — Goods (Notification 1/2017-CTR) and Services (Notification 11/2017-CTR)]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: Section 9(1) CGST Act, Section 5(1) IGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Rates]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification | GST_Council]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/gst-goods-services-rates.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Rate_lookup]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

The entire GST rate universe is built on a small set of parent notifications.
The rate module must resolve every rate answer to one of these anchors plus
its amendment chain:

GOODS — Notification No. 1/2017-Central Tax (Rate), 28-06-2017:
- Schedule I: 2.5% CGST (5% total)
- Schedule II: 6% CGST (12% total)
- Schedule III: 9% CGST (18% total)
- Schedule IV: 14% CGST (28% total)
- Schedule V: 1.5% CGST (3% — gold, precious metals)
- Schedule VI: 0.125% CGST (0.25% — rough diamonds/precious stones)
Each schedule entry = (S.No., Chapter/Heading/Sub-heading/Tariff item,
Description). Classification follows the Customs Tariff Act First Schedule
and its interpretation rules (the rate notifications adopt Customs Tariff
interpretation rules explicitly).

GOODS EXEMPTIONS — Notification No. 2/2017-Central Tax (Rate), 28-06-2017:
nil-rate exemption list for goods (fresh produce, unbranded staples, etc.).

SERVICES RATES — Notification No. 11/2017-Central Tax (Rate), 28-06-2017:
rate table keyed by SAC Heading (Chapter 99) with conditions (e.g.,
construction with/without ITC, GTA options, restaurant categories).

SERVICES EXEMPTIONS — Notification No. 12/2017-Central Tax (Rate),
28-06-2017: the master exemption list for services (healthcare, education,
specified government services, etc.), each entry with conditions.

RCM NOTIFICATIONS: Goods RCM — 4/2017-CTR; Services RCM — 13/2017-CTR
(advocate, GTA, sponsorship, security services, etc.).

COMPENSATION CESS — Notification No. 1/2017-Compensation Cess (Rate):
luxury/sin goods cess over the 28% slab.

IGST mirrors: every CTR notification has an IGST (Rate) twin with doubled
rates (e.g., 1/2017-Integrated Tax (Rate)). State SGST notifications mirror
the CGST side.

RATE-CHANGE LAYER (critical for VALID_FROM/VALID_TO design): rates are never
amended in the Act — only by amendment notifications to the parent
notifications above, following GST Council recommendations. The rate engine
must therefore store: parent notification + S.No. + amendment notification
no./date + effective date, and resolve a rate AS ON the invoice date (Time of
Supply, Section 14, decides which rate applies when rates change — see
CHUNK_083). NOTE: the GST Council's rate-rationalisation exercise has been
ongoing; before answering any current-rate query, the platform should verify
the entry against the official rate finder (CHUNK_111) rather than rely on a
static slab memory.

---
[CHUNK_110]
[TOPIC: Exemption Notifications — Structure, Conditions, and How to Read an Entry]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: Section 11 CGST Act, Section 6 IGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Rates]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/central-tax-rate-notfns-2017.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Rate_lookup | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Exemptions are granted ONLY under Section 11 CGST / Section 6 IGST by
notification on GST Council recommendation. An exemption entry has four
parts the rate engine must parse separately:

1. ENTRY NUMBER (S.No.) — the citation anchor (e.g., "Entry 74 of N/N
   12/2017-CTR" for healthcare services).
2. CHAPTER/HEADING (HSN/SAC) — classification gate. An exemption claimed
   under the wrong heading fails even if the description fits.
3. DESCRIPTION — the operative scope, read strictly (exemption notifications
   are construed strictly against the claimant — settled interpretation
   principle; the burden of proving the exemption lies on the taxpayer).
4. CONDITION column — many exemptions are CONDITIONAL (e.g., threshold-based
   hotel tariff exemptions, charitable-entity registration under Income-tax
   Act Section 12AA/12AB, pure-services-to-government conditions). The
   condition must be evidenced in the client document vault when the
   exemption is relied upon in a notice reply.

Compliance consequences of an exempt classification (the engine must chain
these automatically): (a) issue BILL OF SUPPLY, not tax invoice (Rule 49);
(b) report in GSTR-1 Table 8 and GSTR-3B Table 3.1(c); (c) trigger Rule
42/43 common-credit reversal if the taxpayer also makes taxable supplies
(see CHUNK_088); (d) include exempt turnover in AGGREGATE turnover for
registration threshold and GSTR-9/9C applicability.

Distinguish: NIL-RATED (rate schedule says 0%) vs EXEMPT (Section 11
notification) vs NON-GST (outside levy) — full matrix in CHUNK_087. For ITC
reversal both nil-rated and exempt count as "exempt supply" (Section 2(47)).

---
[CHUNK_111]
[TOPIC: Official Rate/HSN Lookup Tools — CBIC GST Rate Finder and Portal Search]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: NA]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Rates]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: GST_Portal | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/gst-goods-services-rates.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Rate_lookup]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Official, citable rate-lookup endpoints (use ONLY these for rate answers):

1. CBIC GST Rates page — https://cbic-gst.gov.in/gst-goods-services-rates.html
   Consolidated, amendment-updated rate tables for goods and services keyed
   to the parent notifications in CHUNK_109. This is the primary citation
   source for "what is the rate on X".
2. GST Portal HSN search — https://services.gst.gov.in/services/searchhsnsac
   (Services → User Services → Search HSN Code). Maps description ↔ HSN/SAC;
   used to validate HSN entries before GSTR-1 Table 12 filing.
3. CBIC notification archives —
   https://cbic-gst.gov.in/central-tax-rate-notfns-2017.html (and yearly
   pages) for the authoritative text and amendment history of every rate/
   exemption entry.
4. GST Council — https://gstcouncil.gov.in for press releases/minutes that
   explain rate-change intent (useful in reply drafting; not a levy source
   by itself — the levy needs the CBIC notification).

Rate-answer protocol for the assistant: (1) classify to HSN/SAC; (2) locate
schedule entry + latest amendment; (3) state rate WITH effective date and
notification citation; (4) if the supply straddles a rate change, apply
Section 14 time-of-supply transition rules (CHUNK_083); (5) if
classification is genuinely disputed, flag the Advance Ruling route
(CHUNK_145) instead of guessing.

PART 50: RETURN FORM SCHEMAS — MACHINE-READY FIELD-LEVEL STRUCTURES
