---
[CHUNK_112]
[TOPIC: GSTR-1 Field-Level Schema — Machine-Readable Table/Field Map]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1]
[SECTION: Section 37 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 59 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Schema | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/downloads/returns_offline_tool.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2025-05-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Canonical field schema for GSTR-1 (aligned to the GSTN Returns Offline Tool
template — the official machine format; JSON keys per GSTN dev schema shown
in parentheses). Use form-qualified keys: GSTR-1::Table_N.

GSTR-1::Table_4 (B2B, key "b2b") — one record per invoice line-rate:
  ctin            Recipient GSTIN/UIN. 15 chars, regex
                  ^[0-9]{2}[A-Z0-9]{10}[0-9A-Z]{3}$, must be ACTIVE on
                  invoice date (portal validates).
  inum            Invoice number. ≤16 chars, alphanumeric + "/" "-",
                  unique per FY per supplier.
  idt             Invoice date. DD-MM-YYYY; ≤ filing date; within tax period
                  or amendable window.
  val             Invoice value (total incl. tax). Decimal(15,2).
  pos             Place of supply. 2-digit state code (01–38, 96/97 special).
  rchrg           Reverse charge flag. Y/N.
  inv_typ         R(egular)/SEZ supplies with payment (SEWP)/SEZ without
                  payment (SEWOP)/Deemed Export (DE).
  itm_det[]       Per rate line: rt (rate %, enum 0/0.1/0.25/1/1.5/3/5/6/
                  7.5/12/18/28), txval (taxable value), iamt/camt/samt/csamt
                  (tax amounts — IGST only if pos ≠ supplier state or SEZ;
                  CGST+SGST only if intra-state).
  Cross-field rule: iamt mutually exclusive with (camt+samt); each tax =
  round(txval × rt component, 2) ± Rs. 1 tolerance.

GSTR-1::Table_5 (B2C Large, "b2cl"): inter-state, unregistered, invoice
  value > Rs. 2,50,000. Fields: inum, idt, val, pos, itm_det[] (IGST only).

GSTR-1::Table_6A/6B (Exports/SEZ, "exp"): exp_typ (WPAY/WOPAY), inum, idt,
  val, sbpcode (port code, 6 chars), sbnum (shipping bill no.), sbdt
  (shipping bill date ≥ invoice date), itm_det[] (IGST only; zero if WOPAY
  under LUT).

GSTR-1::Table_7 (B2C Small, "b2cs"): aggregated by pos × rt × supply type
  (intra/inter): typ, pos, rt, txval, iamt/camt/samt, csamt.

GSTR-1::Table_8 (Nil/Exempt/Non-GST, "nil"): matrix of 4 supply categories
  × 3 value columns (nil_amt, expt_amt, ngsup_amt).

GSTR-1::Table_9B (Credit/Debit Notes Registered, "cdnr"): ctin, nt_num,
  nt_dt, ntty (C/D), pos, rchrg, inv_typ, itm_det[]. (Original invoice link
  no longer mandatory — delinked since N/N 03/2019 era amendment to Section
  34 reporting.)
GSTR-1::Table_9B-unreg ("cdnur"): for B2CL/export notes; typ = B2CL/EXPWP/
  EXPWOP.
GSTR-1::Table_9A/9C (Amendments "b2ba"/"cdnra" etc.): carry BOTH original
  keys (oinum, oidt) and revised record; original must exist in a prior
  filed period.

GSTR-1::Table_10 (Advances "at") / Table_11 (Adjustment "txpd"): pos, rt,
  ad_amt — services advances only (goods advances not taxable since
  15-11-2017, N/N 66/2017-CT).

GSTR-1::Table_12 (HSN summary, "hsn"): from May 2025 — SEPARATE B2B and B2C
  sub-tables; fields: num (serial), hsn_sc (4/6/8 digits per AATO slab —
  CHUNK_062), desc (≤30 chars, optional if HSN given), uqc (enum per portal
  UQC list), qty, txval, iamt/camt/samt/csamt. HSN dropdown-validated
  against portal master (manual free-text disabled in phased rollout).

GSTR-1::Table_13 (Documents issued, "doc_issue"): doc nature (12 categories:
  invoices, CDN, receipt/payment/refund vouchers, delivery challans), from/to
  serial, totnum, cancel, net_issue.

GSTR-1::Table_14/14A and 15/15A (ECO Section 9(5) supplies): supplier-side
  taxable value (no tax) in 14; ECO-side full detail in 15; amendments in
  the A variants.

Schema discipline: persist every record with (gstin, ret_period, table_key,
record_hash) to make amendment tracking and GSTR-9 Tables 10/11 roll-ups
deterministic.

---
[CHUNK_113]
[TOPIC: GSTR-3B Field-Level Schema — Machine-Readable Table/Field Map]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: Section 39 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 61 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Schema | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm#t=Create_and_Submit_GSTR3B.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2024-09-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-3B canonical schema (form-qualified keys GSTR-3B::Table_N; all money
fields Decimal(15,2), non-negative unless noted):

GSTR-3B::Table_3.1 — five rows (a)–(e), columns: txval, iamt, camt, samt,
  csamt.
  (a) outward taxable (auto from GSTR-1/1A; downward edit triggers RED flag)
  (b) zero-rated (IGST only; camt/samt locked)
  (c) nil/exempt outward (tax columns locked)
  (d) inward RCM (tax payable side; pairs with ITC in 4A(3))
  (e) non-GST outward (tax columns locked)
GSTR-3B::Table_3.1.1 — Section 9(5): row (i) ECO-payable (full columns);
  row (ii) supplier-through-ECO (txval only; NEGATIVE values permitted from
  Sep-2024 period onwards).
GSTR-3B::Table_3.2 — inter-state to unregistered/composition/UIN: pos ×
  txval × iamt; must be ≤ corresponding 3.1(a) interstate values; from the
  2025 hard-locking advisories this table is auto-populated from GSTR-1 and
  non-editable (correct via GSTR-1A, not here).
GSTR-3B::Table_4 — ITC:
  4A(1) import goods | 4A(2) import services | 4A(3) RCM ITC | 4A(4) ISD |
  4A(5) all other ITC — each iamt/camt/samt/csamt.
  4B(1) reversal Rule 38/42/43 + Section 17(5) | 4B(2) other reversals
  (Rule 37, 37A, re-claimable pool).
  4C = 4A − 4B (system-computed net ITC credited to ECrL).
  4D(1) ITC reclaimed (must trace to earlier 4B(2)) | 4D(2) ineligible
  Section 16(4)/POS (info-only).
  Hard validation: cumulative 4D(1) reclaims ≤ cumulative 4B(2) temporary
  reversals (Electronic Credit Reversal & Re-claimed Statement enforces the
  running balance).
GSTR-3B::Table_5 — exempt/nil/non-GST INWARD: 2 rows (composition+exempt+
  nil; non-GST) × 2 cols (inter, intra).
GSTR-3B::Table_5.1 — interest (editable upward; auto-computed for late
  payment per Section 50) and late fee (system-computed, non-editable).
GSTR-3B::Table_6.1 — payment grid: per head — liability, paid-through-ITC
  (matrix obeying Section 49A/49B order: IGST credit→IGST→CGST→SGST; CGST
  credit↛SGST; SGST credit↛CGST), paid-in-cash, interest, late fee.

Pre-file validation set the engine must replicate locally:
V1 GSTR-1 filed for period (sequential rule) | V2 prior-period GSTR-3B filed
| V3 3.1(d) ≥ implied RCM in GSTR-2B (warning) | V4 4A claims ≤ GSTR-2B
available + opening reclaimable balance (Rule 36(4)) | V5 cash+credit cover
in 6.1 before "Proceed to File" | V6 negative values only where the schema
permits (3.1.1(ii), and Table 4 nets where advisories allow).

---
[CHUNK_114]
[TOPIC: GSTR-9 Field-Level Schema — Annual Return Table/Field Map and Auto-Population Sources]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-9]
[SECTION: Section 44 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 80 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Schema | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Annual]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: GST_Portal | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/returns/index.htm#t=Manual_gstr9.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2025-09-17]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Schema_reference | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTR-9 schema with auto-population lineage (FY 2024-25 form per Notification
No. 13/2025-Central Tax). Editability flags: [A]=auto+editable,
[L]=auto+locked, [M]=manual.

Tables 1–3 [L]: FY, GSTIN, legal/trade name.
Table 4 [A]: outward taxable — 4A B2C, 4B B2B, 4C exports-with-pay, 4D SEZ-
  with-pay, 4E deemed exports, 4F advances unadjusted, 4G RCM inward (tax
  payable), 4G1 Section 9(5) ECO supplies, 4I–4L CDN/amendments. Source:
  Σ GSTR-1 tables + GSTR-1A.
Table 5 [A]: non-taxable outward — 5A exports-without-pay (LUT), 5B SEZ-
  without-pay, 5C RCM-recipient supplies, 5C1 supplier-side 9(5), 5D exempt,
  5E nil, 5F non-GST, 5H–5K CDN/amendments.
Table 6 [mixed]: 6A [L] = Σ GSTR-3B Table 4A; 6A1 [M] NEW — current-FY claims
  of PREVIOUS-FY invoices; 6B–6H [M] split of claims by source (forward, RCM
  registered/unregistered, import goods/services, ISD) and by type (inputs/
  capital goods/input services); 6J [auto] = 6A − Σ(6B..6H) — must explain
  if non-zero; 6K/6L TRAN credits; 6M other; 6O grand total.
Table 7 [M]: reversals — 7A Rule 37, 7A1 Rule 37A (NEW split), 7B Rule 39,
  7C Rule 42, 7D Rule 43, 7E Section 17(5), 7F/7G TRAN reversals, 7H other;
  7I = total; 7J = net ITC (6O − 7I).
Table 8 [mixed]: 8A [L] from GSTR-2B (invoice-wise document download
  available); 8B [auto] = 6B + 6H; 8C [M] ITC of FY claimed in next FY
  (Apr–Nov); 8D [auto] = 8A − 8B − 8C (the scrutiny magnet — see CHUNK_092);
  8E/8F ITC available-but-not-availed / ineligible; 8G–8K import-IGST
  reconciliation.
Table 9 [A]: tax payable [M-editable] vs paid-through-cash/ITC [L from
  GSTR-3B Table 6.1]; FY 2024-25: variance REQUIRES explanation note.
Tables 10/11 [M]: next-FY-reported additions/reductions of supplies.
Table 12/13 [M]: next-FY ITC reversal/availment of this FY's documents.
Table 14 [auto]: differential tax payable on 10/11 and paid.
Table 15 [M]: refunds claimed/sanctioned/rejected/pending; demands.
Table 16 [M]: composition-supplier purchases, deemed supplies (Sec 143
  job-work lapses), goods-on-approval lapses.
Table 17 [M, MANDATORY FY 2024-25]: HSN outward summary (hsn, uqc, qty,
  txval, rate-wise tax). Table 18: late fee payable/paid (NEW).

Payment hook: additional liability surfaced in GSTR-9 → DRC-03 (cause:
"Annual Return"); from FY 2024-25 payable through ITC as well as cash
(N/N 13/2025-CT) — see CHUNK_091.

PART 51: PORTAL VALIDATION ERRORS AND E-INVOICE IRP ERROR CODES

---
[CHUNK_115]
[TOPIC: GST Portal Return-Filing Validation Errors — Common Codes, Causes, Resolutions]
[GST_FORM: GSTR-1 | GSTR-3B]
[SECTION: NA]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Errors | Return_Filing]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://selfservice.gstsystem.in/]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Error_resolution]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Error taxonomy for the filing engine's troubleshooting layer. Official
resolution channel: GST Self-Service Grievance portal
(https://selfservice.gstsystem.in) — raise a ticket with ARN/error screenshot
when portal-side; the codes below are the recurring client-side ones.

GSTR-1 JSON/upload errors (Returns Offline Tool / API):
- RET191106 — "Invoice already exists / duplicate invoice number": same inum
  for same GSTIN+FY already filed. Fix: change invoice series or amend the
  earlier record via Table 9A instead of re-adding.
- RET191113 — "GSTIN of recipient is invalid/cancelled": ctin failed master
  validation (inactive on invoice date). Fix: verify via Search Taxpayer
  (https://services.gst.gov.in/services/searchtp); if recipient was active on
  invoice date but later cancelled, retain proof; if truly cancelled, treat
  as B2C.
- RET191114 — "Date is invalid": idt outside the tax period / future-dated /
  before registration grant date.
- RET191175 — "Original invoice not found for amendment": Table 9A amendment
  keys (oinum/oidt/period) don't match any filed record. Fix: locate the
  original via the filed-return download, match exactly (case-sensitive).
- RET191150 — "Invoice value mismatch": val ≠ Σ(txval + taxes) beyond
  tolerance. Fix: recompute rounding per line.
- "Checksum/Processed with error" on JSON upload: stale offline tool version
  or schema drift. Fix: regenerate JSON with the latest Returns Offline Tool
  from https://www.gst.gov.in/download/returns.
- HSN block (phased mandatory validation): hsn_sc not in portal master or
  digit count below AATO slab. Fix: pick from dropdown master; see CHUNK_062.

GSTR-3B stage errors:
- "Filing not allowed — previous tax period return not filed": sequential
  rule (Section 39 / Rule 61 as enforced from Aug-2024 chain). Fix: file the
  oldest pending period first.
- "RCM/ITC statement balance not posted — SAVE disabled": pending entries in
  the RCM Liability/ITC Statement for a prior period. Fix: post/adjust the
  statement (Services → Ledger → RCM Liability/ITC Statement), then reopen
  3B.
- RED-cell warning: edited value deviates adversely from auto-population
  (down in 3.1, up in 4A). Not a hard stop, but it is logged — the platform
  must capture a CA-entered justification before allowing file.
- "System failure / try again" at OFFSET stage: ledger sync lag after
  PMT-06 payment. Fix: wait for cash ledger reflection (verify in Electronic
  Cash Ledger) before retrying offset; never double-pay.
- DSC errors ("Failed to establish connection to the server" / emSigner):
  restart emSigner as administrator, ensure https://127.0.0.1:1585 trusted,
  re-register DSC under My Profile → Register/Update DSC.

Registration/auth errors:
- "Authentication has failed at emas" (OTP/EVC failures): regenerate OTP,
  confirm registered mobile/email of authorised signatory.
- PAN-validation mismatch at REG-01: name mismatch with CBDT records — fix
  the name as per PAN, not as per deed.

Engine behaviour: every portal rejection must be stored as (form, period,
error_code, raw_message, resolution_applied, retry_count) so recurring
client-specific patterns (e.g., chronic duplicate-series issues) surface in
the risk dashboard.

---
[CHUNK_116]
[TOPIC: E-Invoice IRP Error Codes — Validation Failures and Correction Workflow]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: NA]
[RULE: Rule 48(4) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | Exporter]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Errors | E_Invoice]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: IRP_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://einvoice1.gst.gov.in/Others/MasterCodes]
[VALID_FROM: 2020-10-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Error_resolution]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

High-frequency IRP (NIC einvoice1) validation error codes the platform's
e-invoice module must map to automated fixes (full official list: IRP portal
→ Help → Error Codes / Master Codes):

2150 — "Duplicate IRN": the document (GSTIN+doc type+doc no.+FY) already has
  an IRN. Fix: do NOT regenerate; retrieve the existing IRN via the Get IRN
  API; if the earlier e-invoice was wrong, cancel within 24h and reissue
  under a NEW document number (same number cannot be reused even after
  cancellation).
2172 — "For intra-state transaction IGST amounts are not applicable; only
  CGST and SGST" (and converse 2173/2174 family): POS/state-code vs tax-head
  mismatch. Fix: re-derive POS per IGST Act Sections 10–12, regenerate JSON.
2176 / 2177 — "Invalid HSN code" / HSN-rate mismatch: HSN not in master or
  digit count short (6-digit minimum for e-invoice mandated taxpayers). Fix:
  validate against portal HSN master before submission.
2182 — "Taxable value of all items must equal total taxable value": line-sum
  vs header mismatch beyond ±Rs. 1 tolerance per tax head. Fix: recompute
  header from lines, control rounding at line level.
2189 / 2193 / 2194 — invoice-value / item-value computation mismatches:
  same class as 2182 at different aggregation levels.
2211 — "Supplier and recipient GSTIN should not be same" (B2B self-invoice
  not allowed on IRP except notified cases).
2227 / 2228 — recipient GSTIN invalid/cancelled on document date. Fix: sync
  GSTIN status via the e-invoice "Search GSTIN" before generation; if newly
  registered, use "Sync GSTIN from GST CP" API to refresh IRP master.
2233 — "Duplicate serial number of items": item SlNo repeated in JSON.
2234 — "Invalid document date": future date, or beyond the 30-day reporting
  window for AATO ≥ Rs. 10 crore (from 01-04-2025 — see CHUNK_061); the IRP
  hard-rejects late documents. Fix: there is NO regularisation at IRP — the
  supply must still be reported in GSTR-1 manually, and the invoice is
  non-compliant under Rule 48(5) (treated as not issued), exposing Section
  122 penalty; escalate to CA immediately.
3028 / 3029 — "GSTIN not present in e-invoice system / not active": IRP
  master lag. Fix: use the taxpayer/API "Sync GSTIN" function, retry.

Cancellation/correction workflow (no amendment exists at IRP):
1. Within 24 HOURS of IRN generation → Cancel IRN API/portal (reason code +
   remarks). Cancelled IRN flows to GSTR-1 as cancelled if auto-populated.
2. After 24 hours → IRN cannot be cancelled at IRP. Correct ONLY through GST
   portal instruments: credit note (Section 34) against the invoice, and/or
   amendment of the auto-populated record in GSTR-1 before filing.
3. E-way bill linked to the IRN must be cancelled FIRST (within its own 24h
   window) before IRN cancellation is accepted.
4. Reissue under a fresh document number; never reuse a cancelled number.

PART 52: E-WAY BILL ADVANCED WORKFLOWS AND STATE-WISE THRESHOLDS
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_117]
[TOPIC: E-Way Bill Advanced Operations — Cancellation, Part-B Update, Extension, Rejection, Transporter Assignment]
[GST_FORM: EWB-01 | EWB-02 | EWB-03]
[SECTION: Section 68 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 138, 138A, 138B, 138C CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: EWB]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules | EWB_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://docs.ewaybillgst.gov.in/]
[VALID_FROM: 2018-04-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Error_resolution]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Beyond basic generation (CHUNK_048), the EWB module must support:

CANCELLATION (Rule 138(9)): generator may cancel within 24 HOURS of
generation if goods are not transported or not transported as per the EWB
details. CANNOT cancel if the EWB has been VERIFIED in transit by an officer.
After 24h, the generator cannot cancel — the RECIPIENT may still reject (see
below). Portal: e-Waybill → Cancel → enter EWB no. + reason.

REJECTION by counterparty (Rule 138(12)): the other party named on the EWB
(recipient or supplier) can REJECT it within 72 HOURS of generation or
actual delivery, whichever is earlier; silence = deemed acceptance. Use:
defence against fake EWBs raised against the client's GSTIN — the platform
should poll "EWBs generated by others" daily and alert for unknown documents.

PART-B UPDATE / VEHICLE CHANGE (Rule 138(5)): Part-B (vehicle no./transport
doc) can be updated ANY number of times DURING the validity period — for
transhipment, breakdown, or mode change. EWB without Part-B is not valid for
movement (exception: distance ≤ 50 km within the state between consignor and
transporter for Part-A-only generation). Validity is NOT extended by a
Part-B update.

VALIDITY EXTENSION (Rule 138(10)): only within the window 8 HOURS BEFORE to
8 HOURS AFTER expiry, by the CURRENT transporter/generator, citing reason
(breakdown, natural calamity, law-and-order, transhipment delay). New
validity recalculated from remaining distance (1 day per 200 km; ODC 1 day
per 20 km). Expired EWB in transit = goods liable to detention under Section
129 — the engine must alarm at T-12h before expiry for in-transit
consignments.

TRANSPORTER ID and ASSIGNMENT: unregistered transporters enrol on the EWB
portal and receive a 15-digit TRANSIN (Transporter ID). Generator quotes
TRANSIN in Part-A to ASSIGN the EWB; the transporter then fills/updates
Part-B. Re-assignment: the currently assigned transporter can re-assign to
another transporter; after re-assignment the original generator loses
Part-B edit rights.

CONSOLIDATED EWB — FORM EWB-02 (Rule 138(6)/(7)): a transporter carrying
MULTIPLE consignments in ONE vehicle generates EWB-02 listing the individual
EWB numbers — one document for the conveyance. Individual EWBs retain their
own validities; EWB-02 itself has no independent validity. Regenerate (or
update) on vehicle change for the remaining leg.

MULTI-VEHICLE OPTION: where one consignment is moved in parts on multiple
vehicles after an initial leg (e.g., hub-and-spoke, ODC split), the portal's
"Change to Multi-Vehicle" facility divides the EWB quantity across vehicle
groups; each sub-movement updates its own Part-B against the same EWB.

DETENTION REPORT — FORM EWB-04 (Rule 138D): if a vehicle is INTERCEPTED AND
DETAINED for more than 30 MINUTES, the transporter may upload the detention
report on the portal — creates an official record used in Section 129
representations.

OFFICER-SIDE forms for awareness in reply drafting: EWB-03 (Rule 138C) is
the INSPECTION/VERIFICATION REPORT — Part A (summary) uploaded by the
officer within 24 HOURS of inspection, Part B (final report) within 3 DAYS
(extendable to 6). Rule 138C(2): once goods are verified in one state, NO
SECOND physical verification in the same state during that transit unless
specific tax-evasion information exists — cite this against repeat
interceptions. Detention/seizure proceedings then run under Section 129
(MOV-01 to MOV-09 series: statement, inspection order, detention order
MOV-06, notice MOV-07, penalty order MOV-09 uploaded as DRC-07 summary).

---
[CHUNK_118]
[TOPIC: State-Wise Intra-State E-Way Bill Thresholds and Variations]
[GST_FORM: EWB-01]
[SECTION: Section 68 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 138(1) CGST/SGST Rules (state notifications)]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: EWB]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: EWB_Portal | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://ewaybillgst.gov.in/Notifications.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2018-04-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Eligibility | Rate_lookup]
[JURISDICTION: State_Specific]

INTER-STATE movement: uniform Rs. 50,000 threshold nationwide (Rule 138(1))
— no state can vary it.

INTRA-STATE movement: each State/UT notifies its own threshold and
exemptions under its SGST Rules. The authoritative, always-current source is
the STATE NOTIFICATIONS page of the official EWB portal
(https://ewaybillgst.gov.in/Notifications.html) — the platform must resolve
intra-state questions from there at query time. Stable, well-known
variations to seed the jurisdiction filter (verify on the portal before
relying in a reply):

- DELHI: Rs. 1,00,000 for intra-state movement.
- TAMIL NADU: Rs. 1,00,000 intra-state.
- WEST BENGAL: Rs. 1,00,000 intra-state (single-bill consignments).
- BIHAR: Rs. 1,00,000 intra-state.
- PUNJAB: Rs. 1,00,000 intra-state.
- RAJASTHAN: Rs. 1,00,000 for movement WITHIN the state for specified
  goods/janitorial categories notified; Rs. 50,000 otherwise — and a
  separate relaxation for intra-CITY movement.
- MAHARASHTRA: Rs. 1,00,000 intra-state; no EWB for intra-state movement of
  specified goods irrespective of value where notified.
- GOA: EWB required intra-state only for 22 specified goods categories.
- JHARKHAND: Rs. 1,00,000 for goods other than specified categories.
- ODISHA (platform's home jurisdiction): standard Rs. 50,000 intra-state
  threshold — no enhanced general limit notified; verify current Odisha
  Finance Department/Commissionerate notifications on the EWB portal before
  advising.
- KERALA, KARNATAKA, GUJARAT (goods other than specified job-work/hank-yarn
  type exemptions), UP, MP, CHHATTISGARH, NE STATES: generally Rs. 50,000,
  with state-specific commodity exemptions.

Additional state-variation classes the engine must model: (a) commodity
carve-outs (e.g., Gujarat intra-city job-work exemptions); (b) DISTANCE
carve-outs (intra-state short-haul exemptions); (c) GOLD/precious metals —
EWB for gold (Chapter 71) is enabled as a state-optional requirement (Kerala
was the first mover; Part-B not required for gold EWBs); (d) document
requirements during movement (Rule 138A: invoice/challan + EWB; IRN QR code
suffices as invoice copy for e-invoice taxpayers per Rule 138A(2)).

Retrieval rule: any EWB threshold answer MUST carry a [JURISDICTION] match
and a "verify state notification" caveat with the portal link.

PART 53: REGISTRATION — AMENDMENT, NRTP, OIDAR, UIN WORKFLOWS
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_119]
[TOPIC: Form GST REG-14 — Amendment of Registration: Core vs Non-Core Fields]
[GST_FORM: REG-14 | REG-15]
[SECTION: Section 28 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 19 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Registration]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/registration/index.htm#t=Amendment_of_Registration_Core_Fields.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Amendments to registration are filed in FORM GST REG-14 within 15 DAYS of
the change event (Section 28(1), Rule 19).

CORE FIELDS (require OFFICER APPROVAL; order in REG-15 within 15 working
days of application, deemed approved if no action):
- Legal name of business (no PAN change).
- Principal place of business / additional places of business (address
  changes, additions, deletions) — proof of address mandatory.
- Addition/deletion of promoters, partners, directors, Karta, managing
  committee (stakeholder changes).
If the officer needs clarification, notice in REG-03 within 15 working days
→ reply in REG-04 within 7 working days → approval REG-15 or rejection
REG-05.

NON-CORE FIELDS (auto-approved on filing, no officer intervention):
- Bank account details (must be furnished within 30/45 days of registration
  per Rule 10A or before first refund, whichever earlier — non-furnishing is
  a suspension/cancellation ground under Rule 21(d)).
- Authorised signatory changes, mobile/email of signatories (OTP-verified).
- Goods/services (HSN/SAC) dealt in, state-specific information.

NOT AMENDABLE via REG-14 — require NEW registration:
- Change of PAN (constitution change that alters PAN, e.g., proprietorship
  → partnership): fresh REG-01 + cancellation of old GSTIN with ITC-02
  transfer (CHUNK_104).
- Change of state of principal place of business: GSTIN is state-bound —
  new registration in the destination state, cancellation in origin state.

Effective date: amendment generally takes effect from the DATE OF
OCCURRENCE of the event; officer may approve a different effective date for
core-field amendments where justified.

Platform checklist hooks: track the 15-day filing clock from event date;
attach proofs (electricity bill/rent deed/ownership proof ≤ permitted age
for address; board resolution/consent letters for stakeholder changes).

[CHUNK_120]
[TOPIC: Form GST REG-09 — NRTP Registration Workflow (Detailed)]
[GST_FORM: REG-09]
[SECTION: Section 24(v), Section 27 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 13, Rule 15 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: NRTP]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Registration]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/registration/index.htm#t=Application_for_Non_Resident_Taxpayer.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

REG-09 workflow for Non-Resident Taxable Persons (extends CHUNK_055):

Timing: application at least 5 DAYS PRIOR to commencement of business in
India (Rule 13(1)). Registration is mandatory irrespective of turnover
(Section 24(v)).

Pre-requisites and documents:
- Self-attested copy of valid PASSPORT (individuals). For a foreign COMPANY/
  entity: tax identification number (TIN) or unique number of its home
  country, or PAN if it has one.
- An AUTHORISED SIGNATORY in India: an Indian resident with valid PAN — the
  application is signed by this person (DSC/EVC).
- Indian bank account details (can be furnished post-grant via amendment).
- Estimated values of supplies for the registration period → drives the
  MANDATORY ADVANCE TAX DEPOSIT (Section 27(2)): estimated net tax liability
  deposited at application; registration certificate (REG-06) is issued only
  AFTER the deposit credits the Electronic Cash Ledger.

Steps: gst.gov.in → Services → Registration → New Registration → select
"Non-Resident Taxable Person" → Part A (legal name as per passport/TIN,
country, email/mobile → TRN generated) → Part B in REG-09 within 15 days
(business details, authorised signatory, place of business in India, bank,
advance-tax challan) → submit with DSC/EVC → officer processing as per Rule
9 timelines → GSTIN (REG-06) with validity = period sought or 90 days,
whichever earlier.

EXTENSION — FORM REG-11 (Rule 15): apply BEFORE expiry of the current
validity; one extension of up to a further 90 days; ADDITIONAL advance tax
for the extension period must be deposited at application.

Compliance bundle auto-attached by the platform on NRTP onboarding:
GSTR-5 monthly (13th; final return within 7 days of expiry — CHUNK_055/056),
no composition option, refund of surplus advance deposit only after ALL
GSTR-5s are filed (claim via RFD-01, excess-cash-ledger category).

---
[CHUNK_121]
[TOPIC: Form GST REG-10 — OIDAR Registration Workflow (Detailed)]
[GST_FORM: REG-10]
[SECTION: Section 14 IGST Act, Section 24(xi) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 14 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: OIDAR]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Registration]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: IGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/registration/index.htm#t=manual_oidar.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

REG-10 is the registration application for persons supplying ONLINE
INFORMATION AND DATABASE ACCESS OR RETRIEVAL (OIDAR) services from OUTSIDE
India to NON-TAXABLE ONLINE RECIPIENTS in India (B2C — for B2B imports the
Indian recipient pays under RCM instead, CHUNK_098).

Definitional update: Finance Act 2023 (effective 01-10-2023) WIDENED the
net — "minimal human intervention" was deleted from the OIDAR definition,
and "non-taxable online recipient" now means any UNREGISTERED person
receiving OIDAR services in the taxable territory (the earlier
government/individual-purpose qualifiers were removed). Many previously
out-of-scope foreign digital suppliers became registrable from that date —
tag VALID_FROM 2023-10-01 for scope questions.

Workflow (Rule 14):
- Single PAN-India registration (no state-wise registration) — administered
  centrally (Principal Commissioner, Bengaluru West jurisdiction handles
  OIDAR registrants).
- Application in REG-10 at least 5 days before commencement; signed by an
  authorised representative IN India OR the foreign supplier may appoint an
  agent in India who registers and pays on its behalf (Section 14(2) IGST
  proviso).
- Documents: certificate of incorporation/home-country tax ID, authorised
  signatory/representative details with PAN (if in India), bank details
  (foreign bank acceptable; tax payable via SWIFT/NEFT-linked challan modes).
- No advance deposit requirement (unlike NRTP).

Post-registration compliance bundle: GSTR-5A monthly by 20th (CHUNK_057);
IGST only; cash-only payment (no ITC availment or distribution); intermediary
platforms ("electronic commerce operator or intermediary arranging the
service") are deemed suppliers liable to register unless the conditions of
Section 14(1) proviso are met (invoice issued by actual supplier, etc.).

---
[CHUNK_122]
[TOPIC: Form GST REG-13 — UIN Grant Workflow for Embassies/UN Bodies]
[GST_FORM: REG-13]
[SECTION: Section 25(9) CGST Act, Section 55 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 17 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: UIN_Holder]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Registration]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Low]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Circular]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/registration/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

UIN grant (Rule 17): specialised agencies of the UN, multilateral financial
institutions notified under the United Nations (Privileges and Immunities)
Act 1947, consulates and embassies, and any other class notified by the
Commissioner apply in FORM GST REG-13 (or registration is granted suo motu
by the proper officer based on MEA recommendation).

Key mechanics:
- UIN is granted centrally and is valid ACROSS India — a SINGLE UIN serves
  all states (CBIC clarified single-UIN sufficiency for refund claims;
  suppliers anywhere in India quote the same UIN).
- Certificate issued in REG-06 within 3 WORKING DAYS of complete application.
- UIN structure differs from GSTIN (it is a 15-character ID but not
  PAN-derived).
- Purpose-bound: UIN exists ONLY to enable refund of taxes on inward
  supplies under Section 55 (reciprocity-based for diplomatic missions, per
  MEA certification); UIN holders make no outward supplies under GST.
- Downstream compliance: quarterly GSTR-11 (CHUNK_107) → refund in RFD-10
  (filed within the prescribed window from the last day of the quarter) →
  refund processed per Rule 95 (minimum invoice value conditions and MEA
  reciprocity certificate apply for missions).

Supplier-side rule for the filing module: invoices to UIN holders are
reported as B2B in GSTR-1 Table 4 with the UIN in the recipient field; tax
IS charged (these are not exempt supplies); failure to quote UIN breaks the
holder's refund chain.

PART 54: ASSESSMENTS — PROVISIONAL, BEST JUDGMENT, SUMMARY, SCRUTINY SOP

[CHUNK_123]
[TOPIC: Provisional Assessment — Section 60, Forms ASMT-01 to ASMT-07]
[GST_FORM: ASMT-01 | ASMT-02 | ASMT-03 | ASMT-04 | ASMT-05 | ASMT-06 | ASMT-07]
[SECTION: Section 60 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 98 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Assessment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility | Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Provisional assessment (Section 60) is taxpayer-INITIATED: used when the
taxpayer is UNABLE TO DETERMINE (a) the VALUE of supply (e.g., pricing
pending finalisation, related-party valuation disputes) or (b) the RATE
(classification uncertainty).

Form flow (Rule 98):
ASMT-01: Taxpayer's application requesting provisional payment, with
  documents and grounds (why value/rate cannot be determined).
ASMT-02: Officer's notice seeking additional information; reply in ASMT-03
  (taxpayer may also appear in person).
ASMT-04: ORDER allowing provisional assessment — specifies the provisional
  value/rate and the BOND + SECURITY (security ≤ 25% of the bond amount)
  the taxpayer must execute. Order due within 90 DAYS of ASMT-01.
ASMT-05: Taxpayer furnishes the bond (with bank guarantee security as
  ordered). Tax is then paid provisionally on that basis.
ASMT-06: Officer's notice calling for information for FINALISATION.
ASMT-07: FINAL assessment order — due within 6 MONTHS of ASMT-04
  (extendable: +6 months by Joint/Additional Commissioner; up to 4 YEARS by
  the Commissioner for sufficient cause).

Settlement consequences:
- Shortfall on finalisation: pay differential WITH INTEREST under Section
  50(1) from the original due date of the tax (not from finalisation).
- Excess paid: REFUND with interest under Section 56 (subject to unjust
  enrichment).
- Release of security: apply in ASMT-08 after final order + payment;
  officer releases via ASMT-09 within 7 working days.

Use-case guidance for the platform: recommend provisional assessment over
"pay under protest + litigate" where a recurring valuation/classification
issue affects ongoing supplies — it caps interest exposure and creates a
clean finalisation path; pair with an Advance Ruling application (CHUNK_145)
for the legal question where eligible.

---
[CHUNK_124]
[TOPIC: Best Judgment Assessments — Section 62 (Non-Filers, ASMT-13) and Section 63 (Unregistered, ASMT-14/15)]
[GST_FORM: ASMT-13 | ASMT-14 | ASMT-15 | GSTR-3A]
[SECTION: Section 62, Section 63 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 100 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Assessment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Penalty | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

SECTION 62 — Best judgment assessment of RETURN NON-FILERS:
Trigger chain: return not filed → notice in GSTR-3A (15 days to file) →
still not filed → officer assesses tax liability to the BEST OF HIS
JUDGMENT using available material (GSTR-1, e-way bills, GSTR-2B of buyers,
bank data) → order in ASMT-13 with summary in DRC-07.
Time limit for the order: within the Section 73/74/74A limitation frame for
the relevant FY.
WITHDRAWAL SAFETY VALVE — Section 62(2) as amended by Finance Act 2023
(effective 01-10-2023): if the taxpayer FILES THE VALID RETURN WITHIN 60
DAYS of service of ASMT-13 (extendable by a FURTHER 60 days on payment of
additional late fee of Rs. 100/day under the proviso), the ASMT-13 order is
DEEMED WITHDRAWN — but interest (Section 50) and late fee (Section 47)
survive. (Pre-01-10-2023 the window was 30 days — tag historical queries.)
Reply strategy the engine should draft: (1) file the pending return
immediately with payment; (2) letter invoking Section 62(2) deemed
withdrawal quoting return ARN; (3) if beyond 120 days, the ONLY remedy is
appeal (APL-01) — ASMT-13 is an appealable order; amnesty schemes for
deemed-withdrawal of old ASMT-13s should be checked on cbic-gst.gov.in.

SECTION 63 — Best judgment assessment of UNREGISTERED persons:
Applies to (a) persons LIABLE to register who failed to, and (b) persons
whose registration was CANCELLED under Section 29(2) but who were liable to
pay tax for the period.
Procedure (Rule 100(2)): notice in ASMT-14 (show cause, 15 days) →
opportunity of being heard → assessment order in ASMT-15 + DRC-07 summary.
Time limit: within 5 YEARS from the due date of the annual return of the
relevant FY.
Defence angles for drafting: threshold computation (aggregate turnover
below Section 22 limits — produce the PAN-level turnover working),
exempt-supply composition of turnover, and natural-justice failures (no
ASMT-14 served / no hearing) which vitiate the order under Section 75(4).

---
[CHUNK_125]
[TOPIC: Summary Assessment — Section 64, Forms ASMT-16/17/18]
[GST_FORM: ASMT-16 | ASMT-17 | ASMT-18]
[SECTION: Section 64 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 100(3)-(5) CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Assessment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 64 SUMMARY ASSESSMENT is an emergency power: the proper officer,
WITH PRIOR PERMISSION of the Additional/Joint Commissioner, may assess tax
on EVIDENCE OF TAX LIABILITY where he believes DELAY WOULD ADVERSELY AFFECT
REVENUE (e.g., taxpayer about to abscond/dispose of assets). No prior SCN —
this inverts normal due process, which is why the withdrawal remedy is
generous.

Forms (Rule 100(3)-(5)):
ASMT-16: the summary assessment order (with DRC-07 summary).
ASMT-17: TAXPAYER'S APPLICATION FOR WITHDRAWAL of the order — within 30
  DAYS of receipt, to the Additional/Joint Commissioner.
ASMT-18: order accepting (withdrawing ASMT-16, after which the matter
  proceeds under Section 73/74 normally) or rejecting the withdrawal.

Special deeming: where the taxable person to whom the liability pertains is
NOT ASCERTAINABLE and the liability relates to GOODS, the PERSON IN CHARGE
OF THE GOODS (transporter/warehouse keeper) is deemed the taxable person —
relevant in transit-interception fact patterns.

Drafting angles: (1) ASMT-17 within 30 days arguing the order is ERRONEOUS
(the statutory ground) — attack the evidence basis and the absence of
revenue-risk facts; (2) absence of recorded prior permission of Addl/Jt
Commissioner is a jurisdictional defect; (3) even the Addl/Jt Commissioner
SUO MOTU may withdraw an erroneous ASMT-16; (4) if withdrawal fails,
ASMT-16 is appealable under Section 107.

---
[CHUNK_126]
[TOPIC: Return Scrutiny SOP — Officer-Side Process Mapping (Instruction 02/2022-GST and ASMT-10 Lifecycle)]
[GST_FORM: ASMT-10 | ASMT-11 | ASMT-12]
[SECTION: Section 61 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 99 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: Regular | QRMP | Composition]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Assessment | Notice]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CBIC_Instruction | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cbic-website/hindi/pdf/instructions/Instruction-No-02-2022-GST.pdf]
[VALID_FROM: 2022-03-22]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Reconciliation]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Knowing the OFFICER'S SOP (CBIC Instruction 02/2022-GST dated 22-03-2022
for FY 2017-18/2018-19; scrutiny is online/automated via the DGARM-ACES-GST
workflow per Instruction guidance for later years) lets the reply engine
anticipate exactly what the officer must do — and where procedural defects
arise:

Officer-side sequence:
1. SELECTION: GSTINs selected centrally by DGARM on risk parameters; list
   pushed to jurisdictional officers' scrutiny dashboard.
2. SCRUTINY SCHEDULE: officer scrutinises with a defined monthly disposal
   norm; one notice per GSTIN per FY covering ALL discrepancies (the SOP
   discourages piecemeal multiple ASMT-10s for the same FY — a drafting
   point when a client receives serial notices).
3. ASMT-10 ISSUE: must QUANTIFY the tax/interest where possible and must
   state the SPECIFIC discrepancy (vague "reconcile your returns" notices
   are challengeable). Response time: as specified, up to 30 days.
4. INDICATIVE PARAMETER LIST (Annexure B of the Instruction — mirror these
   in the platform's pre-emptive risk scan, CHUNK_099):
   GSTR-1 vs 3B liability gap | 3.1(d) RCM vs GSTR-2B RCM inward gap |
   ITC 4A(5) vs GSTR-2B/2A gap | TDS/TCS credits (GSTR-7/8) vs turnover
   declared | liability vs e-way bill turnover | Rule 42/43 reversal absence
   despite exempt supplies | Section 17(5) patterns | ITC from cancelled/
   non-filer/composition suppliers | Rule 36(4) breach | late-fee/interest
   short-payment on delayed filings.
5. TAXPAYER REPLY in ASMT-11 (with DRC-03 if any discrepancy accepted).
6. CLOSURE: officer issues ASMT-12 (acceptance) — the platform must DEMAND
   ASMT-12 closure and not let matters rest on an unacknowledged ASMT-11.
7. ESCALATION: reply unsatisfactory / no reply → officer proceeds to Section
   73/74 (DRC-01A/DRC-01), or recommends audit (Section 65) / special audit
   (Section 66) / inspection (Section 67). Scrutiny itself is a NON-INTRUSIVE
   desk review — officers cannot demand books wholesale at ASMT-10 stage
   (documents beyond the discrepancy scope can be respectfully declined
   citing the Instruction's "minimal interface" mandate).

Reply skeleton (ASMT-11): cite notice ref → para-wise discrepancy response
with reconciliation tables → ARNs/GSTR extracts as annexures → DRC-03
particulars for accepted points → prayer for ASMT-12 closure.

PART 55: ADJUDICATION PRINCIPLES, DRC FORM FAMILY, RECOVERY PROVISIONS
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_127]
[TOPIC: Section 75 — General Provisions for Determination of Tax: Natural Justice, Hearings, Limitation, Order Validity]
[GST_FORM: DRC-01 | DRC-07]
[SECTION: Section 75 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 142 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Notice | Assessment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 75 supplies the procedural backbone for ALL Section 73/74/74A
adjudications. Every sub-section is a potential defence — the reply engine
must test each order against this checklist:

75(1) — Limitation EXCLUSION for stay periods: where an appellate
authority/court stays the SCN, the stay period is excluded from the 3/5-year
limitation.
75(2) — FRAUD ALLEGATION NOT SUSTAINED: if an appellate authority/court
holds that the Section 74 charge (fraud/wilful misstatement/suppression) is
NOT established, the officer must re-determine the tax AS IF under Section
73 — penalty drops from 100% to the Section 73 scale. Always plead this
alternatively in Section 74 replies.
75(3) — Re-determination after such direction: within 2 YEARS of the
direction.
75(4) — HEARING IS MANDATORY where (a) a written request is made, OR (b)
ANY ADVERSE DECISION is contemplated. An order passed without offering a
hearing despite adverse findings is void for natural-justice violation —
the most successful writ/appeal ground in practice. The reply engine must
ALWAYS include a line requesting personal hearing.
75(5) — Maximum THREE ADJOURNMENTS of hearing per party, on sufficient
cause recorded in writing.
75(6) — The order MUST be a SPEAKING ORDER: it shall set out the relevant
facts and the BASIS of the decision. Orders that merely reproduce the SCN
and reject the reply without dealing with each contention are challengeable.
75(7) — DEMAND CANNOT EXCEED THE SCN: the order cannot demand tax/interest/
penalty beyond the AMOUNT specified in the notice, and NO demand can be
confirmed on GROUNDS not raised in the SCN. Compare DRC-07 against DRC-01
line-by-line — any excess is per se illegal.
75(8) — Modified demand flows down: if the appellate forum modifies the tax,
interest and penalty stand automatically modified.
75(9) — Interest is MANDATORY on confirmed tax whether or not the order
specifies it (do not assume silence = no interest).
75(10) — DEEMED CONCLUSION: adjudication NOT completed within the Section
73(10)/74(10) time limit (3/5 years) means the proceeding is DEEMED
CONCLUDED — a hard limitation kill-switch; always compute and plead.
75(11) — Issue decided against revenue and under appeal: limitation pauses
for that issue in other proceedings.
75(12) — SELF-ASSESSED TAX SHORTCUT: tax SELF-ASSESSED in a RETURN (GSTR-1
declared but unpaid in GSTR-3B — the Explanation includes Section 37
outward-supply details) can be recovered DIRECTLY under Section 79 WITHOUT
any SCN. This is the statutory teeth behind DRC-01B/Rule 88C — but Rule 88C
reply opportunity must still be exhausted before Section 79 recovery
(Rule 142B / DRC-01D intimation operationalises this).
75(13) — NO DOUBLE PENALTY: where Section 73/74 penalty is imposed, no
other penalty under any other provision for the SAME act/omission. Deploy
against stacked Section 122 + Section 74 penalties.

---
[CHUNK_128]
[TOPIC: DRC Form Family — DRC-01 to DRC-25: Post-Order Demand, DRC-07/08, and Recovery Forms Map]
[GST_FORM: DRC-01 | DRC-02 | DRC-03 | DRC-04 | DRC-05 | DRC-06 | DRC-07 | DRC-08 | DRC-09 | DRC-10 | DRC-13 | DRC-16 | DRC-20 | DRC-22 | DRC-25]
[SECTION: Sections 73-79, 84 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rules 142, 143-161 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Recovery | Notice]
[FREQUENCY: Reference]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Schema_reference]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Complete DRC map for the notice-classification module (Rule 142 and the
recovery rules 143–161):

PRE-ADJUDICATION:
DRC-01A — Intimation of ascertained tax BEFORE SCN (Part A officer; Part B
  taxpayer response — pay or contest). Optional for the officer since
  15-10-2020 ("may" communicate).
DRC-01 — Summary of SHOW CAUSE NOTICE (the SCN proper is attached; DRC-01
  alone without a detailed SCN violates Rule 142(1) — drafting point).
DRC-02 — Summary of STATEMENT under Section 73(3)/74(3) (subsequent periods,
  same grounds — no fresh SCN needed).
DRC-03 — Taxpayer's voluntary/SCN-stage payment intimation (CHUNK_091).
DRC-04 — Officer's ACKNOWLEDGEMENT of DRC-03 payment.
DRC-05 — Order CONCLUDING proceedings after full SCN-stage payment.
DRC-06 — Taxpayer's REPLY to the SCN (the portal vehicle for the written
  defence; personal-hearing request checkbox lives here).

POST-ADJUDICATION:
DRC-07 — SUMMARY OF ORDER: uploaded electronically; creates the DEMAND
  entry in the Electronic Liability Register Part-II. The order itself +
  DRC-07 together complete adjudication; demand becomes recoverable after
  3 MONTHS from order service (Section 78) unless appealed with pre-deposit
  (appeal + 10% pre-deposit STAYS the balance — Section 107(7)).
DRC-08 — RECTIFICATION/WITHDRAWAL summary: modifies or withdraws DRC-07
  pursuant to a Section 161 rectification or appellate outcome — the
  liability register re-aligns to DRC-08. If an appeal succeeds but the
  register still shows the old demand, demand DRC-08 issuance.

RECOVERY CHAIN (Section 79 modes — see CHUNK_129):
DRC-09 — Recovery by deduction from money owed BY ANY GOVERNMENT OFFICE to
  the defaulter (Section 79(1)(a)).
DRC-10/DRC-11/DRC-12 — Recovery by AUCTION of goods under control of the
  officer: sale notice / successful-bidder intimation / sale certificate.
DRC-13 — GARNISHEE notice to a THIRD PERSON (bank, debtor, customer) who
  owes money to the defaulter (Section 79(1)(c)) — banks freeze on receipt;
  the third party paying is discharged; failure to comply makes the third
  party a defaulter. DRC-14: certificate of payment by garnishee.
DRC-15 — Execution through CIVIL COURT decree route.
DRC-16/17/18/19 — ATTACHMENT and SALE of movable/immovable property:
  attachment order / sale notice / auction / sale-proceeds certificate;
  DRC-23 releases attachment on payment.
DRC-20/21 — INSTALMENT/DEFERRED payment application and order (Section 80
  — CHUNK_130).
DRC-22 — PROVISIONAL ATTACHMENT order under Section 83 (CHUNK_130);
  DRC-22A: taxpayer's objection; DRC-23: release.
DRC-24 — Recovery intimation to LIQUIDATOR (Section 88, company in
  liquidation).
DRC-25 — CONTINUATION/reduction of recovery proceedings when demand is
  enhanced/reduced in appeal/revision (Section 84): no fresh notice needed
  for reduced demands; recovery continues from the stage already reached.

Classifier rule: map portal notice metadata (form code) to this table FIRST;
the form code alone determines the procedural stage, deadlines, and which
reply template (GST_REPLY_DEMAND vs recovery-objection letter) applies.

[CHUNK_129]
[TOPIC: Recovery Provisions — Section 78 Initiation and Section 79 Modes; Bank Attachment Handling]
[GST_FORM: DRC-09 | DRC-13 | DRC-16]
[SECTION: Section 78, Section 79 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rules 143-157 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Recovery]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Penalty]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

SECTION 78 — WHEN recovery starts: any amount payable under an ORDER becomes
recoverable if unpaid within 3 MONTHS from the date of SERVICE of the order.
PROVISO: the proper officer may, for reasons RECORDED IN WRITING and in the
interest of revenue, require payment within a SHORTER period — an
early-recovery order without recorded reasons is challengeable (CBIC
Instruction No. 01/2024-GST, 30-05-2024, restricts early recovery to
exceptional, reasoned cases and requires Principal Commissioner-level
consideration — cite it against premature DRC-13s).

SECTION 79 — recovery MODES (officer may use one or more, any order):
(a) deduction from money the department owes the defaulter (DRC-09);
(b) detention and SALE of goods belonging to the defaulter under the
    officer's control (DRC-10/11/12);
(c) GARNISHEE — notice to any person who owes money to, or holds money for,
    the defaulter (banks, debtors) to pay the government directly (DRC-13);
(d) distraint and sale of movable/immovable PROPERTY (DRC-16 chain);
(e) recovery through the DISTRICT COLLECTOR as arrears of land revenue;
(f) recovery via MAGISTRATE as a fine.
Section 79(4): recovery of SGST arrears can be made by CGST officers and
vice versa (cross-empowerment), remitted to the respective government.

BANK-ATTACHMENT (DRC-13) RESPONSE PROTOCOL for the platform:
1. Verify the FOUNDATION: is there a served order + DRC-07 + 3-month lapse
   (or recorded early-recovery reasons)? If the demand is only at DRC-01B/
   SCN stage, the DRC-13 is without jurisdiction — write to the issuing
   officer and the bank immediately.
2. Check APPEAL STATUS: if APL-01 was filed with 10% pre-deposit, recovery
   of the BALANCE is DEEMED STAYED (Section 107(7)) — furnish APL-02
   acknowledgement + pre-deposit challan to officer and bank; demand
   DRC-13 withdrawal.
3. If demand is genuinely due: negotiate instalments (Section 80, DRC-20 —
   CHUNK_130) or pay and seek DRC-23/withdrawal.
4. Operational-account hardship (salaries/statutory dues blocked): represent
   for partial de-freezing; escalate via grievance to jurisdictional
   Commissioner; writ jurisdiction is the last resort for disproportionate
   attachment.

[CHUNK_130]
[TOPIC: Provisional Attachment (Section 83, DRC-22) and Payment in Instalments (Section 80, DRC-20/21)]
[GST_FORM: DRC-22 | DRC-22A | DRC-23 | DRC-20 | DRC-21]
[SECTION: Section 83, Section 80 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 159, Rule 158 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Recovery]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Instruction]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2021-01-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Eligibility]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

SECTION 83 — PROVISIONAL ATTACHMENT (pre-adjudication asset freeze):
Scope (post-Finance Act 2021 text, effective 01-01-2022): after INITIATION
of any proceeding under Chapter XII (assessment), XIV (inspection/search) or
XV (demands/recovery), the COMMISSIONER — and only the Commissioner, with a
WRITTEN OPINION that attachment is necessary to protect revenue — may
provisionally attach property INCLUDING BANK ACCOUNTS of the taxable person
(or of a Section 122(1A) beneficiary). Order in DRC-22 (Rule 159).
HARD SUNSET: every Section 83 attachment CEASES TO HAVE EFFECT after ONE
YEAR from the order — no extension; a fresh order needs fresh satisfaction.
Taxpayer remedies (Rule 159(5)): file OBJECTION in DRC-22A within 7 DAYS of
attachment contending the property was not liable to attachment; entitled
to a HEARING; release via DRC-23. Perishable/hazardous goods releasable on
payment/security. Key objection grounds the engine should draft: (i) order
not by the Commissioner personally / no recorded opinion; (ii) no pending
Chapter XII/XIV/XV proceeding against the person; (iii) attachment of raw
materials/working capital destroying the business is disproportionate
(supported by CBIC's own guidelines in Instruction CBEC-20/16/05/2021-GST,
23-02-2021: attachment is a draconian, last-resort power; prefer
non-operational assets; not to be used routinely).

SECTION 80 — PAYMENT IN INSTALMENTS:
On WRITTEN APPLICATION (FORM GST DRC-20), the COMMISSIONER may allow any
amount due (OTHER THAN self-assessed tax shown in a return — that is
statutorily excluded) to be paid in MONTHLY INSTALMENTS up to a MAXIMUM OF
24, with interest under Section 50, against an order in DRC-21 (Rule 158;
the jurisdictional officer reports on financial condition before the
Commissioner decides).
DEFAULT CLAUSE: default in ANY ONE instalment makes the ENTIRE outstanding
balance due immediately without further notice.
Eligibility guardrails: not available if the taxpayer has defaulted on a
prior instalment plan in the same FY or where the amount is self-assessed
return tax (for which only late payment with interest, or appellate routes,
exist). Use case: confirmed DRC-07 demands where appeal is not pursued but
liquidity is constrained.

---
================================================================================
PART 56: ENFORCEMENT — INSPECTION, SEARCH, SEIZURE, SUMMONS, DGGI
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_131]
[TOPIC: Inspection, Search and Seizure — Section 67, INS Forms, Rights and Handling Protocol]
[GST_FORM: INS-01 | INS-02 | INS-03 | INS-04 | INS-05]
[SECTION: Section 67 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 139, Rule 140, Rule 141 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Enforcement]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

SECTION 67(1) — INSPECTION: an officer not below JOINT COMMISSIONER must
record REASONS TO BELIEVE that (a) a taxable person suppressed transactions/
stock/claimed excess ITC or contravened the Act to evade tax, or (b) a
transporter/warehouse operator is keeping escaped goods or false accounts.
Authorisation in FORM GST INS-01 to a subordinate officer. Inspection =
access and examination; no seizure power by itself.

SECTION 67(2) — SEARCH AND SEIZURE: on reasons to believe (again JC-level)
that goods liable to CONFISCATION or relevant documents/books/things are
secreted in any place — authorisation INS-01; SEIZURE ORDER in INS-02.
- Where seizure is not practicable: order of PROHIBITION in INS-03 (goods
  not to be removed without permission).
- Documents not relied upon in the SCN must be RETURNED within 30 DAYS of
  SCN issue (Section 67(3)).
- Seized goods: PROVISIONAL RELEASE on bond (INS-04) + security/bank
  guarantee covering applicable tax, interest and penalty (Rule 140); final
  release order INS-05 on conclusion.
- Section 67(7): if NO NOTICE is issued within SIX MONTHS of seizure of
  goods (extendable by a further 6 months on sufficient cause), the goods
  MUST be returned — diary this date on every seizure matter.
- Section 67(8)/(9) + Rule 141: perishable/hazardous inventory may be
  disposed of; inventory list rights apply.
- Section 67(10) imports the Code of Criminal Procedure search safeguards
  (now the corresponding BNSS provisions): two independent WITNESSES,
  PANCHNAMA/memo of proceedings, copy to the occupant.

TAXPAYER PROTOCOL CHECKLIST (embed in the platform's "search response"
playbook):
1. Ask for and PHOTOGRAPH the INS-01 authorisation (officer names, premises
   address must match) and officer ID cards.
2. Insist on two independent witnesses; read the panchnama fully before any
   signature; record objections IN the panchnama.
3. Statements recorded during search are under Section 70 oath rules — the
   deponent may state facts only to the best of knowledge and may decline
   speculation; retraction of coerced statements should be by affidavit at
   the earliest (delay weakens retraction).
4. Obtain copies/hash values of seized electronic devices and the document
   seizure memo (entitled to copies under Section 67(5) — officer may permit
   copies/extracts in his presence unless it prejudices investigation).
5. NO TAX "RECOVERY" DURING SEARCH: any DRC-03 signed under the stress of
   search may be contested; CBIC Instruction No. 01/2022-23 (GST-Inv.)
   dated 25-05-2022 mandates that payments during search must be VOLUNTARY,
   and officers must inform taxpayers they can pay later — complaints lie
   to the Pr. Chief Commissioner. The platform should advise clients to
   avoid on-the-spot payment commitments and seek CA presence.
6. Post-search: compile a search-day minute (timeline, persons present,
   items seized), reconcile seized stock count methodology, and prepare
   provisional-release application (INS-04 route) for business-critical
   goods.

---
[CHUNK_132]
[TOPIC: Summons under Section 70 — Rights, Obligations, Reply Protocol, and DGGI Investigations]
[GST_FORM: NA]
[SECTION: Section 70 CGST Act, Section 136 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Enforcement]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Critical]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CBIC_Instruction]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cbic-website/hindi/pdf/instructions/instruction-no-03-2022-23.pdf]
[VALID_FROM: 2022-08-17]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

SECTION 70: the proper officer may SUMMON any person to give evidence or
produce documents; the inquiry is a "JUDICIAL PROCEEDING" within the meaning
of the criminal-law provisions on false evidence — false statements are
prosecutable. Attendance is legally compulsory; non-appearance can attract
Section 122(3)(d) penalty and BNSS/IPC-equivalent consequences.

CBIC GUARDRAILS the defence can invoke — Instruction No. 03/2022-23
(GST-Investigation) dated 17-08-2022 on summons discipline:
- Summons is NOT to be used casually for documents obtainable by a simple
  LETTER; officers should prefer letters for routine information.
- Issued by Superintendent-level and above WITH PRIOR WRITTEN APPROVAL of
  an officer not below Deputy/Assistant Commissioner (recorded reasons);
  oral approval permissible only in urgency, reduced to writing promptly.
- SENIOR MANAGEMENT (CMD/MD/CEO/CFO) of companies should NOT be summoned in
  the first instance unless their involvement in the decision leading to
  revenue loss is indicated.
- Summons must DISCLOSE the name of the offence/matter under investigation
  (the relevant column is not to be left vague) unless investigation would
  be prejudiced.
- Repeated summonses without appearance: maximum three opportunities; then
  the matter proceeds ex parte / prosecution for non-attendance considered.
- Related CBIC material on investigation discipline: Instruction No.
  01/2023-24-GST (Inv.) dated 30-03-2024 (Commissioner-approval gates for
  investigating big industrial houses/MNCs, listed entities; convey
  investigation conclusion promptly; avoid piecemeal document calls; prefer
  official records already available digitally).

SUMMONS RESPONSE PROTOCOL (platform playbook):
1. Authenticate the summons: verify DIN (Document Identification Number) on
   https://esanchar.cbic.gov.in/DIN/DINSearch — a CBIC communication WITHOUT
   a DIN is treated as INVALID per Circular No. 122/41/2019-GST (05-11-2019)
   and 128/47/2019-GST (23-12-2019).
2. Seek adjournment in writing if dates clash (medical/travel proof) —
   never simply skip a date.
3. Document production: deliver with a covering letter + itemised annexure
   and acknowledgement; keep copies/hashes of everything supplied.
4. Statement stage: answer truthfully, from records; "I will verify from
   books and revert" is a legitimate answer; the deponent may read the
   statement before signing and note corrections; advocates are generally
   permitted at visible distance (not within hearing) per judicial practice
   on Section 70 — request in advance.
5. Track INVESTIGATING FORMATION: DGGI (Directorate General of GST
   Intelligence) operates nationally with intelligence-based jurisdiction;
   parallel investigations by DGGI and state/centre jurisdictional officers
   on the SAME subject should be consolidated — represent for transfer to
   one formation citing CBIC's own circulars on avoiding parallel
   proceedings.
6. Map the endgame: summons inquiry typically matures into (a) closure, (b)
   DRC-01A/SCN under 73/74, or (c) arrest/prosecution where Section 132
   thresholds (Rs. 5 crore evasion for cognisable offences) are in play —
   monitor exposure and consider voluntary DRC-03 only as an informed,
   counselled decision (it can mitigate Section 74 penalty to 15% before
   SCN).

PART 57: APPEALS DEEP PROCESS, RECTIFICATION, REVISION, ADVANCE RULING
================================================================================

---
[CHUNK_133]
[TOPIC: APL-03 and APL-04 — Departmental Appeals/Review and the Demand-Crystallising Order Summary]
[GST_FORM: APL-03 | APL-04]
[SECTION: Section 107(2), Section 107(11), Section 112(3) CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 109, Rule 113 CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Appeal]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-rules.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

APL-03 — DEPARTMENT'S application to the First Appellate Authority:
- Section 107(2): the Commissioner may, on his own motion or on request,
  EXAMINE any adjudication order and direct a subordinate officer to apply
  to the Appellate Authority — filed in FORM GST APL-03 within 6 MONTHS of
  the order (taxpayer's window is 3 months; the department gets double).
- The APL-03 is treated AS IF it were an appeal; the taxpayer becomes
  RESPONDENT and gets full hearing rights.
- Platform alert: a favourable adjudication order is not final until the
  6-month departmental review window lapses — diarise it and preserve the
  evidence file.
- No pre-deposit applies to departmental appeals.

APL-04 — SUMMARY OF THE APPELLATE ORDER (Rule 113):
- Issued by the Appellate Authority (and by the Tribunal Registrar for
  GSTAT orders) stating the FINAL confirmed amounts head-wise.
- APL-04 is what re-states the demand in the Electronic Liability Register
  — recovery proceeds on APL-04 figures, not the original DRC-07. If the
  appeal succeeded, chase APL-04 + DRC-08 alignment; if amounts in APL-04
  exceed the appellate order's operative text, seek rectification
  (Section 161) immediately.
- Section 107(11) limits the FAA: it may confirm/modify/annul but cannot
  REMAND; it can ENHANCE only after a show-cause to the appellant
  (enhancement without SCN is void).
- FAA must decide, where possible, within 1 YEAR of filing (Section 107(13));
  the order must be a speaking order communicated to appellant, adjudicator,
  and jurisdictional Commissioners.

---
[CHUNK_134]
[TOPIC: APL-05 — GSTAT Appeal Process in Depth (Tribunal Stage)]
[GST_FORM: APL-05 | APL-06 | APL-07]
[SECTION: Sections 109-113 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 110, Rule 111 CGST Rules; GSTAT (Procedure) Rules 2025]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Appeal]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | CBIC_Notification]
[SOURCE_URL: https://www.gstat.gov.in/]
[VALID_FROM: 2025-04-24]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Due_date | Document_checklist]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

GSTAT appeal mechanics (operational from 2025; e-filing on the GSTAT portal
www.gstat.gov.in under the GSTAT (Procedure) Rules 2025, G.S.R. 256(E)
dated 24-04-2025):

WHO/WHAT: appeal against FAA (Section 107) or Revisional Authority
(Section 108) orders — Section 112(1). The Tribunal may REFUSE appeals
where the disputed amount is ≤ Rs. 50,000 (Section 112(2) discretion).
Anti-profiteering and other notified matters lie before the Principal Bench.

TIME LIMIT: 3 months from communication of the order (department: 6 months
via APL-07 review route under Section 112(3)); condonable by 3 further
months on sufficient cause (Section 112(6)). For the operationalisation
backlog, the notified universal deadline for legacy appeals is 30-06-2026
— file all pending FAA-order appeals before that date.

PRE-DEPOSIT (Section 112(8), as amended by Finance (No.2) Act 2024):
10% of the disputed TAX (reduced from 20%), capped at Rs. 20 crore each
under CGST and SGST — IN ADDITION to the 10% already deposited at FAA
stage. On deposit, recovery of the balance is STAYED (Section 112(9)).
Penalty-only orders: pre-deposit of 10% of the penalty where the dispute
involves no tax (per the 2024 amendments for e-way bill/detention cases).

FILING BUNDLE (APL-05 + GSTAT portal annexes):
certified copy of the FAA order (upload within 7 days of e-filing where
self-certified initially); grounds of appeal; statement of facts; FAA-stage
APL-01/APL-04; original DRC-01/SCN and DRC-07; pre-deposit challans (both
stages); authorisation (board resolution/letter) and vakalatnama where
represented; fee per Rule 110 (Rs. 1,000 per lakh of disputed amount,
minimum Rs. 5,000, maximum Rs. 25,000; no fee for rectification
applications).
CROSS-OBJECTIONS: respondent may file memorandum of cross-objections in
FORM GST APL-06 within 45 days of receiving notice of appeal.

HEARING/ORDER: Tribunal benches (Judicial Member + Technical Members
Centre/State); endeavour to decide within 1 year (Section 113(4)); may
amend its own order for apparent errors within 3 months (six months under
Section 113(3) for rectification on application). Further appeal: High
Court on substantial question of law within 180 days (Section 117) — note
GSTAT is the LAST fact-finding forum, so the evidentiary record must be
complete at this stage; the platform should freeze and index the full
documentary record at APL-05 filing.

---
[CHUNK_135]
[TOPIC: Rectification of Errors Apparent on Record — Section 161]
[GST_FORM: DRC-08 | APL-04]
[SECTION: Section 161 CGST Act]
[RULE: NA]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Appeal | Assessment]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 161 permits the AUTHORITY THAT PASSED any decision/order/notice/
certificate to rectify an ERROR APPARENT ON THE FACE OF THE RECORD —
suo motu, or when brought to notice by a GST officer, or BY THE AFFECTED
PERSON.

Time limits (strict, jurisdictional):
- Taxpayer must bring the error to notice WITHIN 3 MONTHS of issuance.
- Rectification must be COMPLETED within 6 MONTHS of issuance.
- EXCEPTION: the 6-month cap does NOT apply to purely CLERICAL or
  ARITHMETICAL errors arising from accidental slip/omission — those are
  rectifiable any time.
- Natural justice proviso: if rectification ADVERSELY affects any person,
  hearing is mandatory.

What qualifies as "error apparent": computation mistakes, demand in DRC-07/
APL-04 exceeding the order's operative text, ignoring a payment already
made via DRC-03, wrong tax-period mapping, non-consideration of a reply
THAT IS ON RECORD (supported by departmental practice; note also the
special Section 148-based rectification window N/N 22/2024-Central Tax,
08-10-2024, for orders confirming Section 16(4) ITC demands now covered by
Sections 16(5)/16(6) — a dedicated rectification application route).
What does NOT qualify: anything needing fresh investigation, re-appreciation
of evidence, or a debatable legal point — those need appeal (Section 107)
or revision, not rectification.

Strategic use by the engine: rectification is FREE (no pre-deposit), fast,
and does not extend appeal limitation — so where both a clear apparent
error AND debatable issues exist, file rectification AND protective APL-01
in parallel within their respective clocks; never let the 3-month appeal
window lapse waiting for a rectification outcome.

---
[CHUNK_136]
[TOPIC: Revision by Revisional Authority — Section 108]
[GST_FORM: RVN-01]
[SECTION: Section 108 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rule 109B CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Appeal]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: High]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules]
[SOURCE_URL: https://cbic-gst.gov.in/cgst-act.html]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: Reply_drafting | Due_date]
[JURISDICTION: India_All]

Section 108 is the REVENUE-PROTECTIVE counterpart to appeal: the REVISIONAL
AUTHORITY (Principal Commissioner/Commissioner-level, as designated) may —
on its own motion, on information, or on the Commissioner's request — call
for and examine any order of a SUBORDINATE officer, and revise it if it is
(i) ERRONEOUS AND (ii) PREJUDICIAL TO THE INTEREST OF REVENUE (both limbs
must coexist), including where the order is illegal, improper, or passed
without material facts (whether or not available at the time), or in
consequence of a CAG observation.

Procedural safeguards:
- Notice to the taxpayer in FORM GST RVN-01 (Rule 109B) + opportunity of
  hearing before any adverse revision.
- BARS on revision (Section 108(2)): cannot revise an order that (a) is
  under appeal at FAA/GSTAT/HC/SC, (b) before expiry of the taxpayer's
  appeal period (the appeal route gets first right of way for 6 months),
  (c) more than 3 YEARS after the original order, (d) has already been
  revised, or (e) is a revisional order itself.
- POINT-SEVERABILITY: points not raised/decided in an appeal CAN be
  revised — within 1 year from the appellate order or the 3-year outer
  limit, whichever is later.
- Stay power: the Revisional Authority may stay the operation of the
  subordinate order pending revision.

Taxpayer-side relevance for the platform: (1) RVN-01 is a distinct notice
class — classify it separately from SCNs; the defence is to attack either
limb (no error / no prejudice to revenue — e.g., revenue-neutral
classification differences); (2) a revision order is itself appealable to
GSTAT (Section 112); (3) the 3-year revision shadow means even fully
favourable adjudications should have their defence files preserved for at
least that period.

---
[CHUNK_137]
[TOPIC: Advance Ruling — ARA-01 Application, AAR/AAAR Process, Binding Effect]
[GST_FORM: ARA-01 | ARA-02 | ARA-03]
[SECTION: Sections 95-106 CGST Act]
[RULE: Rules 103-107A CGST Rules]
[TAXPAYER_TYPE: All]
[COMPLIANCE_AREA: Appeal | Rates]
[FREQUENCY: Event_Based]
[RISK_LEVEL: Medium]
[SOURCE_TYPE: CGST_Act | CGST_Rules | GST_Portal]
[SOURCE_URL: https://tutorial.gst.gov.in/userguide/advanceruling/index.htm]
[VALID_FROM: 2017-07-01]
[VALID_TO: Current]
[USER_INTENT: How_to_file | Eligibility | Rate_lookup]
[JURISDICTION: State_Specific]

Advance Ruling secures binding certainty BEFORE or DURING a supply
arrangement. The platform should propose it whenever classification/rate/
ITC-eligibility ambiguity is recurring and material.

ELIGIBLE QUESTIONS (Section 97(2) — exhaustive list):
(a) classification of goods/services; (b) applicability of a notification;
(c) determination of time and VALUE of supply; (d) admissibility of ITC;
(e) determination of LIABILITY to pay tax; (f) whether registration is
required; (g) whether a particular activity amounts to a SUPPLY.
NOT eligible: place-of-supply questions are not in the list (rulings differ;
treat as high-risk to admissibility), and questions ALREADY PENDING OR
DECIDED in the applicant's own proceedings are barred (Section 98(2)
proviso).

PROCESS:
1. FORM GST ARA-01 on the portal (Services → User Services → My
   Applications → Advance Ruling), fee Rs. 5,000 EACH under CGST and SGST
   (Rs. 10,000 total). Unregistered persons may also apply (temporary ID).
2. Authority for Advance Ruling (AAR) of the STATE: two members (Centre +
   State). Admission hearing → ruling within 90 DAYS of receipt
   (Section 98(6)).
3. Members differing → reference to the APPELLATE Authority (AAAR).
4. APPEAL to AAAR: FORM GST ARA-02 (applicant) / ARA-03 (jurisdictional
   officer) within 30 DAYS (+30 condonable), fee Rs. 10,000 each Act for
   the applicant; AAAR decides within 90 days (Section 101).

BINDING EFFECT (Section 103): binds ONLY (a) the APPLICANT and (b) the
jurisdictional officer in respect of the applicant — it is NOT a
precedent for other taxpayers (persuasive only) and is STATE-SPECIFIC
(another state's AAR ruling does not bind). It remains in force until the
LAW, FACTS or CIRCUMSTANCES change (Section 103(2)).
VOID AB INITIO (Section 104): a ruling obtained by FRAUD, suppression, or
misrepresentation is void, and the normal demand provisions revive (the
period from ruling to voiding is excluded from limitation).

Use-cases the engine should auto-suggest: new product launch with HSN
ambiguity; exemption-entry condition interpretation; composite vs mixed
supply structuring; ITC admissibility on large capex; whether an activity
(e.g., inter-branch service) is a "supply". Caution note: an adverse ruling
binds the applicant — pre-assess downside with the CA before filing.
